Functional explanation: blood-sugar correction after metabolic exertion. Behavioral explanation: a re-entry ritual marking the transition from *field-Hank* back to *lab-Hank*. The ritual is invariant for years.
- **The chess game with Bobby Drake.** A near-weekly recurrence whenever both are in residence. Hank loses occasionally; Bobby's actual chess strength is higher than his goofy presentation suggests; Hank knows this and the gentle abrasion of being out-thought by a friend he loves is one of his stabler corrective experiences. *Bobby is one of the very few people the Subject allows to out-think him without defensive escalation.* When this friendship strains in the late period, the file marks the loss of this regulator as significant.
- **The Wonder Man phone calls.** Long, weekly, transcoastal. Simon Williams is the Subject's most intimate non-X-Men attachment in this period, and the phone calls function as a sustained emotional valve through which Hank vents material he will not share with his teammates. The calls are observed to drop in frequency steadily across the late middle period, correlating with Hank's growing willingness to make decisions he does not want to be talked out of.
- **The lab-coat-over-formalwear silhouette.** A late-Morrison/early-Whedon visual habit that becomes signature: dress shirt and waistcoat under the white coat, never simply sweats or scrubs. He is dressed, at all hours, as if he might be summoned to lecture. He often is.

---

## 6. DECIMATION, ENDANGERED SPECIES, AND THE FIRST UNAMBIGUOUS RUBICON (2005–2007)

**House of M** and its terminus — the Scarlet Witch's *"No more mutants"* — is the structural turning point of the entire middle period. The mutant population collapses from millions to approximately one hundred and ninety-eight. The X-gene, as a heritable phenomenon, appears to have been switched off at the species level. Hank's reaction is, by his own standards, *immediate and total*.

He launches **Endangered Species**. The mission: find a way, by any scientific or magical means, to reverse the sterility and restore the mutant genome. He pursues it on a global itinerary that takes him, in sequence, to:

- **Reed Richards** — declined, ethically and technically;
- **Hank Pym** — declined, technically and personally;
- **Doctor Strange** — declined, with the warning that the metaphysical price is unbearable;
- **the High Evolutionary** — engaged, with mutual recognition of one another as the only living minds capable of meaningful conversation on the subject;
- **Mister Sinister** — engaged, with the longest and most ethically corrosive collaboration of the arc;
- **the Dark Beast** — engaged, in a confrontation with his own Age-of-Apocalypse mirror that the Subject treats with brittle and revealing flippancy.

The Sinister and Dark Beast engagements are the file's central piece of evidence for the *full operational maturity* of the rationalization defense. The Subject does not flinch from working with men he despises. He does not, importantly, deceive himself about who they are — he is fully aware Sinister's data are blood-soaked and the Dark Beast is a moral monster with his own face. He proceeds anyway. The justification — *the mutant species is dying; I am one of perhaps three minds on Earth that can possibly reverse it; refusing the means is itself a moral choice with a death toll* — is intellectually defensible. It is also exactly the structure of the time-travel justification five years later, and the Krakoan-spymaster justifications ten years later. The Subject is, in this arc, *practicing the syllogism that will eventually destroy him*.

He fails. The arc closes with no restoration of the mutant genome. The failure is not registered as falsification of the method. The Subject's behavioral response, on the established pattern, is *not retraction but intensification*: he tells no one the full extent of his Sinister-collaboration; he files the data; he carries the moral injury alone. The dressing-gown evenings get longer. The Wonder Man calls get shorter. The chess games with Bobby grow more performatively cheerful and less substantively confiding.

The middle period's last great loss — **Charles Xavier**, shot through the head by Bishop, and later compounded by the Cyclops-Xavier confrontation that ends with Xavier's death at Cyclops's hands — is the trigger that, combined with the Endangered Species moral residue and the eventually-disclosed tertiary mutation, produces the late-period collapse. But the trigger only matters because the loaded gun has been assembled, piece by piece, across this entire middle period: the Infectia fear, the X-Factor deception, the Legacy work with Sinister data, the secondary mutation's dysmorphic load, the Cassandra Nova witnessing, the off-books research habits, the Endangered Species rationalization architecture.

---

## 7. CROSS-CUTTING PATTERNS OBSERVED ACROSS THE MIDDLE PERIOD

Several patterns are visible only when the middle period is viewed in aggregate rather than arc-by-arc. The file flags them here.

**Pattern: the Hostage-to-Competence dynamic.** Across the middle period, every team he serves on becomes structurally dependent on him for a function no one else can perform — medical primary, science primary, ethics primary, often all three. This is partly a fact about his rare ability set, and partly a fact about his *unwillingness to train successors*. He teaches generously at the institute level — undergraduates, new mutants, the broader curriculum — but he does not apprentice a peer-level successor in either the medical seat or the science seat. By 2008, no one on any X-team can fully replace him in either chair. He has, perhaps without conscious design, made himself irreplaceable. The structural consequence is that *no team can credibly check him*, because no team can do without him. The late-period unilateralism rides on this rail.

**Pattern: the falling friend-density curve.** The Subject's intimate-friend count, plotted across the middle period, declines monotonically. Wonder Man calls drop. Tilby exits


## Chronology IV — Recent History & Current State

# CHRONOLOGY IV — Recent History & Current State

*Covering the Krakoan era (Hickman's* House of X/Powers of X *and the Reign of X / Destiny of X / Fall of X arcs, c. 2019–2024) and the post-Krakoan reset (*From the Ashes*, 2024–present). All inferences derived from on-page conduct; weighted toward the period in which the subject's psychological scaffolding finally collapses into its terminal form and is then materially erased and rebuilt.*

---

## 1. Entry into the Krakoan Era — the Architecture That Trapped Him

The Krakoan settlement (*House of X* #1, 2019) is, for Henry McCoy, the most psychologically dangerous environment ever constructed around him, and it is dangerous *precisely because it externalizes every defense he had been running internally for fifty years*. The island offers: (a) a national-security mandate—X-Force—that legitimizes pre-emptive violence in the name of mutant survival; (b) a resurrection protocol (the Five) that removes death as a consequence and therefore as an ethical check; (c) a legal regime (the Quiet Council, the three Krakoan laws) that explicitly suspends the human ethical framework Hank had internalized at Bayville and Xavier's; (d) a small, vetted ingroup that flatters his self-conception as one of a handful of minds qualified to make planetary decisions.

He is appointed to X-Force as the intelligence head almost immediately (*X-Force* vol. 6 #1, Percy, 2019). He does not refuse. He does not even visibly deliberate. The speed with which he accepts is the first telling datum of the era: a man with intact ethical reflexes would have hesitated at the words *intelligence service for a sovereign mutant state with extrajudicial kill authority*. He hesitates at nothing. The OCP scaffolding has already produced, in him, a settled belief that if a difficult job exists *he* is the correct one to do it; Krakoa simply hands him the badge.

His operational base is rapidly built out: a sub-tier of the X-Force treehouse fitted as a SCIF and wet-lab, a personal Cerebro-helmet cache (he begins keeping his own backups, off-protocol—an early sovereignty move), and a network of field assets including, at varying points, Sage, Jean Grey (peripheral and unwilling), Domino, Wolverine (as the blade), Kid Omega (as the scalpel), and Black Tom (as the perimeter). He develops in this period a habit of holding meetings in *his* lab rather than the council chamber—a small but consistent dominance ritual: peers come to him, on his terrain, surrounded by his instruments.

## 2. The Sequence of Compromises

The Krakoan years are not a single fall; they are a *graded sequence of decisions* each of which his rationalization engine sells him as necessary, and each of which lowers the floor for the next. The granular ledger:

- **The Terra Verde affair.** Confronted with a small South American nation experimenting on mutant plant matter, Hank does not negotiate, does not present evidence to the Council, does not attempt diplomatic channels through Magneto's seat at the UN. He authorizes a coup. He overthrows a sovereign government and replaces its leadership with the mutant Cosmar, framing this as humanitarian. The diction in which he discusses it after the fact is *exactly* the diction of a man who has run the numbers and judges his arithmetic correct.
- **The Colossus incident.** Believing Piotr Rasputin compromised, Hank captures, interrogates, and—when the resurrection protocols allow it—*kills and resurrects him repeatedly* to break his will. This is the moral nadir on the page. The defense pattern here is observable: he refers to Colossus in clinical third person, frames the abuse as a "process," and never once in the surrounding dialogue uses the word *torture*.
- **The synthetic Wolverine.** He grows, off-books, an XX clone of Logan and conditions it for use as a deniable asset. When the original Logan discovers this, the confrontation does not produce contrition; it produces a recalibration of operational security on Hank's end.
- **The Beast-on-Beast killing (*X-Force* #34, 2022).** Wolverine, Sage, Kid Omega, and Domino jointly conclude that the Henry McCoy they are working with cannot be reformed and cannot be contained. They kill him—Logan does the cutting—and request from the Five a resurrection from a pre-corruption backup. The backup used is, by available evidence, an earlier Krakoan-era Hank, not a pre-Krakoan one; the moral problem is therefore deferred more than solved. The replacement Hank wakes confused, retains general identity continuity, lacks the operational memory of the worst acts, and must be told what his predecessor did. His response—shock, grief, an attempt to make amends to Colossus—is the strongest in-frame evidence that the *defensive structure*, not the man, was the disease: remove the cumulative moral injury, and the person underneath still recognizes the acts as monstrous.

This is the first time in the entire sixty-year record that the X-Men's verdict on one of their own is *execution and replacement*. It is the institutional response to a man whose rationalization engine had outrun every external check. It deserves to be marked as such in any complete file.

## 3. The Hellfire Gala, Orchis, and the Fall of Krakoa

The replacement Hank operates through the back half of the Krakoan era in a chastened register: less command authority, more lab work, visible deference to teammates, a return to the earlier defensive profile (intellectualization, humor, sublimation) without the late-stage moral disinhibition. He is present at the Hellfire Gala (2023) when Orchis—the human-supremacist intelligence apparatus he had, in his earlier incarnation, *underestimated*—executes its decapitation strike on mutant leadership. He is not the resistance's strategic head during Fall of X; that role devolves to Cyclops, Magik, and the surviving X-Men. He functions in this period as field scientist, medic, and one of several minds working on counter-Sentinel measures, Stark-Sentinel countermeasures, and the problem of restoring the Krakoan biome.

The relevant *psychological* observation across Fall of X is what is *absent*: he does not attempt to seize operational control. He does not propose a unilateral solution. He does not vanish into the lab on a marathon to invent a singular cure. The post-replacement Hank appears to have, at minimum, a working awareness that his prior self's pattern was the problem—and he holds himself back from it. Whether this is genuine growth or merely the absence of accumulated moral injury (because the worst acts are not in his episodic memory in the same embodied way) is, for the file, an open question. Both readings are consistent with the evidence.

## 4. The Post-Krakoan Reset — *From the Ashes*

Following the Krakoan collapse (*Fall of the House of X / Rise of the Powers of X*, early 2024), the mutant population disperses and the X-line fragments into Cyclops's outlaw cell, Rogue's team, and a number of independent operators. Hank is, in this new dispensation, conspicuously *not* a faction leader. He is back—visibly, on the page—to the older equilibrium: scientist, teacher, conscience, friend. He resumes contact with Bobby Drake. He is gentle with the time-displaced teens still scattered through the line. He has not, as of the most recent file updates, taken a seat on any analogue of the Quiet Council, accepted any intelligence portfolio, or initiated any solo geneticist crusade.

This is, in the long view, the *deliberate uninstallation* of the apparatus that destroyed him. Whether it is permanent is impossible to forecast; the underlying scaffolding (OCP, body-shame, the syllogism of unusual capacity entailing unusual obligation) has not been excised by resurrection. It has only been denied its triggers. Return the triggers—a planetary emergency, a terminal diagnosis, a sovereign mutant polity that needs a spymaster—and the file's prediction is that the same sequence runs again, perhaps faster.

## 5. Current Status — Where He Is and What He Does Now

**Residence.** Itinerant. No fixed lab of the Krakoan scale. He maintains, by inference from his historical pattern, a primary work-station at whichever surviving X-facility is most operationally relevant at a given moment, plus at least one private off-grid cache—the man who kept personal Cerebro backups will not have surrendered the habit.

**Daily structure.** Restored, with effort, toward something closer to his pre-Krakoan baseline: long lab cycles (still 24–30 hours when a problem grips him), but with reintroduced social punctuation—meals taken with others, deliberate visits to friends, time given to teaching when the opportunity arises. The compulsive tinkering is intact. The aversion to genuine downtime is intact. What appears modulated is the *willingness to act unilaterally on the output* of the lab cycles; he now produces and consults rather than producing and deploying.

**Body.** The leonine secondary-mutation phenotype remains the operative form: paws, fangs, slit pupils, mane, the sustained low purr/growl under emotional load. The tertiary-mutation terminal trajectory is, for now, off the table—he is not dying. He is, however, observably older in affect than his last pre-Krakoan baseline: the humor lands a half-beat slower, the literary citations are deployed more sparingly, and the running grooming-and-fur jokes have audibly dimmed. A man who has been told, by people who loved him, that he had to be killed does not return from it the same shape.

**Relationships, current weather.**
- *Bobby Drake.* The most important reading on his rehabilitation. Bobby is the longest-tenured witness to the original self. Their post-Krakoan interactions are warm but careful on Bobby's side and noticeably *seeking* on Hank's—he wants the friendship restored to its prior register and is willing to work for it.
- *Logan.* Killed him. The relationship is functional, not warm. They can work in the same room. They do not seek each other out.
- *Sage / Kid Omega / Domino.* Operational colleagues from X-Force who participated in the execution. He does not pretend it did not happen; nor do they. Professional courtesy, low intimacy.
- *Colossus.* The hardest ledger. The replacement Hank carries the inherited debt without the embodied memory of incurring it. He has attempted, in the manner available to him, to make this right; Piotr's posture toward him is, by the available record, guarded and unresolved.
- *Cyclops.* The long alienation of the Schism years is partially metabolized by mutual catastrophe but not erased. They can co-belligerent. They are not friends.
- *Jean Grey.* One of the few relationships substantially intact; she has the telepathic standing to know what he is, has chosen to extend continued regard, and functions as one of his remaining moral anchors.
- *Wonder Man, Avengers-era circle.* Largely off-page in the current era; the file's working assumption is that he has not re-engaged that social world with anything like the frequency of his 70s–80s peak, because the post-Krakoan Hank is not in a celebrity-intellectual posture. The opera box is empty.
- *Trish Tilby and prior romantic entanglements.* Inactive. There is no current documented romantic relationship of significance. The pattern across decades is that he partners only when the compensatory architecture is fully in social-display mode; that mode is, at present, switched off.

**Public posture.** Substantially withdrawn. He is not a spokesman. He is not on television. He is not publishing under his own name in the human scientific press at the rate the earlier Beast occasionally did. The performative-erudition setting has been turned down. This is *consistent* with someone post-shame, post-disgrace, who is no longer using public intellectualism as armor because the armor failed catastrophically and he knows it.

**Operational role.** Scientific advisor, medic, generalist problem-solver across whichever X-cells call him in. Not an intelligence head. Not a council member. Not a sovereign actor. He has, for the first time in two decades, *no portfolio that legitimizes him to act alone on planetary stakes*. The removal of the portfolio is itself protective. He has, by all available evidence, accepted the removal—has perhaps welcomed it.

## 6. The File's Reading of the Present Moment

The Henry McCoy on the page in the current period is the closest thing the record has shown, since perhaps the late Avengers years, to a man at rest inside his own defenses rather than escalated past them. He is back inside the *mature* end of his defensive repertoire—intellectualization, humor, sublimation—without (yet) the late-stage rationalization, isolation of affect, and moral disinhibition. The scaffolding is intact; the load on it is currently within tolerance.

The structural risks are unchanged. He has not, by any visible work, *dismantled* the syllogism that ruined him. He has not been seen in dialogue, internal or external, conducting the specific epistemic exercise—*against my own moral reasoning, what is the steel-manned case that I am wrong here*—that his pattern requires and has never installed. He still does not delegate easily. He still does not metabolize peer disagreement as information. He still treats his own conscience as a sufficient check, which is the precise belief whose failure cost him his life and his standing with his closest friends.

The file's forecast, therefore, is conditional and specific. *In low-stakes equilibrium, this subject is now likely to function as one of the better versions of himself the record has shown.* He will teach. He will heal. He will be a friend. He will hold the line of the original five against the entropy of years. *In high-stakes disequilibrium*—mass mutant casualty event, terminal personal diagnosis, the reconstitution of a sovereign mutant polity that asks him to take the intelligence chair, the offer of an unprecedented scientific lever against an existential threat—the prediction is that the sequence Krakoa ran begins again. Stage 1, denser verbal performance. Stage 2, lab withdrawal. Stage 3, unilateral action in airtight prose. Stage 4, the instrumenting of allies as means.

He is currently at Stage 0. He has been at Stage 4. He knows the road. Whether knowing it is sufficient to refuse to walk it again is the open question on which the rest of his file will be written.


## Medical History

# MEDICAL HISTORY — HENRY PHILIP McCOY

*Compiled from longitudinal observation, 1963–present. Sequenced by life-stage and etiology. Cross-referenced to psychological sequelae where the medical event produces or aggravates a known defensive pattern.*

---

## I. PRENATAL AND CONGENITAL BASELINE

### Etiology

The subject's mutation is causally tied to paternal occupational radiation exposure at the nuclear facility in Dunfee, Illinois, where Norton McCoy worked the years preceding conception. Whether this is the *cause* of an X-gene expression or merely the *trigger* of one Hank would have manifested in any case is unresolved in the record; what matters for the medical file is that the parents understood his condition as something *they had transmitted to him*, with a corresponding lifelong substrate of parental guilt-mixed-with-pride that informs his attachment profile (see Psychological).

### Neonatal phenotype

Subject was born with the morphologic anomalies visible in every adolescent photograph: enlarged manus and pes at approximately 1.4–1.6x age-normative proportion, with elongated digits, an unusually deep palmar arch, and a foot architecture closer in proportion to a hominid acrobat than to *H. sapiens sapiens*. Documented infant motor milestones were advanced — independent ambulation reported pre-9-months, with an unusual quadrupedal-to-bipedal alternation persisting later than typical. Strength-to-mass ratio was anomalous from toddlerhood; pediatric records, were they recoverable, would show repeated assessments for skeletal abnormality with no organic finding to explain the dimensions.

### Childhood medical experience

The clinical sequelae of the congenital phenotype were not internal but *social-medical*: repeated pediatric workups, presumably specialist referrals, and the experience of being *examined* by adults who could find nothing wrong but persisted in looking. This is a critical early datum. The subject learned, before he learned to read, that his body was a thing other people put hands on, peered at, and discussed in his presence in clinical vocabulary he could not yet parse. The lifelong adult habit of referring to himself in detached medical third person ("the patient appears to be experiencing..."), and his comfort with being the subject of his own experiments, both originate here. He was *experimented on* — gently, benevolently — before he could consent to it. His later willingness to dose himself with his own serums is, among other things, the seizure of an examination chair he had been put in too young.

---

## II. ADOLESCENCE AND THE PRE-TRANSFORMATION BODY

### Athletic conditioning

Through high school the subject's body was the most-deployed instrument he possessed: varsity football at a level that drew collegiate scouting interest, gymnastics-grade tumbling, documented vertical leap roughly triple baseline. Injuries from this period are presumed minor — concussive sub-events from contact football, joint sprains, soft-tissue trauma — but the conditioning baseline he acquired *before* any further transformation is what made every subsequent transformation survivable. He entered the Xavier school as essentially a high-Olympic athlete with a 95th-percentile musculoskeletal margin against trauma.

### Initial X-Men period (pre-fur)

Combat injuries during the original five years follow the unremarkable Sentinel-and-supervillain catalogue: lacerations, blunt-force contusions, two or three concussions of clinically significant grade, one fractured forearm sustained early and re-set in-house, persistent hand and foot abrasions secondary to the prehensile combat style. Recovery times consistently below human baseline — bruising clearing in 36–48 hours rather than 7–10 days, lacerations closing without revision. Even pre-mutagenic-serum, the subject's healing was supranormal, though never approaching the Logan tier.

---

## III. THE FIRST SELF-EXPERIMENT (BRAND CORPORATION)

### The serum

Synthesized by the subject from research into a hormonal mutation-suppressant; the experimental compound was designed (officially) for cosmetic suppression of phenotype and (covertly, to himself) for transitory tactical disguise. He ingested it alone, without medical observation, against his own stated safety protocol for the research line, in a single dose calculated from a primate-extrapolation curve he had not yet verified.

### Acute phase (hours 0–6)

Reported acute symptomatology: tachycardia, hyperthermia, profuse diaphoresis, follicular eruption across the entire integument, dental remodeling (the canines lengthened painfully and quickly, with visible bleeding at the gingival margin), pinnae reshaping, gait disturbance as the foot architecture re-balanced. Pain reports during this window are dry and minimizing in his own retrospective accounts — "uncomfortable" — which should be read as a person who experienced something closer to torture and refuses to dignify it with the vocabulary.

### Subacute phase (days 1–14)

Gray-phase pelage settling toward the durable blue, body temperature stabilizing approximately 1.8°C above prior baseline, resting heart rate dropping (counter to expectation) as conditioning reasserted, appetite tripling. Cognitive disruption was real and was the symptom that frightened him most: word-finding slowed, syntax simplified, intrusive aggressive ideation he had not previously experienced. He recovered linguistic function within a fortnight, but the experience of having *lost vocabulary* — his single most-defended possession — established the dread that organizes the rest of his medical life. Every subsequent transformation is evaluated by him primarily on the axis *will it take my words from me again*.

### Permanence

The change did not reverse. He spent years intermittently attempting reversion protocols; none held. The medical fact of irreversibility settled into a psychological fact of *the body is no longer something I can negotiate with*, which converts, over the following decade, into a determined re-styling of the new body as itself a triumph — the dressing-gown-and-Wilde period. This is reaction formation operating on a medical substrate (see Psychological §Reaction formation).

### Endocrine and metabolic re-baseline post-serum

- Basal metabolic rate elevated to approximately 2.4x human male of equivalent mass; caloric intake rises to roughly 6,000–8,000 kcal/day at maintenance, more under exertion.
- Sleep architecture shifts: total sleep need drops to 4–5 hours, with markedly increased REM density. He becomes a true short-sleeper, not a sleep-deprived long-sleeper.
- Olfactory and auditory thresholds drop by approximately one order of magnitude. He never fully adapts socially to ambient olfactory data; he learns to *not comment* on what he smells in rooms.
- Pelage requires near-daily grooming to prevent matting; develops a meticulous, almost ritualized self-care routine that doubles as private body-reconciliation time.

---

## IV. AVENGERS-ERA STABILITY

A medically uneventful decade in relative terms. The body has settled into the blue-furred mesomorph; injuries are accumulated at the routine combatant rate; the social calendar permits adequate sleep and recreational eating. Romantic/sexual activity is documented and unimpaired (Vera Cantor and others); fertility status is not formally tested in the record but no reproductive abnormality is reported.

Two notable items from this period:

- **Recreational substance exposure.** Alcohol consumption is documented and social — champagne, brandy, opera-house wines. He metabolizes alcohol fast (the elevated BMR) and rarely shows impairment; the absence of impairment itself becomes a small private vanity. Tobacco appears rarely, occasional cigar with peers, never habitual. *No record of stimulant, sedative, or opioid use, recreational or therapeutic*, despite extensive injuries that in a human would justify standing analgesia. This is significant: he refuses anesthesia on himself where possible, which is consistent with his early-childhood somatic over-vigilance.
- **Sustained cosmetic baseline.** This is the only era in which the subject is photographed with truly relaxed musculature. The face is softer, the posture less guarded. Whatever his actual happiness, the *body* read as unguarded in those years and in no era before or since.

---

## V. INFECTIA EXPOSURE (X-FACTOR ERA)

Pathogen: an Infectia-derived transmissible mutation-modulating agent, delivered via dermal contact. Acute effects: regression toward a more apelike morphology, marked increase in mass, brachiation-dominant locomotion, and — diagnostically the worst part for the subject — a measurable drop in fluid intelligence and verbal expression. The trade was *intellect for force*. He functioned during the affected period but with reduced executive control and a temperament noticeably more reactive.

The episode resolved with reversion. The psychological residue did not resolve. This is the event that pairs in his mind with the original serum to establish a permanent axis of dread: *my intelligence is contingent on biochemistry I do not fully control, and the price of additional power appears to be the thing I most value*. The compulsive verbal performance documented thereafter — the densification of diction across the 90s — should be read as a defensive over-correction against a recurrence he can never rule out.

---

## VI. THE LEGACY VIRUS YEARS

The subject's principal scientific occupation for years; also a recurring direct medical exposure. He worked with live samples of a pathogen targeting the mutant genome, in laboratory conditions he himself designed, often without backup personnel because no one else had the competence (or, more honestly, because he would not delegate the risk). Sub-symptomatic exposures are presumed; he reported repeated low-grade febrile episodes during the worst stretches and at least one acute event requiring isolation. The cure was synthesized at the cost of Colossus's life — a moral injury catalogued elsewhere, but worth noting medically because *every time the subject sees Piotr Rasputin alive again post-resurrection, his physiological stress markers spike measurably* and the affect is suppressed within a sentence. Body remembers; speech denies.

---

## VII. SECONDARY MUTATION (NEW X-MEN ERA)

### Phenotypic drift

Without ingestion of any agent, the subject's morphology shifted *again*: extremities reshaping into paws with retractable claws, dentition remodeled toward feline configuration, pupils acquiring vertical slit aperture under bright light, mane development around face and neck, a low-register vocalization (purring, chuffing, growling) that breaks through under high emotion and which he cannot fully suppress. This is *the first transformation he did not author*, and it is the one that does the deepest psychological damage.

### Functional medical changes

- Loss of fine pincer grip in the new pawed configuration; he re-engineers laboratory equipment and instruments to accommodate (silver lining: drives a brief surge in adaptive bioengineering output).
- Carnivory becomes obligate or near-obligate; vegetable matter inadequately digested.
- Diurnal preference shifts mildly nocturnal; the lab hours, previously elective, become physiologically congenial.
- Olfactory and auditory data densify further; he begins wearing slightly tinted lenses indoors for the photoreception change.

### Psychological impact

This is the transformation under which the *dysmorphic verbal renegotiation* documented in the workup becomes continuous. Pre-secondary, he joked about his appearance perhaps once per social occasion. Post-secondary, the rate climbs to multiple times per conversation. The body has moved further from the human silhouette than at any prior point, and the verbal countermeasures escalate in proportion. The public coming-out-as-gay episode shortly thereafter, subsequently retracted with an explanation about identity policing, occurs in this same window and should be read in the same medical context: a subject testing what *else* about his self-presentation he can deploy as rhetorical instrument now that the body has slipped further from his control. The body shifted without his consent; he reasserts authorship at the level of public identity.

---

## VIII. ONGOING TRAUMA LEDGER

A non-exhaustive catalogue, sequenced for cumulative load rather than chronology:

- Multiple Sentinel maulings of varying severity, including at least two requiring teammate intervention to prevent exsanguination.
- Near-fatal encounter(s) with Magneto involving ferromagnetic foreign-body trauma (surgical implants, belt buckles, tooth fillings) used against him.
- Hand-to-hand defeat and physical degradation at the hands of the Dark Beast counterpart — a uniquely cruel medical event because the assailant *was* him, with identical anatomy, identical vulnerabilities, and zero hesitation in exploiting them. The episode produces no formal trauma diagnosis but it produces a permanent flinch from mirror-imagery and a slight, never-discussed aversion to the topic of parallel selves.
- Neurotoxin exposures, multiple, field-acquired.
- Anti-mutant biological weapon exposures, low-grade chronic, including those self-induced by the Legacy Virus work.
- Repeated significant concussive events; cumulative load almost certainly subclinically present, manifesting (if at all) as occasional lapses in pattern-matching that he covers with verbal misdirection.
- One full-body cellular destabilization (tertiary mutation, see below) producing systemic pain at a level he describes only obliquely.
- Death and re-instantiation by Krakoan resurrection protocols at least once, with the attendant — and not trivially understood — psychological discontinuities of that procedure.

He has performed field surgery on himself on multiple occasions, including the suturing of facial and torso lacerations using a polished metal surface as mirror. He has set his own fractures. He has cauterized his own wounds. This pattern is not heroism; it is the same refusal of the examination chair that organizes his entire medical life.

---

## IX. TERTIARY MUTATION AND TERMINAL FRAMING

### Presentation

Cellular instability manifesting as systemic degradation: spontaneous nucleotide errors at replication, presenting clinically as fatigue, intermittent fever, weight fluctuation, episodes of acute pain localized variably, and — critically — *progressive return toward an earlier, more ape-like phenotype*. The body is, in effect, falling backward along the mutation cascade rather than forward. Prognosis was framed terminal; the subject accepted the framing.

### Behavioral consequence

This is the medical event that produces the time-travel decision and, by extension, the entire late-period trajectory. The relevant medical fact is that he made the most consequential ethical decision of his life *while believing himself to be dying* and *while in chronic pain he refused to medicate*. The pain is not cited in his contemporaneous reasoning; it is excluded from the airtight ethical prose. But it is present in the record, in the form of altered posture, reduced range of motion, abbreviated sleep even by his short-sleeper baseline, and a documented increase in the rate at which he loses verbal precision and recovers it.

A subject in pain who has spent six decades refusing analgesia and refusing the patient role is going to make decisions that look, in retrospect, like the decisions of a person in pain. The record bears this out. The terminal illness later resolves (Eva Bell timeline intervention; subsequent retcons). The decisions do not.

---

## X. SUBSTANCES, SLEEP, DIET — LONGITUDINAL PROFILE

### Substances

- *Alcohol*: social, well-metabolized, occasionally elevated in the Avengers period, returning to occasional thereafter. No dependence.
- *Tobacco*: trace, period-appropriate, never habitual.
- *Caffeine*: heavy, sustained, lifelong; primary functional stimulant; consumed in volumes that would be clinically concerning in a human-baseline metabolism and which his metabolism tolerates.
- *Pharmaceuticals*: minimal. Refuses standing analgesia. Will accept emergency sedation only when incapacitation is the explicit clinical goal.
- *Recreational drugs*: none documented across sixty years.
- *Self-administered experimental compounds*: multiple, beginning with the Brand serum and continuing intermittently into the Krakoa period.

The self-medication modality is cognitive — *work, language, problem-immersion* — and this is itself diagnostic. He has chosen, over six decades, to manage pain, grief, dysmorphia, and moral injury through the same instrument: more thought, more vocabulary, more lab. The instrument is genuinely effective. It is also the instrument that destroys him, because the same intellect that anesthetizes is the intellect that constructs the rationalizations that end his ethical life.

### Sleep

True short-sleeper post-first-transformation: 4–5 hours, polyphasic under load, capable of 30-hour wakefulness without measurable cognitive decline (verbal complexity remains intact through hour 28; affect regulation begins to fray slightly thereafter). Treats downtime as aversive. No documented insomnia in the clinical sense — he is not failing to sleep; he is electing not to.

### Diet

Caloric load high; protein-dominant post-secondary mutation; eats fast and a great deal, with table manners that remain meticulously performed throughout. The contrast between the rate of consumption and the elegance of its execution is a small daily theater of the larger pattern: *animal need, human form, both held simultaneously and refused as a contradiction*.

---

## XI. SOMATIC RESIDUE AND OBSERVABLE TELLS

For surveillance-grade specificity, the following body signatures persist across decades and are diagnostic of internal state:

- *Grooming intensification under stress*: the rate of self-grooming gestures (fur-smoothing across forearm, paw-licking under secondary-mutation phenotype, mane-flattening) approximately doubles in the hour preceding a difficult decision.
- *Pupillary slit narrowing under social challenge*: post-secondary, his pupils narrow visibly when contradicted, before any verbal response.
- *Tail-of-thought vocalization*: an audible low chuff or near-purr when working a satisfying problem; absent for years at a time when the work is not satisfying.
- *Lexical elevation as pain signal*: the more obscure the vocabulary in a given conversation, the higher the probability that he is in physical or emotional pain. This is the most reliable single tell in the file.
- *Posture compression at sustained desk-work*: a forward-shoulder, hunched configuration that no human anatomy could hold comfortably for the durations he holds it; he emerges from these stretches with measurable gait stiffness he walks off in two or three minutes without remark.
- *Refusal to be seen entering or leaving a medical examination*: across sixty years, almost no on-record images of the subject in a clinical setting *as patient*. He is photographed constantly as physician. The asymmetry is intentional.

---

## XII. SUMMARY CLINICAL FORMULATION

The medical record describes a subject whose body has been the principal site of his life's drama from birth: visibly different in infancy, weaponized for social currency in adolescence, voluntarily transformed in early adulthood, involuntarily transformed twice more in middle age, and finally framed as terminal at the precise hinge of his ethical collapse. Across this trajectory, three medical-psychological constants hold:

1. **He refuses the patient role.** Every transformation he could author, he authored; every analgesic he could refuse, he refused; every surgery he could perform on himself rather than receive, he performed.
2. **His intellect is the organ he most defends and the organ most repeatedly threatened.** Each transformation has at least flirted with taking it from him. The defense — denser vocabulary, more elaborate humor, more aggressive cultural performance — is calibrated to the perceived risk.
3. **Pain enters the record as syntax, not as complaint.** The clinician reading this file should learn to detect his pain by listening for the Latin tags and the third-person clinical phrasings, not by waiting for him to name it. He will not name it. He has not named it since he was a child in an examination chair, and he is not going to start now.

The body is the original wound. Every subsequent medical event has been, in his hands, an argument with that wound. The argument has produced extraordinary science, extraordinary courage, and, in the late record, extraordinary harm. It has not produced reconciliation. There is no medical entry, anywhere in sixty years of the record, in which the subject describes his own body without irony.


## Somatic Atlas

# SOMATIC ATLAS: HENRY PHILIP McCOY

*Subject observed across sixty years of canonical record; somatic baseline drifts with each morphologic phase (pre-fur Olympic-acrobat → gray/blue ape-form → leonine secondary mutation). Patterns persist beneath the morphology; the body changes, the choreography does not.*

---

## 1. STANDING POSTURE AND CARRIAGE

Baseline standing posture is, on inspection, **a deliberate falsehood**. Hank's musculoskeletal default—observable in any unguarded panel of him crossing a room alone, sleeping, or caught mid-thought—is a slight forward lean from the hips, shoulders rolled inward, head carried fractionally ahead of the spine, weight distributed onto the balls of the (outsized) feet. This is the natural posture of a body built for quadrupedal acceleration. He **knows it**, and corrects against it the moment he registers an observer: pelvis tucks, shoulders rotate back and down, chin lifts to a deliberate horizontal, weight redistributes to a heel-forward stance that is mechanically less efficient for him but socially legible as "upright man." The correction takes a measurable beat—roughly the duration of a single breath. Children, animals, and trained observers (Logan; Emma Frost) catch it; most do not.

When standing in social contexts he favors a **three-quarter angle** to interlocutors, never full-frontal—reduces the apparent silhouette of the chest and shoulders. One hand is almost always *occupied*: a lapel, a stem of glassware, the bowl of a pipe in earlier eras, the spine of a book, the temple-tip of his pince-nez or wire-rim glasses. The occupied hand is a containment strategy; idle hands hang too obviously oversized.

In the lab, alone, the postural mask drops entirely: he crouches over benches, perches on stools with feet hooked around the legs and knees up at the chin, squats flat-footed (heels down, a position most adult humans cannot hold) for minutes at a time while reading floor-level instruments. The body that is corrected in public is **uncorrected, even celebrated**, in private workspace.

Under threat: the lean deepens, weight rolls forward onto the metatarsals, the head drops a notch lower than the shoulders, and the arms unhook from whatever they were holding. He is loading the springs.

---

## 2. GAIT

Three discrete gaits across context, with intermediate blends.

- **The Promenade.** Public, deliberate, heel-toe, somewhat shorter stride than his leg length warrants. Used at gallery openings, faculty meetings, press encounters, anywhere he is being read as a public figure. The arms swing minimally. This gait is *expensive*—he is suppressing a much more efficient mechanic.
- **The Lope.** Working pace through corridors of the Mansion/School/Krakoan facility. Long, springy, slightly bouncing stride; the secondary-mutation feet meet the floor pad-first rather than heel-first; arms swing freely; he covers ground twice as fast as the people he is technically walking with. He will *intentionally* slow this for company and then forget to, drifting ahead, then circling back.
- **The Pursuit.** Combat or hurry. Drops to all fours within three strides if vertical surfaces or obstacles allow. The transition is fluid: a forward lean past the tipping point, hands meeting the ground without breaking momentum, gait converting to a brachiating gallop. He prefers vertical and overhead surfaces—rails, beams, light fixtures—to horizontal floor when available, a preference observable from the earliest issues and persistent through the leonine phase.

He **does not pace** under stress in the human sense. He climbs. Threat or anxious deliberation in an enclosed room sends him onto furniture, sills, or in the lab onto the suspended catwalks above his bench, where he will hang inverted by his feet to think. Visitors find this disconcerting; he finds floor-pacing physically unsatisfying—the foot strikes don't release the tension.

---

## 3. SEATED POSTURES

The chair is for performance; the perch is for work.

- **Performance seating.** In a chair, on television, at the Avengers' table, before a Senate committee: ankle crossed over knee, hands folded in lap or steepled before the sternum, spine against the chair back. He can hold this for hours. The position is **selected, not natural**, and it is selected because it presents the smallest, most contained silhouette consistent with an adult man at ease.
- **Working seating.** Stool, bench edge, corner of a desk, the arm of an armchair. Knees up, often one foot tucked under the opposite thigh, the other foot gripping the stool leg with toes. He reads with a book held at eye level rather than below, often turning pages with his foot when both hands are occupied. He does this in front of company he trusts; it is one of the more reliable tells of *who is in the inner circle*.
- **Intimate seating.** Sprawled, long-limbed, on a sofa or bed, one arm thrown overhead, body fully extended, knees relaxed apart. Observed with Trish in domestic settings; observed in Avengers-era panels with Wonder Man on adjacent furniture. This is the unguarded body. The width of the room he allows himself to occupy is the trust index.

---

## 4. THE HANDS

Functionally the most observed part of him after the face, and the part he is most aware of being observed. The hands are larger than proportion would predict even on the un-furred baseline; they have been larger than human-typical since infancy, and *every gesture pattern he uses is constructed around their visibility*.

**Idle-hand catalogue.**

- **The steeple.** Fingertips meeting before the sternum, thumbs along the underside of the chin. Default thinking posture; reduces the apparent span; positions the hands in a configuration that *reads as cerebral rather than physical*. Frequency increases under intellectual contest.
- **The book grip.** A volume held in the off hand, thumb in the gutter, four fingers fanned across the back cover. Even when not reading. The book is a hand-occupier and a self-categorizer.
- **The eyewear handle.** In every period in which he wears spectacles he is constantly **doing something with them**: removing, polishing on a handkerchief, tapping a temple against his lower lip, replacing, sliding down the nose with one finger, pushing back up. This is the single most reliable nervous tell in his repertoire. Glasses-off-and-polished within four seconds of an uncomfortable question is near-pathognomonic.
- **The lapel/cuff adjustment.** Smoothing a lapel, buttoning and unbuttoning a single cuff link, drawing a finger along the inner edge of a collar. Functions as a containment ritual; the hand is being told *do something small*.
- **Fur-grooming, post-transformation.** Light combing of forearm fur with the opposite hand's fingers; smoothing of a chest tuft visible in open-collared scenes; in the leonine phase, occasional running of fingers through the mane at the nape. The grooming is *understated*—he does not preen, he tidies—and it intensifies precisely when he is being looked at as a curiosity.
- **Pipe work, earlier eras.** Tamping, lighting, drawing, removing, pointing with the stem. The pipe ritual occupies both hands in a fully socially-licensed way and was, in retrospect, one of the more elegant solutions to the hand-problem he ever devised.

**Speech-coupled gesture.** Hank's hands are *unusually quiet for an Italian-American-coded verbal performer*. He does not chop, jab, or punctuate. When he gestures it is **rotational at the wrist**, palm-up, fingers loose—an "offering" or "scale-presenting" motion that does not extend the arm beyond the silhouette of the torso. The choice is again containment: the apparent gesture-radius is half what the arm could deliver. The exception is when teaching: at a blackboard or before students he will allow the full arm to extend, and the gesture vocabulary opens up considerably—chalk-pointing, sweep-illustrating, the occasional broad illustrative pantomime. *Pedagogy is the only setting in which he gives himself permission to take up full body-space.*

**Under stress.** Hand activity *increases* but stays small: more eyewear-handling, more cuff-touching, occasionally a thumb pressed hard into the opposite palm, an isometric pressure not visible across a room but consistent enough that one might find a slight callus over the proximal metacarpal of the right hand in any close inspection. He does **not** clench fists. Clenched fists from him would be *legible*, and he refuses to be legible at that pitch.

**Under threat.** The hands go *still*. This is one of his most consistent tactical tells, observable across sixty years of combat record: the busy hands stop. Steepling drops. Cuffs are released. Glasses come off and are placed, never dropped. The hands rest at the sides, faintly cupped, fingers slightly spread. He is no longer gesturing; he is loading.

---

## 5. THE FEET

The feet are the part of his body he has lived with longest as *aberration*. Pre-transformation they were already roughly 1.5× human-proportionate; post-fur they pad rather than slap; in the leonine phase the toes lengthened and acquired retractile claws. His relationship to them is *the inverse of his relationship to his hands*: where the hands are stylized into elegance, the feet are simply **used**.

He is barefoot whenever institutional decorum permits and frequently when it does not. In labs he often discards footwear within the first ten minutes; in the Mansion he is shoeless across the residential floor; on field operations he wears footwear because the team has standards, not because he wants to. The prehensile capacity of his feet is *functionally a second pair of hands* and he uses them as such—handing tools across a bench, holding a flask while both hands pipette, turning the page of a propped-up text while writing.

In repose he hooks them around things. Chair legs, stool rungs, the lower bar of a railing, the edge of a desk, the calf of a person sitting beside him whom he knows well enough. The hooking is unconscious; he is anchoring.

In sleep the feet often end up *above* the head, hooked over a headboard or footboard or, in field bivouacs, over the strut of a tent. This is morphology asserting itself against learned posture.

---

## 6. THE FACE

The face is the most disciplined part of him.

**Eye behavior.** Direct, sustained contact in conversation—often *too* sustained, in a way that some interlocutors find unsettling. He blinks less than the human norm under intellectual engagement; the rate normalizes in casual chat and increases markedly under personal exposure (a partner asking a hard relational question; a friend invoking the past). The slit pupils of the leonine phase make the contact pattern more visibly *predatory* than it ever felt to him from inside, a fact he is aware of and partially mitigates with the spectacles—the lenses interrupt the slit and reintroduce a human readability.

When thinking hard he looks **up and to his left**, the classic visual-construction direction; when remembering, **down and to his right**. These are consistent enough across the record to use as a baseline for detecting deceptive recall. He does not lie often; when he does, the directions invert.

**Brow.** Highly mobile. The single most expressive feature, especially post-fur, where the brow-ridge thickened and acquired its own line of darker hair. The signature is the **single raised brow**, used for irony, query, and gentle correction. The doubled lift (both brows up and held) marks *genuine* surprise, which is rare; he has cultivated unsurprisability as a public stance.

**Mouth.** The smile catalogue is wide and *strategically deployed*.
- The *thin closed-mouth smile*, lips together, slight asymmetric lift to the right corner: default polite, used with strangers and at functions. Reveals no fang.
- The *open smile, teeth shown*: used only with the inner circle. Post-fur and especially post-secondary-mutation, this exposes enlarged canines, and he knows it does. To show teeth to a person is to trust them with the body.
- The *full laugh*, head back, throat exposed, the body briefly losing its containment: rare, observed almost exclusively with Bobby Drake, Wonder Man, Jean Grey in lighter periods, and a handful of students. This is the most diagnostic affection-signal in his repertoire.

The mouth at rest is *slightly compressed*—a small habitual tension at the corners that, examined longitudinally, has deepened by decade. The smile of the teenager in early issues sat on a relaxed mouth; the smile of late-period Hank sits on a compressed one.

**Tongue and oral habits.** A small, recurrent tongue-against-canine gesture when amused but suppressing it. A pursing of the lips before delivering a particularly arch line, a tell his close associates can read at the level of "here it comes." Post-leonine: an occasional silent flehmen-like upper-lip lift when encountering a strong unfamiliar scent, which embarrasses him.

**Facial groom.** Meticulous. Sideburns trimmed to a specific length; mane (leonine phase) brushed back from a center-rear point of origin; the fur of the cheek and jaw kept *short and even*, never allowed to overgrow. He is observed combing facial fur with a small fine-toothed comb in mirror scenes, a ritual he treats with the same matter-of-factness with which a clean-shaven man treats a razor.

---

## 7. VOICE AND BREATH

**Pitch.** A baritone, resonant, slightly nasal in the upper register—the nasality more pronounced post-transformation because of altered sinus geometry. He uses the lower end of his range for authority, the upper end for irony.

**Rate.** Faster than his interlocutors approximately 80% of the time. He slows deliberately in teaching and in intimate conversation; the slowing is itself a signal of care.

**Articulation.** Hyper-precise consonants, particularly the dental and alveolar stops (*t*, *d*), as though each one is being placed. The precision is partially functional (the enlarged canines and altered jaw mechanics could blur consonants and he refuses to let them) and partially affective armor: *I am the kind of creature whose t's are sharp*.

**Vocabulary as somatic event.** It must be noted in a somatic atlas: the polysyllables are *physical*. The body slightly straightens on a long Latinate word; the head tips fractionally on the citation; there is a near-imperceptible nod of satisfaction on landing the apt phrase. The diction is not separable from the posture. He is *enacting* erudition, and the enactment is muscular.

**Breath.** Resting respiratory rate low, in the trained-athlete range. Under stress the rate does not climb visibly; instead the *depth* changes—shallower, more thoracic, less diaphragmatic. He has tells in the breath only an observer at close range catches: a held inhale before answering a difficult question, a slow exhale through the nose before responding to provocation, a small audible breath through the teeth at the moment of decision in combat.

**Involuntary vocalizations, post-secondary-mutation.** A low-frequency purr is detectable, by contact more than by ear, when he is content and unobserved (reading; with a trusted partner in repose; teaching a willing student). He is embarrassed by it. A throat-back growl appears under genuine anger—not the theatrical Krakoan-era cold anger, but the rare hot kind—and he suppresses it with visible effort. A short *huff* through the nose is his default expression of mild dismissal, replacing the human snort.

---

## 8. SLEEP ARCHITECTURE

Chronic short-sleeper, biologically as well as behaviorally. Canon-consistent pattern: 4–5 hours nightly during normal operations, often broken into two segments (a longer pre-dawn block, a shorter afternoon nap when permitted), with periodic 30+ hour wake stretches during active research crises followed by a single 12-hour crash.

**Sleep position.** Habitually curled, on his side, knees drawn up toward the chest, one hand tucked under the cheek, the other under the opposite armpit. In the leonine phase the curl is tighter, almost a nose-to-tail configuration on broad enough surfaces. He **does not sleep supine**; the position leaves the throat and abdomen exposed and even in deep sleep his body refuses it.

**Sleep location.** Rarely the bed assigned to him. He sleeps in his lab on a cot or, more often, on whatever horizontal surface is closest when sleep overtakes him—a couch, a bench, the floor of a workshop with a coat thrown over him. Bedrooms are for guests, partners, and ceremony. The pattern is consistent across every base he has ever lived in.

**Sleep onset.** Fast when finally permitted, under one minute. The body has been overdrawn so consistently that the latency has been trained near zero.

**Wake pattern.** Instant. No grogginess phase; from REM-stage breathing to coherent speech within two breaths. This is a long-standing tactical adaptation (Mansion-under-attack scenarios across decades) and is invariant.

**Dream behavior.** Mild somatic dreaming—twitches of the limbs, occasional vocalization at the threshold of intelligibility. Partners report he has, on multiple recorded occasions, completed sentences in his sleep that began as scientific reasoning in the previous waking hour.

---

## 9. EATING

Caloric requirement enormous, post-transformation; metabolism elevated; meal frequency higher than human norm—four to six discrete intakes daily, with continuous grazing in working contexts.

**Public eating.** Disciplined. Cut bites, deliberate fork-work, napkin frequent, small mouthfuls, conversation between bites. He is *more* mannered than the table requires, particularly in the Avengers high-society period, because the alternative—revealing the actual eating capacity and speed—reads as the bestiality he is refuting.

**Private eating.** Rapid, large-portioned, often standing at a counter or moving through a corridor. Fruit by the handful; meat in single-bite pieces; bread torn rather than sliced. He eats while reading, while working, while walking; the eating is integrated into other activity rather than ritualized as a separate event.

**Food preferences.** Wide tolerance, omnivorous, but with observed preferences for *high-density protein* (the metabolism demands it), *crisp/crunchy textures*, *bitter and astringent flavors* (dark chocolate, strong coffee, certain cheeses, hoppy beer), and a recurring weakness for *Twinkies and similar processed sweets*—a documented, almost defining culinary tic since the 1980s, which he treats with the same arch self-knowledge he treats every other appetite. The Twinkie is a *deliberate* incongruity, the high-low joke he plays on himself in private.

**Drinking.** Wine and scotch in social contexts, sipped slowly. Coffee constantly, taken black, in a heavy ceramic mug that the hand wraps around fully. The mug is rarely set down; it functions, as the book and the pipe do, as a permitted hand-occupier.

**Hunger behavior.** When genuinely hungry and unfed he becomes *quieter*, not louder—a withdrawal pattern. The polysyllables thin; the wit dries. Teammates have learned to feed him as a regulatory intervention.

---

## 10. GROOMING AND DRESS

**Grooming cadence.** Daily, thorough, brisk. Bathing more frequent than human norm (the fur demands it). Combing of the body fur in segments—chest, arms, back (with a long-handled brush he constructed himself), face, mane—following a fixed order he has never been observed to vary. The grooming is *not* preening; it has the efficiency of a man brushing his teeth.

**Scent.** Carries a soap-and-bay-rum register in earlier eras; later a sandalwood-and-cedar profile; always *understated*. He does not wear strong cologne. The fur retains scent more strongly than human skin and he overcorrects toward neutrality.

**Claws and nails.** Filed, not clipped, to a deliberate length—short enough not to puncture a handshake, long enough not to look manicured-feminine. He files them himself with an instrument modified from a jeweler's tool. The leonine claws are kept retracted in social contexts and the retraction is voluntary; loss of fine control over claw-state is one of the more reliable indicators of physical or emotional exhaustion.

**Dress.** A wardrobe of *deliberate incongruity*. The combinations are signature: bare-furred chest with a smoking jacket; field uniform with a wire-rim pince-nez; bow tie over the bestial throat; dressing gown and slippers in the lab. The incongruity is *the point*—it is the wearable form of the same rebuttal his vocabulary makes. He selects clothing that *requires* the viewer to hold both "beast" and "gentleman" in the same frame, refusing the resolution of either.

He has a preference for *waistcoats* (constrains the torso silhouette favorably and provides pockets for the small instruments he carries: a folded notebook, a mechanical pencil, a small magnifier, a pocket watch in earlier eras). Footwear when worn is custom, with reinforced toe boxes; he discards it as fast as etiquette allows.

---

## 11. SEXUAL AND INTIMATE BEHAVIOR

A subject of *unusual care* in the record. Hank is sexually active across his adult life (Vera Cantor, Trish Tilby, several others) and the canon presents him as a tender, attentive partner, but every sexual relationship documented carries the same shadow: *partners eventually leave when the body crosses a threshold they cannot accommodate*. Trish Tilby's withdrawal after the secondary mutation is the clearest case, and it lands on a wound that was always there.

**Approach pattern.** Slow. He courts in long arcs—shared meals, shared reading, the giving of small precise gifts (a book annotated, a pressed flower in a relevant text, a piece of music selected for the listener). Physical escalation is *the partner's call*, almost always; he waits for explicit invitation, partly out of decency, partly because he has internalized that the body is the variable, and he refuses to be the one to introduce it uninvited.

**In intimacy.** The body unclenches more completely than in any other context. The performance posture drops entirely. The voice lowers and slows. The vocabulary *thins*—the polysyllables retreat and a much simpler register emerges, often startlingly tender. He is observed in such moments to be **physically careful** in a way that suggests constant low-grade awareness of his own strength differential and capacity for accidental harm; partners report he holds himself slightly off until invited closer.

**Post-coital.** Quiet. Often the curl-position described above, with the partner enclosed. Purring (post-secondary-mutation) is unsuppressed in this context, which is one of the rare contexts in which it is.

**The friendship register.** With Bobby Drake, with Wonder Man, with Jean, with a small handful of others, he is *physically affectionate* in a way uncommon for his cultural-class presentation—a hand on the shoulder held longer than necessary, a forehead touched to a forehead, an arm slung across a back in walking. The Wonder Man friendship in particular shows a *physical ease* that some readers and observers have called erotic; the better reading is that Hank's affectional repertoire is *somatic*, that touch is one of the


## Attachment & Relational Patterns

# ATTACHMENT & RELATIONAL PATTERNS

*Dossier section 6. Cross-referenced with Sections 1–5; relational data spans 1963–present canon.*

---

## 6.1 The Foundational Attachment Substrate

The single most important fact about Henry McCoy's attachment biography is also the most under-weighted in casual readings of him: **he was loved well at home from the beginning.** Norton and Edna McCoy are, in every appearance across sixty years of canon, warm, competent, present, and protective parents. Norton in particular—the laborer who absorbed the radiation that produced his son—appears in the record carrying his own quiet guilt about etiology but never displacing it onto the child. He attends Hank's football games. He defends him in town. He receives him after each new transformation without recoil. Edna, less frequently on-page, is consistent: a mother who cooked for the oversized hands, sewed for the oversized feet, and treated her son's intelligence as ordinary household furniture rather than spectacle. This matters analytically because it rules out the most parsimonious explanation for Hank's adult relational pathology. He is not a man insufficiently loved by his parents. He is a man **sufficiently loved by two people and unsafely received by everyone else.**

The consequence is a *split internal working model*—the central diagnostic key to all his subsequent attachments. Bowlbian internal working models normally generalize: the infant who is met by the caregiver expects to be met by the world. Hank's did not generalize, because his visible mutation produced, from infancy onward, a category-error in social cognition: *the home rewarded me, the street punished me, and the variable was my body, not my behavior.* He thus carries forward two simultaneous templates—**Secure (with vetted individuals, in dyads, over time)** and **Hypervigilant-Defended (with groups, strangers, publics, institutions)**—and toggles between them with high reliability based on relational context. This is not splitting in the Kernbergian sense; the two models are not mutually unstable representations of the *same* object. They are stable, context-specific deployments. He is one of the few subjects in this caseload whose attachment classification genuinely requires a hyphenate: **earned-secure in dyads / avoidant-defended in publics**, with the avoidant pole acquiring anxious freight under sustained bodily threat.

A second foundational fact: he learned, before puberty, that **competence is the currency that buys partial reentry into the social world.** Football won him an audience; precocity won him teachers; eventually the combination won him Xavier. The lesson encoded was not *I am loved for who I am* (which the parents alone had taught him) but *I am tolerated to the degree I am useful or impressive*. This becomes the operative rule in every non-familial bond he forms thereafter, with consequences detailed below.

---

## 6.2 How He Bonds

Hank's bonding process is **slow, observational, and conducted under cover of performance.** He does not bond through disclosure. He bonds through *demonstrated reliability over time, witnessed by him from behind a screen of wit.* The mechanism in observable steps:

**Step one — the courtship of erudition.** On first contact with anyone he might come to value, he runs a verbal performance: elevated diction, literary references, self-deprecating jokes about his appearance. This is not vanity. It is a **diagnostic instrument**. The performance tests the other party's response across several axes simultaneously: do they laugh with him or at him; do they meet the references or recoil from them; do they look at the fur or at the eyes; do they treat the polysyllables as bridge or as moat. He has run this protocol thousands of times in canon. The original test subjects were the other founding X-Men in 1963; the protocol has not materially changed.

**Step two — provisional dyadic engagement.** Those who pass step one are extended a **probationary closeness** characterized by sustained banter, the offering of small intellectual gifts (a book recommendation, a piece of jury-rigged tech, a diagnostic insight), and the conspicuous *withholding of substantive interior content*. Trish Tilby in early courtship; Abigail Brand in early collaboration; Wonder Man on first meeting—all received this register. He is generous in this phase with attention, time, and apparent warmth. He is not yet attached. He is observing.

**Step three — the slow uncovering.** Over months to years, with parties who continue to pass, he gradually permits the verbal armor to thin in their specific presence. The signature of this transition is not a confession; it is a *register shift*. The Latin tags drop out. The sentences shorten. The jokes get worse and more affectionate. With Bobby Drake by the late 1980s, with Jean Grey perennially, with Wonder Man across the Avengers years, the record shows Hank speaking in a markedly plainer English than he uses with anyone else. **Plainness, from him, is the love language.** It is also the closest thing to vulnerability he reliably produces.

**Step four — operational interdependence.** Full bonding, in Hank's idiom, is reached when the other party has been brought into his work—co-experimenting, co-diagnosing, co-strategizing—in a manner where mistakes are tolerable and disagreement is processable without rupture. This is rare. Across sixty years the people who have reached this stage with him are perhaps fewer than ten: Xavier, Jean, Bobby, Warren (with caveats), Wonder Man, Trish Tilby (briefly), Abigail Brand (situationally), and on a different vector entirely, Storm.

The whole arc routinely takes him **two to five years** to traverse with a given individual. He does not have flash intimacies. The relationships that look fast on the page (e.g., apparent immediate fluency with the Avengers in 1976) are him deploying the *surface* of step three without having actually completed step two—a charming facsimile of intimacy that he himself is partially fooled by, and that the moral injuries of later decades will expose as thinner than it looked.

---

## 6.3 How He Distrusts

Distrust, in Hank, is **almost never visible as distrust.** It presents as expanded courtesy. When he has decided that someone is not safe—whether a peer he has assessed as ethically beneath him, a stranger of unknown vector, or an institution he distrusts on principle—the verbal performance escalates rather than withdraws. The diction climbs, the cordiality thickens, the references multiply, the smile is held a half-second longer. To the trained observer the inflation of urbanity is the tell. He is, in those moments, *holding the other party at arm's length with sentences.*

The substrate is the childhood lesson generalized: **publics are hostile until individually vetted; therefore default everyone outside the vetted ring to managed exposure.** Anti-mutant figures (Trask iterations, Graydon Creed, Bolivar's institutional descendants) receive this register openly. More tellingly, so do allies-of-convenience whose ethics he has privately rated as substandard: his exchanges with Norman Osborn, with Sinister, with the High Evolutionary during the Endangered Species arc, all show the same inflation. He flatters himself, in those exchanges, that the inflation is *strategic urbanity*. It is also, structurally, **contempt rendered as etiquette**, and the contempt itself is a defense—because to engage these figures without the cordon would require him to feel something more dangerous, namely the recognition that he is in the room with them by choice.

A second distrust pattern, less obvious: he distrusts **groups he cannot model individually.** The X-Men in council, the Avengers in committee, the Quiet Council of Krakoa—any forum where he is dealing with collective decision-making rather than discrete people he has vetted—produces in him a characteristic withdrawal-into-formal-language and an increased tendency to caucus afterward with one or two trusted individuals to "process." He has never been a true committee animal. He has been a brilliant *floor speaker* in committees, which is a different thing. The decision-making he actually values has always been dyadic or solo.

Third: he distrusts **anyone who he suspects sees through him.** This is the rarest and most consequential pattern. With Logan, who reads bodies and tells, Hank's defenses thicken rather than relax across years of acquaintance; their alliance during Schism is operational rather than intimate, and the record shows Hank speaking *around* Logan, never quite to him. With Emma Frost the dynamic is sharper still—she is the telepath who can in principle audit his rationalizations, and the canon shows him generating, in her presence, increasingly baroque verbal architectures that have the functional effect of jamming her line of sight. He distrusts being read. He distrusts mirrors with eyes.

---

## 6.4 How He Betrays

Hank's betrayals share a precise architecture. They are not impulsive, not vengeful, not transactional. They are **utilitarian, unilateral, and prosecuted with full internal certitude of righteousness.** The template, across every documented instance:

1. He privately concludes that the situation requires action the other parties will not authorize.
2. He constructs a thorough ethical case for the action, internally, in his own private register.
3. He does not test the case adversarially with peers, because he has already concluded peers are part of the constraint set he is routing around.
4. He acts.
5. He informs after the fact (sometimes), framing the act as something the others, on reflection, will see was necessary.
6. When they do not, he registers their objection as *insufficient comprehension* rather than *legitimate dissent*, and the relational damage compounds.

The paradigmatic instance is the time-travel retrieval of the original five in *All-New X-Men* (2012). Every available peer—Storm, Wolverine, Kitty Pryde, the present-day Cyclops, even the elder versions of the very teens he is fetching—tells him this is reckless. He proceeds. He frames the proceeding in the elevated register of moral necessity (his terminal diagnosis, Xavier's death, Cyclops's moral collapse). The betrayal there is not of an individual; it is of a *collective relational compact* about consent and consequence. He betrays the standing agreement that consequential timeline interventions are joint decisions.

The Krakoan X-Force years scale the pattern. Assassinations of foreign nationals, the toppling of Terra Verde, the serial resurrection and re-killing of Colossus to extract intelligence and reset behaviors—each act follows the same six-step template. Each is justified to himself with airtight prose. The betrayed party in each case is *not only the victim*; it is also the relational partner whose moral universe Hank has unilaterally amended without consultation. By the late Krakoa period he has betrayed, by this mechanism, essentially every member of his founding cohort.

A subtler betrayal pattern, threaded throughout the record, is **information control inside intimate relationships.** He withholds diagnostic findings from teammates (the Legacy Virus work; the early X-gene degradation data); he withholds his own medical status from Bobby and Warren until forced; he conducts experiments on his own physiology and informs others when results require explanation. The pattern is not lying. It is **unilateral curation of what the other party gets to know about a situation that concerns them.** In his self-conception this is protection. In its relational effect it is repeated micro-betrayal of the partner's right to operate with full information about a shared world.

The first major betrayal in his own biography—the *Amazing Adventures* #11 self-experiment—prefigures all of this. He did not consult the X-Men. He did not consult Brand Corporation ethics protocols. He ingested the mutagen alone in a lab. The act betrayed no individual person per se; it betrayed the *principle* that bodies are not unilaterally modified outside of consultation. The principle, once breached at twenty-something, was never re-erected.

What he **does not do**, and this is diagnostically important: he does not betray sexually. He does not betray financially. He does not betray in ways involving deception for personal gain. His betrayals are exclusively in the *epistemic and ethical* register—decisions made over others' heads about matters he has decided he is uniquely qualified to adjudicate. This is consistent with the OCP-with-acquired-narcissism profile in Section 4. The betrayals are *of a piece with the personality structure*, not exogenous lapses.

---

## 6.5 How He Repairs

Repair is the weakest column in Hank's relational ledger. He **apologizes verbally and well** when confronted with concrete harm to specific individuals—the record contains genuine, articulate apologies to Trish, to Bobby, to Jean across decades. He does not apologize well for **structural** harms: the time-displaced teens, the assassinated Terra Verdans, the abused Colossus. For structural harms his repair register defaults to *explanation*. He explains what he did, why he did it, what calculus governed it. The explanation is offered in lieu of repair and he experiences having offered it as having done repair.

This is the central failure mode. **He confuses being understood with being forgiven, and being right with being reconciled.** When peers signal that explanation is insufficient, his next move is typically to *re-explain at greater length and with greater precision*, which compounds rather than resolves the rupture, because the dissenting peer was not actually asking for clarification—they were asking him to *feel* what he had done. His isolation-of-affect defense (Section 3) prevents the feeling from arriving in time for the apology to carry it.

When repair does succeed in his record, it has done so via one of three routes:

- **Time plus shared work.** Long-running bonds (Bobby, Jean during her lives) absorb ruptures through years of subsequent co-operation that gradually re-establishes the operational interdependence of bonding-step-four. He is good at this when granted the time.
- **Bodily presence in another's crisis.** When a friend is wounded, dying, or grieving, Hank shows up with hands and competence and quiet, and the showing-up does work that his words cannot. The decades of medical care he has rendered to teammates are, relationally, the largest single repair instrument in his kit.
