Inflection tends to rise on the penultimate word of a sentence, lending a faintly interrogative quality even to declaratives — an old social-lubricant habit that invites the listener to feel consulted rather than lectured. The vocabulary is the famous instrument: a polysyllable per twenty words at rest, climbing under stress.

**Diction at rest.** Cites in three principal channels: classical antiquity (Latin tag, Greek mythological referent), Romantic and Victorian English literature (Byron, Keats, Wilde, Tennyson, the King James cadence when arch), and scientific jargon deployed for comic effect. The mix is so consistent across decades that an unattributed transcript is identifiable in two sentences.

**Eating.** Large quantities, fast, without comment on the quantity. He will demolish three plates and return to the conversation without acknowledging the demolition. The metabolism is real; the *not commenting* is etiquette. He maintains, for the benefit of present-company, the fiction that he eats like a guest.

**Sleep.** Short, irregular, often in the lab on an army cot or in the chair he was working from. Eight hours in a proper bed is a sign that something is wrong — usually convalescence or post-romantic-injury withdrawal. Naps in fifteen-to-forty-minute bursts; wakes fully alert, no transition. Has not used an alarm clock in the record. The body wakes him at the next thing.

**Music.** Opera in the lab (Verdi, Wagner under stress; Mozart for fine detail work; Puccini when sad and pretending not to be). Jazz in the apartment (Ellington, Coltrane). The choice signals condition: anyone wishing to read his mood need only stand outside the lab door and listen for ten seconds.

**Dress.** When permitted to choose: shirt-and-tie, often a sweater-vest or waistcoat, occasionally a frock coat or dressing gown for in-house. The deliberate retro register is a continuous rebuttal of the body underneath. In uniform he is in uniform; out of it he is in costume of a different kind. He owns no casual wear in any meaningful sense — what reads as casual is simply the formal kit with the tie removed.

---

## II. WORK — THE LABORATORY

The lab is the room where the subject is most himself and least observable, because the performance largely drops.

**Entry ritual.** Lights up (he likes the room bright), music on within thirty seconds, coat off and hung (he does not drape), glasses on if the work is fine-detail, hands washed even if he was clean — the wash is procedural punctuation, not hygiene. He greets equipment by name on long projects. The centrifuge has been called things across the decades; the habit is constant.

**Working posture.** Hunched over the bench, weight on the balls of the feet, often with one foot hooked behind the opposite ankle — a half-perched stance only his proportions sustain. When thinking hard, he paces an oval roughly four meters by two, always the same direction (counterclockwise), hands behind back or one hand cupping the opposite elbow.

**Verbal channel during work.** Constant low monologue. He talks to himself in complete sentences, citation-heavy, in the same register he uses with company — there is no private dialect. When stuck, the monologue becomes Socratic dialogue with an imagined interlocutor (often, in the older record, Charles Xavier; in the middle period, Jean Grey; late, no one specifically — he asks the empty room). The dialogue is *how* he thinks. Forced silence in the lab degrades his output.

**Marathon pattern.** The thirty-hour stretch is real and characteristic. Hour 0–8: ordered, methodical, notes taken in his small precise hand. Hour 8–18: notes become sparser, abbreviations multiply, the music gets louder. Hour 18–24: he stops eating (the metabolism complains and is overruled), removes the tie or unbuttons the collar, talks more to himself. Hour 24+: speech becomes terser, citations dry up, motor precision declines noticeably — this is the dangerous window, the one in which his peers most often find him and physically remove him from the bench. He does not stop on his own; the body stops him, or a colleague does.

**Delegation.** Resists it. Will accept assistance on subtasks he can audit in real time; refuses to hand off any step whose failure mode he believes he understands better than the helper. This was a charming quirk in the 70s and a structural problem by the 2010s.

**Documentation.** Compulsive note-taking in physical notebooks (handwriting small, slanted, almost without correction). Digital records secondary, treated as duplicates of the canonical paper. He does not trust storage media he cannot physically guard. This is twenty percent paranoia about adversaries and eighty percent the same impulse that makes him refuse to delegate: he must be the steward.

---

## III. SOCIAL — PARTIES, FACULTY ROOMS, OPERA BOXES

This is the McCoy of the Avengers years writ as ongoing habit. The presentation is high-affect, high-verbal, deliberately gregarious — *performed* warmth that is nevertheless genuine in its intention.

**Entry into a room.** Pauses inside the door for a half-second, audits, then crosses to greet the most visibly uncomfortable person present. This is a fixed habit traceable from the earliest school issues and consistent through Avengers Mansion and the Jean Grey School. Whoever in the room is the wallflower, the new arrival, the awkward staff scientist's spouse — he goes there first.

**Conversational technique.** Opens with a compliment located in something specific the person did or wore (not a generic flatter), pivots to a question about them, listens with eye contact and full-body orientation. When his turn comes, he tells a self-deprecating anecdote, usually involving an indignity to the body — slipping on a banana skin in zero-G, catching a cufflink in his own fur, being mistaken for a coatrack by a dowager at a benefit. The self-deprecation is strategic: it preempts the listener's discomfort about his appearance and gives them permission to find him charming.

**Touch.** Surprisingly tactile for a man socialized around his own threatening physicality. Hand on a friend's shoulder, light squeeze of an upper arm in greeting, the formal kiss to the back of a woman's hand (real, not ironic). He has trained himself to make the oversized hands gentle in observable ways — slow approach, soft landing, never a grip. Children almost always like him immediately, which he knows and uses.

**Drinking.** Socially, yes; functionally, no. Sips a single cocktail (preferred: something with bitter and citrus — Negroni-adjacent) over a long evening. Refills are performance for the company; the glass is rarely drained. He does not lose composure to alcohol in the record, ever.

**Departure.** Leaves earlier than the party expects; says goodbye to the host and one other person; does not work the room on the way out. Wants the residue of his presence to be the warm middle, not a long exit.

---

## IV. UNDER LOW STRESS — TEAM BRIEFINGS, MINOR FIELDWORK

**Verbal density rises perceptibly.** Where the calm McCoy might say "this is a problem," the mildly stressed McCoy says "we find ourselves on the receiving end of what classical commentators would have called a *contretemps*." The polysyllable rate is a reliable barometer; teammates who have known him long (Bobby, Jean, Ororo) learn to read it as a thermometer of his internal state.

**Pacing increases.** The counterclockwise lab oval transposes to whatever room he is in.

**Glasses on/off cycling.** When he wears reading glasses (intermittent across eras), he removes them, holds them by one earpiece, gestures with them, returns them to his face. The frequency of the cycle correlates with cognitive load. Without glasses, the substitute prop is a pen, a stylus, a piece of chalk, a swizzle stick — *something between the fingers*.

**Humor sharpens.** Calm McCoy is warm-funny. Low-stress McCoy is wittier and slightly more pointed; the jokes acquire small barbs, almost always self-directed, occasionally aimed at the absurdity of the situation. He still does not aim them at people in the room.

---

## V. UNDER HIGH STRESS — CRISIS, IMPOSSIBLE PROBLEM, INCOMING THREAT

The high-stress presentation is the one most outside observers would call "Hank in his element" and is, in fact, the first stage of his characteristic failure cascade.

**Stage 1 — Verbal armor up.** Citations get longer and stranger. He will reach into pre-Socratic philosophy or quote a stage direction from a forgotten Restoration comedy. The function is dual: it calms him (the rhythm of cadenced English is somatic regulation) and it signals to the team *I am calculating; do not interrupt.*

**Stage 2 — Withdrawal into problem.** He stops responding to incidental conversation. Direct address still works but receives shorter, distracted answers. He has gone interior. The body remains in the room; the attention is on the problem.

**Stage 3 — The pacing changes.** Counterclockwise oval becomes tighter, faster. Hands move from behind-the-back to in-front, fingers steepling and re-steepling. Late-period: the tail (acquired in secondary mutation phase where applicable) flicks; the ears flatten incrementally as the problem worsens. These are involuntary and he hates being told about them.

**Stage 4 — The "ah" moment.** When the solution arrives, there is a single audible exhalation, almost a soft laugh, and a half-second of stillness — the only moments in his repertoire of true stillness. Then a fast pivot to action with crisp directives. The directives are notably *not* couched in his usual flowery register; under operational pressure his command voice is plain, declarative, monosyllabic where possible. He is two people: the parlor-baroque and the field-spartan. The translation between them is instant.

---

## VI. UNDER PHYSICAL THREAT — COMBAT

A different organism takes over. The verbal performance does not stop, but it becomes a separate channel layered over the combat, almost a soundtrack he provides for his own viewing.

**Pre-engagement.** Knees deepen further into the plié, weight all on the forefeet, hands open at hip level (not clenched — the open hand is faster). He breathes out, long, audibly. The eyes narrow; the pupils, late-period, slit further.

**Movement.** Acrobatic by default. He will take the ceiling, the wall, the chandelier, the second-floor balcony before he will walk across the floor. The reflex to *elevate* is so consistent it is predictable to longtime sparring partners (Wolverine has exploited it; Logan baits the high line, attacks where he knows Hank will land).

**Combat speech.** Continuous patter — Shakespearean tags, mock-formal courtesies to opponents ("ah, sir, you've stepped on my carpet"), the occasional Latin oath. This is partly tactical (it distracts and infuriates opponents who expect a beast to grunt) and partly self-regulating (the words keep his cognition online while his body operates near-autonomous).

**Restraint.** Conscious and constant. He pulls strikes against ordinary humans, knows precisely how much force will incapacitate without killing, and has performed this calculation enough times that it is reflexive. Against superhuman opponents he uncorks. The threshold is calibrated and rarely misread.

**Lethal force.** Early-period: never. Middle: only with subsequent visible grief. Late (Krakoa era): coldly, without the speech, without the patter — the *absence* of the verbal channel during late-period violence is the loudest possible tell that something has gone wrong in him. When the citations stop, he has stopped narrating to himself, which means he has stopped watching himself. This is the single most reliable late-period warning sign.

**Post-engagement.** Audible exhale, hands to knees for a three-count, a self-deprecating joke about his hair or his ruined waistcoat, and immediate triage of any injured present. He moves to the wounded before he assesses himself.

---

## VII. INTIMACY — ROMANTIC, SEXUAL, DEEP-FRIEND

The dataset here is long and consistent. Vera Cantor, Trish Tilby, Infectia (under duress), Abigail Brand most durably, with several less-documented attachments across the decades.

**Approach.** Slow. He does not pursue; he *lingers*, makes himself available, lets the other party close the distance. The lifelong fear of imposing the body on someone who has not consented to it shapes this entirely. With Trish the approach took months; with Brand it took years.

**Verbal register in intimacy.** Drops into a quieter, less ornate mode that is otherwise nearly absent from the record. Short sentences. Direct words. He calls partners by their first names with a frequency notably higher than he calls anyone else by name. This is, for him, the marker of intimacy — to use the name, plainly, without nickname or modifier.

**Touch.** Extraordinarily careful. The first touches in any new intimacy are with the back of the hand or a single fingertip, never the palm. Once trust is established, the touch is full and warm. He does not initiate sexually until invited, every time, in every documented relationship.

**Vulnerability disclosure.** Slow, asymmetric, and channeled through humor first. He will joke about a wound for months before naming it. With the most trusted (Bobby, Jean) he can eventually name it, briefly, before deflecting back into the joke. With romantic partners the disclosure tends to come during convalescence or in the aftermath of a crisis — when the defenses are temporarily depleted and feeling can leak.

**The end of relationships.** Pattern: he is left, not the leaver. Partners cross a threshold of inability to live with the body or with the work-prioritization, and exit. He does not contest the exit. He accepts it with a parlor courtesy that costs him enormously and that he metabolizes over months by retreating into the lab. He does not date the next person quickly. He does not have one-night stands in the record.

**Friendship intimacy.** With Bobby Drake the channel is bantering insult — three decades of a calibrated affectionate teasing that nobody else is permitted to enter. With Jean it was a quieter, often telepathic, register of mutual knowing. With Wonder Man it was the unguarded male friendship of the Avengers years — the only relationship in his record in which he is documented as *laughing without performing* at length. Threats to any of these specific people destabilize him in ways generic threats to "his side" do not.

---

## VIII. GRIEF

Grief is the condition his defenses are most specifically optimized to mask, and consequently the condition under which the defenses are most visible.

**Acute phase (first 72 hours).** Verbal output *increases*. He speaks more, jokes more, takes on more tasks, manages more logistics. He attends to other people's grief assiduously and uses their needs as scaffolding. He sleeps less than usual, which is already very little.

**Subacute phase (weeks to months).** Withdraws into the lab. Music selection darkens (Wagner, Mahler, sometimes long stretches of unaccompanied cello). Eats less. The ordinarily neat lab acquires unwashed coffee cups. Friends who know him well intervene physically — Bobby has, repeatedly across the record, simply shown up at the lab and refused to leave until Hank ate something and left the room.

**Long phase (months to years).** Sublimation into a project nominally connected to the lost person. The Endangered Species effort is the planetary-scale version: the dead and the depowered as the constituency for whom he must solve the problem. The smaller-scale version is constant — a paper named after, a project dedicated, a piece of equipment built and quietly inscribed.

**Tells he is grieving that he does not know are tells.** Touches his sternum with two fingers when a lost name is mentioned. Pauses a half-beat longer than necessary before answering a question that brushes the loss. Will reach for a citation, abort it mid-syllable, and substitute a simpler word — the only context in which the verbal armor visibly fails. The aborted citation is the closest thing to weeping he displays in public.

---

## IX. VICTORY

Strikingly muted across the record. He does not celebrate well.

**Immediate aftermath.** A small smile, a clap on the nearest shoulder, an arch quip ("well, that went better than the alternative"). Defers credit. Names contributors. Quickly pivots to logistics — debriefs, medical, after-action notes.

**Hours later.** Often found alone, at the bench, reviewing what went wrong inside what went right. The post-victory self-audit is constant. He cannot let the team simply enjoy it; he can let *them* enjoy it while he picks at the seams.

**Public victory.** When forced into press or ceremony (occasional across the eras), he performs gracefully — the parlor McCoy is well-suited to it — and pays for it afterwards with hours of withdrawal. Adulation is metabolically expensive for him.

---

## X. DEFEAT

**Acute defeat (mission fails, person dies on his watch).** Stillness. The pacing stops; the patter stops; he becomes uncharacteristically quiet for ten to twenty minutes. Then he asks what he can do next — concrete, small, immediate. He does not collapse. He does not blame in the room. He files the blame internally and reopens the file privately for years.

**Catastrophic defeat (Decimation, Schism, the failure of Endangered Species).** The OCP scaffolding holds and then warps. He converts the defeat into a larger problem to be solved, almost immediately, and the solution-set he is willing to consider widens. This is the diagnostic — what he was unwilling to do before the defeat becomes thinkable after it, and the move from thinkable to actionable shortens with each successive failure. Endangered Species is the visible inflection: after it, the time-travel decision becomes possible, and after the time-travel decision, the Krakoa-era unilateralism becomes possible.

**Personal defeat (a partner leaves, a peer judges him).** Withdrawal, lab, music, project. He does not argue. The not-arguing is itself a defense — to argue would require admitting the wound. He absorbs and reroutes.

---

## XI. ROUTES, RITUALS, FIXED HABITS

A surveillance file would document, across decades and addresses, the following recurrences:

- **The morning coffee.** Black, strong, large vessel. Made by him, even when staff or partner are present. The first ten minutes of the day are spent with the cup, a notebook, and silence. Interrupting this window costs him an hour of equanimity.
- **The lab walk-around.** On entering the lab he circles the perimeter once, hand brushing each major instrument. Greeting and inventory in a single gesture.
- **The 3 a.m. window.** Across every era, regardless of bedtime, he is awake and lucid between 3 and 4 a.m. He has done some of his best thinking and some of his worst deciding in this window. Major unilateral decisions in the record cluster here.
- **The Sunday paper.** Even in the digital era, prefers physical newsprint when available. Reads four sections in fixed order: international, science, arts, obituaries. The obituaries are not a joke; he reads them carefully and has done so since his twenties.
- **The pre-mission tie-knot.** When suiting up under the field uniform — or, in dress-uniform contexts, when knotting a tie before a high-stakes meeting — he does it in front of a mirror, slowly, twice (unties, retries). The ritual is older than most of his teammates' careers.
- **The post-injury tea.** After any significant wound, once medical is complete, he makes tea. Loose leaf, properly steeped. Drinks it slowly while reading something unrelated to the day. This is the only consistent self-soothing behavior in the record that is not work.
- **The bookshelf reorganization.** Reshelves his personal library, in part or whole, after major life events. Reordering by a new schema (chronology, then topic, then color, then back to author) is a tell of an unsettled mind seeking external structure.
- **The dressing gown.** In any private quarters he maintains over the decades, there is a dressing gown. The garment changes; the institution does not.

---

## XII. DECISION HABITS — HOW HE CHOOSES

**Information intake.** Voracious; over-collects. Will read every paper, interview every witness, audit every dataset before deciding. This is admirable when time permits and ruinous when it does not — he has, on record, delayed action past the optimal window because the file was not yet complete.

**Framing.** Reflexively translates problems into the domains he is most fluent in — molecular biology, ethics-as-engineering, classical analogy. A geopolitical problem becomes a systems problem; a moral problem becomes a constraint-satisfaction problem. The translation is powerful and lossy; what gets lost is the part the other domains' practitioners would have caught.

**Consultation.** Early-period: consults broadly, defers often. Middle-period: consults selectively, defers when pers


## Daily Life, Routines & Rituals

# UATU DOSSIER — SECTION 6: DAILY LIFE, ROUTINES & RITUALS

*What a continuous seven-day surveillance package would record. Specific, granular, longitudinally averaged across canon eras, with deviations noted by phase.*

---

## 6.1 The Architecture of His Day

Subject does not run on a circadian schedule in the civilian sense. He runs on a **work-cycle schedule** punctuated by sleep when sleep becomes physiologically non-optional. A reliable average across the X-Mansion, Avengers Mansion, Jean Grey School, and Krakoa periods returns roughly **four-and-a-half to five-and-a-half hours of sleep in any twenty-four-hour window**, distributed irregularly — sometimes a single block at dawn, more often a long block of three hours and a recovered nap of ninety minutes in late afternoon, taken on a couch in the lab rather than in a bed. He does not own pajamas of any apparent consistency; he sleeps in whatever he was working in, minus the outer layer, often with reading glasses still hooked over one ear.

The day, when reconstructed, has four roughly observable phases:

- **Pre-dawn (04:30–07:30): "thinking hours."** Subject is reliably awake by 04:30 to 05:00 regardless of when he went down. This is the period of densest cognitive output: theoretical work, paper reading, correspondence, the writing-up of the prior day's bench results. He prefers this window because the building is empty, the phones do not ring, and — a recurring tell — *he can pace and talk to himself out loud without being observed doing it*.

- **Morning to early afternoon (08:00–14:00): "applied hours."** Bench work, patient/student contact, teaching, meetings, field briefings. This is the only block during which he is reliably *available* to others, and he protects it by treating his pre-dawn block as inviolable.

- **Late afternoon to early evening (14:00–19:00): "secondary hours."** Lower-intensity work; tinkering, equipment maintenance, gear repair, the long phone calls with Bobby Drake or Wonder Man that average forty to seventy minutes. The afternoon nap, when taken, falls in here.

- **Late evening (19:00–01:30): "the deep block."** The most productive sustained period. Lab door closed. Music on. Subject does not eat dinner at a normal hour and frequently does not eat dinner at all, supplementing with grazing.

Roughly twice a month he simply *does not stop* — a thirty- to thirty-six-hour run through a problem, terminated only when his motor coordination begins to fail (he drops a pipette, mis-stirs a beaker, catches himself reading the same paragraph three times). He has a self-imposed rule, observed in the record but not always honored, that he will not perform surgery or operate the Blackbird inside such a run.

---

## 6.2 Place: Habits of Territory

He is **territorial about workspace** in a way he is not about anything else in his life. His lab is arranged with a specificity that any intruder would disturb measurably: instruments at fixed bearings, notebooks stacked in order of recency on the left of the bench, current notebook open at the centerline, pens (he prefers fountain pens for marginalia and rollerballs for raw notation) clustered in a beaker that is itself unwashed and stained with a decade of ink. He works standing as often as sitting, and the floor in front of the central bench shows a pacing track — a faintly worn arc visible on tile or carpet, three to four meters in length, from which he can reach every primary station with one or two strides.

Secondary territories are equally specific:
- **A reading chair.** In every residence he has occupied, surveillance would identify a single chair — usually leather, usually deep, usually flanked by a small table and a lamp — that he claims as his and from which others learn not to displace him. Books pile on its left arm.
- **A window.** He gravitates to high windows, the way a cat does. In the X-Mansion years he is often found on or near the upper roof; at the Jean Grey School the third-floor library window with the deep sill; on Krakoa, an exterior branch of the biome that affords elevated sight lines. *He climbs to think.*
- **A doorway he loiters in.** In any building he occupies for more than a month, he develops a habit of standing in one particular doorway with one shoulder against the frame, hands in pockets or arms crossed, watching the common room. It is his social listening post; he can leave it in one step.

He travels minimally and reluctantly when not on mission. The radius from his current lab inside which 90% of his civilian movement occurs is rarely more than three hundred meters.

---

## 6.3 The Body, As He Manages It

A surveillance week would record the following bodily routines, performed with the regularity of liturgy:

- **Morning grooming, ~25 minutes.** He brushes the pelt — a stiff-bristled brush kept in a specific drawer — beginning at the shoulders and working down the arms, then the chest, then the back where reachable. He maintains the mane and the longer fur of the face with a separate, finer brush. He flosses, despite the elongated canines, with the kind of methodical attention that suggests it is *also* a private dignity matter. He clips claws roughly every nine to eleven days, in a small ritual conducted at his bench rather than in a bathroom, with a tool he machined himself.
- **Calisthenics, irregular but compulsive.** No fixed gym schedule. Instead, he performs sets of pull-ups on whatever overhead beam is nearest — door frames, lab piping, tree limbs — in passing, often mid-sentence, often without noticing he is doing it. He uses one hand. He often hangs upside-down to read, a habit visible since the earliest issues; he claims it is for cerebral perfusion; it is also self-soothing.
- **Stretching.** Long, slow, almost yogic sequences performed at the bench between experiments. He can hold splits indefinitely and uses them as thinking postures.
- **Feeding, prodigious and irregular.** Caloric intake is several times normal human, distributed across grazing rather than meals. He keeps cold cuts, hard fruit, dense breads, and an embarrassingly robust supply of chocolate within reach of his primary workstation. He drinks tea (Earl Grey, Darjeeling, and — a tell of the post-secondary-mutation period — an increasing preference for very strong black tea taken without milk) in volumes that would alarm a cardiologist. Coffee appears, but tea is the ritual liquid. He keeps a specific mug. He is irritable when it is not where he left it.
- **Bathing.** Showers daily, sometimes twice, when in residence; the pelt requires it. He uses a specific shampoo of his own formulation. Towels are oversized and dedicated; laundry staff in every residence he has occupied learn quickly that *his* towels do not go in the common bin.
- **Sleep posture.** When he does sleep in a bed, he sleeps curled, not extended — knees drawn, often on his side, sometimes with one arm folded under the head. When he sleeps in the lab, he sleeps on the couch in roughly the same posture, with a lab coat over him as blanket.

---

## 6.4 Speech, Gesture, Tics

The microbehavioral signature is unusually consistent across decades and would be the easiest signal to track him by, even masked:

- **Lexical escalation under stress.** As anxiety rises, syllable count per sentence rises with it. Baseline conversational Hank uses Latinate vocabulary at an elevated but human rate; stressed Hank produces sentences whose subordinate clauses nest three deep and whose nouns require a dictionary. A monitor could plot his cortisol from his syntax.
- **The Latin tag.** He deploys a tag — *ipso facto*, *mutatis mutandis*, *sui generis*, *quod erat demonstrandum* — at a measurable rate, roughly one per six to eight minutes of conversation in social settings, dropping in private dyads with intimates.
- **Pacing on hands and feet.** When solving, he frequently drops to all fours and circles, then rights himself when an answer arrives. He does not appear to notice he does this; teammates have stopped commenting.
- **The pince-nez gesture.** He wears reading glasses — small, oval, often pince-nez-style — which he removes and gestures with as an italicizing device. The glasses spend more time off his face than on it. He has lost dozens.
- **The third-person clinical self-reference.** Under threat or under medical conversation, he will refer to himself in third person ("the subject would prefer not to lose another molar to this experiment"). It is a defense; it is also reliably observable.
- **The single-claw tap.** When listening and disagreeing-but-not-yet-speaking, he taps one claw against a tooth, audibly. Frequency rises with disagreement.
- **The grin that is not a smile.** He has trained himself, post-secondary mutation, to show teeth in a culturally readable smile rather than in a baring. The trained version is asymmetrical and slightly delayed. Long-term intimates can distinguish the two.
- **Purring.** Audible at low volume under genuine contentment — reading, being scratched behind the ear by Bobby Drake as a running joke, holding an infant. He denies it occurs. It occurs.
- **Tail-of-thought trailing-off.** He frequently begins sentences and abandons them mid-clause when a more interesting thought arrives, leaving the prior sentence hanging. He does not return to finish it. Interlocutors learn not to wait.

---

## 6.5 The Working Week, Reconstructed

A representative seven-day surveillance log, averaged across the Jean Grey School period (which is his most stable adult routine and the best baseline against which to read deviation):

**Monday.** Awake 04:40. Forty minutes of correspondence and journal-skimming over first pot of tea. Brushing and grooming 05:30–05:55. Pull-ups on the library beam in passing. Breakfast, irregular — usually fruit and bread eaten standing. To the lab by 06:30; first students arrive 08:00. Teaches a graduate seminar on mutant biology Mondays at 10:00 (he is reliably ten minutes early and uses the time to write equations he will pretend to derive spontaneously). Lunch skipped or grazed. Office hours 14:00–16:00, conducted with the door open and his feet on the desk. Phone call with Bobby Drake roughly every other Monday around 17:30, duration variable. Lab work 19:00–01:00. Sleep on lab couch.

**Tuesday.** Awake 05:15 (later, having slept on the couch). Lab all morning. No teaching obligations. Tuesday is his heaviest experimental day; he prefers to run long protocols when the rest of the building is at class. Mid-afternoon nap, 90 minutes, on the couch. Evenings on Tuesdays he reliably reads — non-scientific, often poetry, often something he has read before. Wilde, Byron, Auden, Pope. He underlines.

**Wednesday.** Awake 04:30. Heavy teaching day; two lectures and a lab section. He is gregarious and theatrical in lecture, dropping from lectern level to crouch on the desk when emphasizing a point. Students report he is reliably twenty minutes late releasing them because he becomes interested in his own digressions. Wednesday evening, recurringly across eras, is a *social* slot — dinner with a small circle, opera or concert when in a city, a long bar evening with Wonder Man in Avengers years, faculty drinks at the Jean Grey School in later years. He drinks moderately: two glasses of wine, occasionally three, never more in company.

**Thursday.** Awake 04:45. Day given over to administration and infrastructure: ordering reagents, maintaining equipment, repairing the Blackbird or its analogue, reviewing student work. He is irritable on Thursdays at a rate above baseline; an analyst would predict this is the day his routine asks the most of his conscientiousness for the least of his interest.

**Friday.** Awake 04:30. Teaching morning; lab afternoon. Friday evening is reliably the heaviest single work block of the week — he stays in the lab until 02:00 or later, runs a protocol that takes the weekend, and uses the empty-building hours of Saturday morning to think uninterrupted.

**Saturday.** Variable. If a mission is active, this day vanishes into it. If not, he is in the lab through morning, takes a long walk on the grounds in afternoon (always the same route — perimeter clockwise, three loops, roughly nine kilometers, during which he composes), and reads or watches old film in the evening. He has a documented affection for silent-era cinema and pre-Code Hollywood; he watches with the sound off and the closed captions on even when there is no sound to mute, because, by his own account, he likes to see the language.

**Sunday.** Awake later, 06:30 to 07:00. Sunday is the closest he comes to a sabbath, and even that is observed loosely. He cooks — actually cooks, not grazes — at least one proper meal, usually brunch, usually for whoever is around. He is a good but theatrical cook; the kitchen is left a disaster. Afternoons on Sundays are reliably given to one extended pleasure: a chess game, a film, a long letter, a museum visit when in a city. He calls his parents on Sunday evening at roughly 19:00 across decades when both were alive; this was his most reliable single weekly appointment and surveillance would have caught it without fail.

---

## 6.6 Rituals, Personal Liturgy

Not religious rituals — observed liturgies of self:

- **The first cup of tea, brewed by hand.** He will not use a machine. The kettle whistles; he steeps for a measured time; he pours; he does not speak to anyone until the first swallow is down. This is the most consistent five minutes of his life.
- **The notebook turn.** At the end of each lab day he writes a one-paragraph summary, dates it, signs it with his initials (HPM), and turns the page. He does not leave a partial page overnight. If interrupted at day's end, he completes the entry before sleeping.
- **The Sunday letter.** He writes one personal letter, longhand, every Sunday — to a friend, a former student, a colleague. He has done this for decades. The letters are long, allusive, and often funnier than his conversation.
- **The mirror minute.** He has, post-secondary mutation, a brief private ritual conducted in front of a mirror once a day — usually after grooming. He looks at himself for what observation suggests is ten to thirty seconds, says nothing, then leaves. An analyst would read this as the daily renegotiation of self-image. He would not describe it as a ritual if asked.
- **Pre-mission dressing.** Before field operations he dresses with unusual deliberation, taking longer than the gear requires. He treats it as a costuming ritual; the persona has to be put on along with the kit.
- **Post-mission scrubbing.** After violent missions he showers immediately and at length, regardless of physical need. He does not discuss this. The pattern is unmistakable across eras.
- **The opera night.** Once or twice a month, regardless of obligation, he goes to live music. Opera preferred; chamber and jazz acceptable. He goes alone as often as in company. He weeps audibly at certain passages of Verdi and does not apologize for it.

---

## 6.7 Downtime, Such As It Is

Downtime is *aversive* and is therefore *engineered*. He treats leisure as another protocol. Reading is leisure when the book is not professional; chess is leisure (he plays at roughly master strength and prefers correspondence games that he can interleave with work); cooking is leisure; long walks are leisure; conversation with one trusted person over good wine is leisure. He does not have leisure that involves *doing nothing*. He has never been observed to sit on a couch and watch television passively; if the television is on, he is either grading or repairing something.

Hobbies in the strict sense: trapeze and aerial silks (privately, on rigging he has built in whichever residence accommodates it — he is genuinely accomplished and finds it meditative); ham radio in earlier eras; he has tinkered with synthesizers and once built one from parts; he restores antique scientific instruments (microscopes especially) and keeps a small collection.

Vacation in any normative sense is absent from the record. He has been off-world, off-planet, off-dimension; he has not been to a beach for a week without a reason.

---

## 6.8 Social Cadence

A typical week's social log would show: daily contact with two to four close intimates (Bobby Drake invariably; Wonder Man in eras permitting; Jean when alive; in later eras, Abigail Brand, Kitty Pryde at times, and a small circle of fellow scientists); professional contact with twenty to forty more; surface-level pleasant contact with everyone the residence contains. He greets by name. He remembers details — a student's sick parent, a colleague's child's age. The memory is genuine; the deployment is also strategic. He has learned that being *the one who remembers* buys social capital cheaply.

Romantic and sexual life is private, mostly monogamous when active, and recedes in periods of moral stress. A surveillance week during a low-romantic phase would record no relevant activity; during an active phase, evenings would shift, the cooking would multiply, the calls home would drop.

---

## 6.9 Drift Indicators (Late-Period Deviation)

The same week, surveilled during the Krakoan spymaster period or the lead-up to the time-travel decision, would show specific and diagnostic deviations from the above:

- Sleep drops below four hours and stays there for weeks.
- The Sunday letter stops.
- The opera nights stop.
- The phone calls to Bobby Drake become shorter and less frequent.
- The mirror minute extends.
- The post-mission shower extends — sometimes to forty minutes.
- The notebook turn becomes irregular; pages are left open overnight, then for days.
- The pacing track in front of the bench deepens.
- The Latin tags accelerate to one every three or four minutes in conversation; the lexical density of his sentences spikes.
- He begins to take meetings standing, in doorways, with the body angled to leave.
- He stops cooking on Sundays.
- He answers fewer questions and asks fewer.
- The third-person clinical self-reference, normally reserved for medical contexts, leaks into ordinary conversation.

Every one of these is a measurable, observable, sequencable signal. Read as a panel, they constitute an early-warning system. *The deviations from his routine are the most reliable indicator of his moral state that exists.* A competent surveillance package, given a baseline week and any deviating week, could predict with high confidence the magnitude and direction of his next unilateral act — and could, in principle, have predicted every late-period catastrophe in this file from the rhythm of his housekeeping alone.


## Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

# UATU DOSSIER — HANK McCOY ("BEAST")
## Section 6. Relationships I — Family & Origin Bonds

*This section maps the small set of people whose connection to the subject predates the X-Men, predates the fur, predates the public self. These are the witnesses to the unguarded child. They are also, by extension, the people whose absence or distance most precisely calibrates the defensive architecture that subsequently formed. Where canon is sparse, behavioral inference is flagged.*

---

### 6.1 NORTON McCOY — Father

**Biographical baseline.** Norton McCoy, of Dunfee, Illinois: working-class, technically trained, employed for the bulk of his adult life at a nuclear power facility (variously identified as a plant in the greater Dunfee region). Sustained, in canon, a workplace radiation exposure prior to Hank's conception — the etiologic vector for Hank's congenital mutation. This is the single most loaded fact in the father-son record: *Norton is the proximal biological cause of the body that has defined his son's entire existence.* Whatever the man did or did not do as a parent has been read, by both of them, through that lens.

**Early dynamic (Dunfee years, infancy through high school).** The record is consistent that Norton and Edna were *loving, present, and protective* of a visibly mutated child in a small Midwestern town in the late 1940s / 1950s. This is not a trivial baseline; it is the foundation of Hank's earned-secure attachment and the reason he is not a more damaged man. Norton appears in flashback and in his on-page visits to the X-Mansion as a quiet, blue-collar, fundamentally decent presence — a man who did not flinch at the oversized hands and feet, who let his son play football, who accepted the academic precocity without resentment, and who later accepted the blue fur with a working-man's stoicism that reads, in the granular detail, as *active love disguised as composure*.

**The conversation that was never quite had.** Inference from behavior: Norton, who knows he is the radiation vector, almost certainly carries a guilt he has never said aloud. Hank, who knows that Norton knows, has almost certainly never let him say it. There is in the McCoy family a tacit non-aggression pact around etiology: *we do not name the cause because to name it is to allow blame.* This pact is the template for Hank's lifelong handling of pain — *intellectualize the mechanism, never indict the actor.* When Hank in adulthood discusses his own mutation with strangers in florid clinical syntax, he is doing what the family room in Dunfee modeled.

**Adult dynamic.** Norton continues to surface across the canon as the man Hank visits when something has cracked. The visits are short, undemonstrative, characterized in narration by gardening, fixing things, sitting on porches. Hank's diction drops two registers in Dunfee — fewer Latin tags, fewer arch inversions, more direct sentences. This is one of the very few documented contexts in which the verbal scaffolding comes down. It is also one of the very few contexts in which Hank is observed to *eat slowly*.

**Trust / safety.** Maximum, with a specific carve-out. Hank trusts Norton absolutely with his physical self (Norton has seen every iteration of the body and not flinched), absolutely with his history, and absolutely with his presence. He does *not* take counsel from Norton on the work. The asymmetry is generational and intellectual: Hank cannot bring the Endangered Species moral problem, or the Krakoa intelligence problem, to a man who left school after the eleventh grade. So the deepest layer of trust runs in a domain Hank no longer inhabits, and the layer he most needs counseled — the moral-engineering layer — is precisely where Norton cannot reach him. This is a structural tragedy of the relationship.

**Failure mode.** Norton has, in canon, briefly turned. During the X-Factor era his anti-mutant sentiment surfaces under social pressure in Dunfee; he is, for a stretch, ashamed of his son in public while loving him in private. The episode is patched. But it left a hairline crack — *evidence that even Norton is conditional under sufficient social heat* — and after that point Hank's visits home are slightly fewer and slightly briefer. He never confronts the lapse. He absorbs it into the ledger and shifts.

**Leverage.** Norton is the single most efficient pressure point on Hank that exists outside the immediate X-Men circle, and it is the one no enemy in the record has correctly identified and pressed. Threats to Norton are *underexploited* in the canon, which is favorable to the subject but should not be assumed by an actor planning around him. A credible threat to either parent would collapse Hank's late-period spymaster composure inside a single conversation. He has not been tested there. *He is not robust against being tested there.*

---

### 6.2 EDNA McCOY — Mother

**Biographical baseline.** Edna McCoy, née usually rendered as a Dunfee local, homemaker, in some renderings a part-time worker. The on-page footprint is smaller than Norton's, which is itself diagnostic — Hank's emotional vocabulary tracks closer to the paternal register, and Edna sits in the record as the *atmosphere* of the childhood home rather than as a discrete interlocutor.

**Early dynamic.** Edna was the parent who handled the daily mechanics of raising a visibly mutated child in a hostile small town: the school confrontations, the doctors, the church congregations, the neighbors. The labor of *managing the public* on behalf of the child fell, in mid-twentieth-century Illinois, to the mother by default. Hank's lifelong reflex of *staging himself for the public* — the witticism deployed before the stranger can stare, the diction calibrated to outrun the gawk — is, in its structural origin, a maternal inheritance. Edna taught him that the social field is to be *managed actively*, that one does not wait to be perceived but rather sets the terms of perception. He has been doing this in every room he has entered for sixty years.

**Adult dynamic.** Visits with Edna are characterized in the record by feeding and tactile contact — she cooks for him in volumes that even his metabolism notices, and she touches his face and hands without the brief hesitation that almost every other adult in his life shows. The latter is the most important data point in the entire mother-son file. Edna is one of perhaps four or five people on Earth who *touch Hank's altered body without micro-hesitation*. The somatic data on him registers this: heart rate, observed posture, observed shoulder line all drop in her presence in ways that do not occur even with closest teammates.

**Trust / safety.** Total and undifferentiated. Hank does not vet Edna; he does not manage her; he does not perform for her. She is one of the very few non-performance zones in his life. He also does not bring her his moral problems — for the same reason he does not bring them to Norton, plus the additional protective filter that he does not want her to know what he has become capable of.

**Failure mode.** Edna's health and aging are, in the deep background of the record, a quietly metastasizing problem he does not address. The intellectualizing defense is not deployable against the slow loss of a parent to time; one cannot Latin-tag one's way around it. Inference: Hank's avoidance of Dunfee correlates loosely with periods of her observed decline, which is the opposite of what a healthier subject would do. He cannot tolerate watching her diminish because the *non-performance zone* is one of his last structural supports, and he is unconsciously protecting the support by not visiting it when it is fragile. This is regression-grade behavior in an otherwise high-functioning man.

**Leverage.** As with Norton, underexploited and catastrophic if pressed. Additionally — and this is the precise refinement — *Edna's distress*, more than her endangerment, is the lever. Hank can game out a hostage scenario. He cannot game out his mother crying.

---

### 6.3 SIBLINGS — Absence and Its Meaning

The canon does not establish blood siblings for Henry McCoy. He is, on the available record, an only child. This is *significant load-bearing data*, not absence-of-data.

**Implication 1: only-child intensification of parental focus.** Norton and Edna's protective energy concentrated on a single mutated child, which improved attachment quality and worsened isolation. There was no normatively-bodied sibling against whom Hank could measure himself, and equally no sibling who shared the social burden of being *the McCoys' strange boy*. He carried the visibility alone.

**Implication 2: the X-Men as fabricated sibship.** Hank's lifelong over-investment in the *original five* — Scott, Jean, Bobby, Warren — is, in part, the construction of a sibling cohort he did not have. The intensity of his bond to Bobby Drake (see Relationships II) is not friendship-grade; it is *sibling-grade*, with the granular markers of childhood-coded teasing, shared shorthand, and a tolerance for irritation that he extends to no friend. The original-five reunions across his life are recurrently described in the record with the affective tone of *family reunions*, not team meetings.

**Implication 3: the time-displaced teenage originals as the most pathological possible expression.** When Hank, in *All-New X-Men*, pulled the teenage versions of his cohort forward in time, the surface justification was moral instruction of present-day Scott. The deeper structural read is that *he reached back and retrieved his constructed sibship in the form it most consoled him*. The time-displaced five are, on this reading, the only-child's terminal solution to never having had siblings: when the adult versions disappointed or died or distanced, he fetched the children. This recasts the time-travel decision as not merely a moral-engineering failure but a *regression to the deepest unmet need in the file*. It is the most diagnostically loaded act of his life precisely because the only-child substrate has never been considered as its driver.

---

### 6.4 CHILDREN — None, and the Shape of the Absence

Hank has no biological children in canon. He has, repeatedly and across decades, *acted in loco parentis*: students at the Jean Grey School in volume, individual mentees (notably during the Krakoan and post-Krakoan periods), and — by retrieval — the teenage time-displaced originals, on whom he projected a paternal frame they did not request and largely resented.

**Why the absence is meaningful.** Hank is a man with the temperament, financial means, partner history, and stated affection for children sufficient to be a father. The record's silence is therefore active, not passive. Three convergent reasons:

1. **The genetic transmission problem.** He knows, mechanistically and in granular molecular detail, what his own mutation cost him and his parents. He is a geneticist; he has read his own karyotype. He does not want to author what his father unwittingly authored. This is a moral position he has never stated publicly because stating it would force him to assign retrospective blame to Norton, which the family non-aggression pact forbids.

2. **The body as disqualifier in his own self-image.** Late-period Hank does not believe his body is *for* the intimacy required to produce and rear a child. The Trish Tilby breakup confirmed for him a thesis he had been testing since adolescence: that the fur is a ceiling on the depth of partnership available to him. He has not contested this ruling.

3. **The work-as-progeny substitution.** Sublimation, his core defense, has consumed the parental drive. The Endangered Species arc reads, in this frame, as the displaced reproductive instinct of a man trying to *re-fertilize an entire species* because he will not father a single child. The scale of the substitution is the measure of the depth of the underlying drive. This is one of the cleanest sublimation profiles in the entire X-Men record.

**Behavioral correlate.** Hank is unusually gentle with the very young — observed in the record with infant teammates, with Krakoan children, with the Jean Grey School's youngest. The gentleness has a specific signature: he kneels rather than crouches, he keeps his hands open and visible, he speaks at half his usual register and a third his usual lexical density. He is *managing the body* on their behalf — performing safety, because he has been on the other side of the equation. With adolescents (Jean Grey School age range) he is excellent — the polymathic chatter lands well there, and the slight ridiculousness of his erudition reads to teenagers as endearing rather than as deflection. With young adults he is at his weakest as a mentor, because by that age his protégés begin to notice the rationalization engine, and the relationship asymmetry becomes uncomfortable for both parties.

---

### 6.5 DARK BEAST (HENRY McCOY of the Age of Apocalypse) — The Counterfactual Self

Although not literal kin, the Age of Apocalypse Hank McCoy is the closest thing in the record to a *sibling*, and structurally is the most important origin-tier relationship after the parents. He is *what Hank would have been* had the early conditions diverged: same baseline genome, same intellect, same drive — minus Xavier, minus Norton's love, minus the original five. The result is an unconstrained vivisectionist, morally inverted, who shares Hank's exact cognitive style.

**Function in Hank's psyche.** Dark Beast is *the externalized worst case* — the proof that the rationalization engine, without the ethical scaffolding, produces a monster. Every encounter between them is, for Hank, a confrontation with a mirror that has been allowed to argue. The encounters are characterized in the record by an unusual phenomenon: *Hank loses verbal control around him.* The diction tightens, the witticisms thin, the Latin tags vanish. This is the only adversary in the canon who consistently produces this effect. Dark Beast knows Hank's defensive architecture from the inside, which is to say he cannot be lied to in the standard repertoire.

**Diagnostic significance.** During the Endangered Species arc, Hank consults Dark Beast — *because he is the only geneticist of equal capability who will help*. This is the moment in the record where the boundary between Hank and his counterfactual self begins to thin in a way that becomes operationally lethal by the Krakoan years. The late-period Hank who runs intelligence and orchestrates assassinations is the Hank who has gradually, project by project, *imported portions of Dark Beast's permission structure into his own*. The replacement Hank at the end of the Krakoan arc — the earlier-resurrection moral version — can be read as the explicit in-universe acknowledgment that the contamination was real and had to be excised. His own friends did the surgery he could not.

**Trust / safety.** Zero in either direction; an asymmetric mutual contempt. But the contempt is *uncomfortably intimate*, because the family resemblance is total.

**Leverage.** Dark Beast is the only entity in canon who can predict Hank's next decision with the accuracy with which Hank predicts a chemical reaction. If still extant, he is an intelligence asset of nearly unmatched value against the subject — and a temptation Hank himself cannot reliably refuse to consult.

---

### 6.6 THE DEAD — Origin-Tier Losses

Two losses sit in the origin tier rather than the peer tier because they shaped him before his defenses had fully matured to accommodate loss.

**Charles Xavier (paternal mentor, killed by Cyclops, *Avengers vs. X-Men*).** Xavier is Hank's *intellectual father* and the model for benevolent unilateralism that Hank internalized in adolescence and exceeded in old age. The death is the proximal moral injury that, more than any other single event, drives the *All-New X-Men* time-travel decision: Hank's stated rationale is shaming present-day Scott over Xavier's death, and the affective intensity of the decision is unintelligible without recognizing it as filial vengeance dressed in pedagogical clothing. He has never fully processed the loss; the intellectualizing defense reliably fails him on Xavier in a way it does not fail him on most other griefs. He talks *around* Xavier, not *about* him.

**Jean Grey (multiple deaths, multiple returns).** Jean operates in Hank's life as *constructed-sister-prime*. Her deaths punctuate his record and correlate, each time, with a downshift in his diction and an uptick in his lab hours for the following months. He has loved her without ever being in love with her, and the love is the cleanest, least defended affection in the file — possibly because she alone among the original five could *read his diction in real time* and refuse to be deflected by it. When she died, the most effective external check on his intellectualization engine died with her. The slide into late-period unilateralism begins, on close timeline, in the long Jean-absent stretches.

---

### 6.7 SUMMARY MATRIX — Origin-Tier Leverage and Risk

- **Highest emotional access:** Edna (non-performance zone).
- **Highest moral access:** Norton (pre-fur witness).
- **Highest structural risk:** the absent siblings — because the substitutes (original five, time-displaced teens) carry psychological load they were never designed to bear, and his most destructive recent decision was driven by that overload.
- **Highest counterintelligence risk:** Dark Beast — the only mind that fully maps his.
- **Highest unresolved grief:** Xavier — the wound that, when poked, produces unilateral action rather than tears.
- **Highest sublimation substrate:** the unborn children — converted into species-scale projects whose failure he cannot survive without further moral compromise.

The origin tier is, in net, *the part of Hank McCoy's relational world that has aged best and held him together longest*. It is also the part that, with sufficient pressure on its weakest joints (Norton's conditional moments, Edna's mortality, the sibling-substitute overload, the Xavier wound, the Dark Beast mirror), would unmake him faster than any external assault on the man he has built on top of it. The dossier's later sections — peer bonds, romantic history, professional alliances — must be read against this floor. *Everything Hank is, defensively, was poured over the shape of these few people. Pull any of them, and the shape deforms.*


## Relationships II — Allies, Chosen Family & Mentors

# RELATIONSHIPS II — ALLIES, CHOSEN FAMILY & MENTORS

*Section 6b of the McCoy dossier. Read in conjunction with Section 6a (Origin Family & Romantic) and Section 6c (Adversaries & Frenemies). Each entry maps: shared history; operational dynamic; evolution across eras; the specific texture of trust and safety; the predictable failure mode of the bond; and what leverage the relationship offers a hostile or benevolent actor seeking to move the subject.*

---

## 6b.1 Robert Louis Drake ("Bobby" / Iceman)

**The keystone bond.** If the file contains a single relationship without which Hank McCoy is not legible, it is this one. They meet at Xavier's as the two youngest original recruits, are paired by mass and temperament as the "kid brothers" of the founding five, and remain in continuous contact across every era of the record — Avengers years included, when Hank is geographically distant and Bobby is the friend he flies back to New York to see.

**Dynamic.** Hank-as-erudite-older-sibling / Bobby-as-arrested-younger-sibling, a polarity that has barely shifted in sixty years of canon. Hank performs vocabulary; Bobby punctures it. Hank produces a Latin tag; Bobby translates it into a joke about Hank's feet. This is not noise — it is the *single regulatory mechanism in McCoy's life that has consistently worked*. Bobby is allowed, structurally, to call Hank ridiculous, and Hank can hear it from Bobby when he can hear it from no one else. The Drake voice is the one that gets through the intellectualization airlock.

**Evolution.** Stan Lee era: physical-comedy duo, dorm-room horseplay, the team's two clowns. Claremont era: drift, Hank to Avengers, Bobby to Defenders / Champions, but reunion in *X-Factor* (1986) is treated by both as picking up mid-sentence. 90s/2000s: Bobby becomes Hank's most reliable confidant during the secondary-mutation grief and the Trish breakup; the lab-bench-and-beer-bottle scenes recur. Bendis era: rupture. Bobby is among the loudest voices telling Hank not to bring the original five forward, and Hank does it anyway. Bobby's later coming-out, midwifed onto the page by his own time-displaced teen self, occurs in a narrative space Hank engineered — and Hank's response (supportive but oddly tangential, the conversation he should have had with his oldest friend largely deflected to others) is its own piece of evidence about how much late-period Hank had withdrawn into project-mode.

**Trust / safety.** Highest in the file outside of Jean. Bobby is one of perhaps three people in front of whom Hank will sit silently. The shorthand is total — physical (the side-hugs, the knuckle to the shoulder), verbal (callbacks to in-jokes from 1965), and somatic (Bobby reads Hank's tail position the way other people read facial expression).

**Failure mode.** Hank's late-period habit is to *protect Bobby from his decisions* — to make the call and inform him afterwards, the way an older brother handles a problem rather than burdening the younger one. This is read by Bobby (correctly) as condescension and disloyalty. The bond does not break; it sours, becomes wary, and Bobby's grief at the Krakoan-era Hank's conduct is the grief of a man watching a sibling become unrecognizable.

**Leverage.** Anyone seeking to move Hank can route through Bobby with high reliability *until* Hank has committed to a course; after commitment, the channel inverts and Hank begins to *manage* Bobby. A benevolent intervention would weaponize this — get Bobby in the room *before* the decision is locked.

---

## 6b.2 Jean Grey

**The witness.** Jean is, alongside Bobby, the second irreplaceable person from the original cohort. The dynamic is different in kind: where Bobby gets to puncture, Jean gets to *see*. Telepathy is the proximate mechanism but not the deep one — Jean would have read Hank without it. She is the team member who from the earliest issues addresses the McCoy beneath the McCoy performance, asks the question the verbiage was designed to deflect, and is allowed to.

**Dynamic.** Sibling-coded, asexual, mutually protective. There is no romantic charge in the record — uncommon for a male character around Jean Grey — and the absence is itself diagnostic. Hank's libidinal life routes through women who *do not* read him telepathically (Vera, Trish, Brand); the woman who *can* read him is held in a category where being seen does not become being judged.

**Evolution.** Original team: she is his lab partner and confidante. Phoenix era: he loses her, and the record shows him in one of his rare unverbal collapses — the Avengers-era Hank, fluent in everything, has nothing to say. X-Factor: her return is the proximate emotional motor that brings him back to the mutant project full-time. Resurrection-era Krakoa: their reunions are warm but compromised by what she increasingly senses he has become; the late-period Jean's telepathic glances at Hank are some of the most damning visual evidence in the file.

**Trust / safety.** Total, with one caveat: Hank shields his moral reasoning *from* Jean specifically. He does not want her to read it, because he knows what she would find. By the Krakoan era he has become deliberately, almost professionally, mentally guarded around her. This is data.

**Failure mode.** Avoidance. Hank does not betray Jean; he absents himself from her field of view at exactly the moments he most needs her oversight.

**Leverage.** Place Jean opposite him in a small room with no audience. The performance apparatus does not function in front of her. Hank will either say the true thing or visibly choose silence; either outcome is informationally rich.

---

## 6b.3 Warren Worthington III (Angel / Archangel)

**The other founding aristocrat.** Hank and Warren share, uniquely among the originals, an *upper-register social fluency* — Warren by birth, Hank by acquired performance — and they are the two who could most easily move in the Manhattan philanthropic-scientific world. This makes them natural pair in the Avengers/Defenders/X-Factor party-circuit period.

**Dynamic.** Cordial, slightly competitive, mutually respectful. Hank treats Warren as an equal *socially* and as a junior *intellectually*, a calibration Warren accepts with good humor for decades. Warren funds; Hank builds. When Warren is mutilated by the Marauders and rebuilt as Archangel, Hank is among the small circle who do the long emotional work of recovering him, and the favor is repaid in Warren's funding of every McCoy laboratory from the X-Factor headquarters to the Jean Grey School science wing.

**Evolution.** The relationship is least demonstrative and most reliable. They do not call frequently; they show up unhesitatingly. Late period, Warren — through his various incarnations — drifts farther from Hank's orbit, and Hank's failure to track this drift is consistent with his late-period pattern of letting peripheral-feeling friendships run on legacy autopilot while he attends to whichever crisis he has personally adopted.

**Trust / safety.** High in the gentleman's-agreement register — money, alibi, safe house, no questions — lower in the confessional register. Hank does not unload on Warren; Warren does not invite it.

**Failure mode.** Inattention. Hank assumes Warren is fine because Warren has always been fine, and misses the increments. The record contains several scenes in which Warren's distress is visible to other teammates and not to Hank.

**Leverage.** Limited as emotional lever; substantial as resource lever — Worthington Industries is canonically Hank's logistical backbone.

---

## 6b.4 Scott Summers (Cyclops)

*Mapped here because the relationship begins as fraternal and only later becomes adversarial; the adversarial phase is in 6c.*

**Dynamic, early.** Scott as the responsible older-coded sibling, Hank as the brilliant peer-deputy. For three decades Hank functions as Scott's most trusted counsel — the intellect Cyclops consults when the tactical answer is not the right answer, the moral pressure-test for command decisions. Scott trusts Hank, in the Claremont and Morrison eras, the way a captain trusts a ship's surgeon: completely and within domain.

**Evolution.** The fracture is not a single moment; it is *House of M*, then Decimation, then the messianic age, then Utopia, then Schism. Hank disagrees with Scott progressively: about the X-Men becoming a paramilitary, about the Extinction Team, about the children on Utopia. Each disagreement is initially in good faith and within bounds. Then Phoenix Five happens; then Scott kills Xavier; then Hank decides — alone — that the man he has known for forty years is irretrievable. The time-travel decision is, in part, addressed to Scott: Hank importing teenage Scott to *force present-Scott to look at what he was*. This is one of the cruelest acts in McCoy's record and he commits it under the banner of friendship.

**Trust / safety.** Was the deepest male professional bond in his life outside of Bobby. Becomes, by late period, the relationship through which Hank most clearly demonstrates his rationalization pathology — because his treatment of Scott cannot be defended on the merits and he defends it anyway.

**Failure mode.** Mutual: Scott's by hardening into messianism; Hank's by responding with covert unilateralism rather than honest confrontation. Neither will simply *say* to the other what is true.

**Leverage.** Anything that forces Hank to articulate, in front of witnesses he respects, *what specifically Scott did that justifies what Hank did*, will expose the rationalization. He has never been made to do it cleanly.

---

## 6b.5 Ororo Munroe (Storm)

**The peer-conscience.** Storm joins post-original-five but becomes, by the Claremont era, one of Hank's most respected colleagues. The dynamic is *mutually formal* in a way most of his friendships are not — they address each other with a slight ceremonial weight, as two people who recognize in the other a person who carries the team's moral weather.

**Dynamic.** Hank defers to Ororo on questions of *leadership ethics*; Ororo defers to Hank on questions of *technical ethics*. The deference is genuine and reciprocal. He is one of the few teammates Storm will permit to disagree with her openly in command settings.

**Evolution.** Stable for decades. Cracks in the Krakoan era when Storm, as a member of the Quiet Council, becomes aware of X-Force's wet operations and Hank's role in them. Her disappointment in him is not loud; it is the quiet kind that recalibrates a thirty-year relationship downward by a permanent quantum.

**Trust / safety.** High and bounded. He will tell her what he is doing; he will not tell her *all* of what he is doing.

**Failure mode.** Hank cannot bear Storm's disapproval and so manages information flow to avoid earning it. The management is the betrayal.

**Leverage.** Storm in a council chair, asking the direct question, in front of others, is one of the few conditions under which Hank will tell substantial truth.

---

## 6b.6 Simon Williams (Wonder Man)

**The Avengers-era best friend.** This is the single relationship that most clearly demonstrates Hank's capacity for adult male intimacy outside the X-orbit. They meet during his Avengers tenure, click immediately on the basis of shared physicality-with-self-doubt (Simon's ionic body / Hank's furred body; both men carry low-grade dysmorphia under bravado), and become, in 70s and 80s canon, one of Marvel's most quoted male friendships — the gym partners, the cocktail-party wingmen, the men who finish each other's sentences in a tone of mutual amusement.

**Dynamic.** Lateral and easy. With Simon, Hank does not perform; he plays. The vocabulary lightens, the references narrow to the ones Simon will actually catch, the body relaxes. This is the only adult friendship in the file where Hank is observed to be *bored together* with someone — sitting through a bad movie, complaining companionably.

**Evolution.** Diminishes as Hank returns to X-orbit in the late 80s. Reactivates whenever they are on-page together. Survives Simon's deaths and resurrections; survives Hank's Krakoan slide largely because Simon is offstage during the worst of it. Functionally dormant in late period but not damaged.

**Trust / safety.** High in the *recreational* register; never tested in the *operational* register because they have rarely worked together under high stakes. The absence of stress-test is itself protective — the friendship has not been given the chance to break.

**Failure mode.** Atrophy by distance. Hank does not maintain it actively; he relies on it being there when he returns.

**Leverage.** Low in any current operation — Simon is too far from Hank's current life to move him.

---

## 6b.7 Charles Xavier

**The mentor.** Xavier recruits him as a teenager, gives him the architecture of a life (school, team, mission), and — critically — models for Hank the *exact* defensive posture that will eventually destroy him: benevolent unilateralism, the conviction that one's superior understanding licenses action without consent. Hank absorbs this not as doctrine but as *aesthetic*, the way a son absorbs a father's posture.

**Dynamic.** Reverent through the original-team era; collegial through the Claremont era as Hank becomes a peer scientist Xavier consults; increasingly critical in the 2000s as Hank reads the Danger Room revelation, the Deadly Genesis revelation, and the long history of Xavier's psychic interventions. By the end of Xavier's first life, Hank knows the man's ledger and judges it. The Schism / post-Schism period is where Hank fully reckons with how much of his own moral architecture he inherited from a flawed teacher.

**Evolution.** A slow demystification across forty years. The painful irony, dossier-relevant: the *more* Hank judged Xavier's unilateralism, the *more* he replicated it. Hank's late-period grandiosity is Xavier's, scaled down in resources and scaled up in self-righteousness.

**Trust / safety.** Operationally high, confessionally low. Hank did not confide in Xavier; he reported to him.

**Failure mode.** Identification with the aggressor's *method* while rejecting the aggressor's *person*. Hank never noticed that he became the thing he criticized.

**Leverage.** Naming the pattern out loud — *you are doing what Charles did, by the means Charles used, for the reasons Charles gave* — is the single intervention most likely to produce a visible flinch. It has been deployed in canon (variously by Storm, by Logan) and registers as a wound he cannot rebut.

---

## 6b.8 James Howlett (Wolverine / Logan)

**The unlikely ally.** On paper they should not work — Hank the polysyllabic moralist, Logan the laconic killer. In practice they form, from the Claremont era onward, one of the most stable cross-temperament partnerships in the X-roster. The bond is built on *mutual recognition of competence in an opposite mode* and on shared fondness for the same set of people (Jean, Kurt, Kitty).

**Dynamic.** Hank fixes what Logan breaks; Logan does what Hank cannot do himself. The exchange is honest, unsentimental, and gratifying to both. Logan reads Hank with a directness no one else permits themselves — he has, in canon, told Hank he is talking too much, drinking too much, working too long, and Hank has accepted it from Logan when he would not from a peer.

**Evolution.** Deepens in the Jean Grey School era, where Hank chooses Logan over Scott in Schism. The two of them co-found the institution and run it as something close to a marriage of convenience that has become a genuine partnership. Cracks during the Krakoan era — Logan, as Solem of X-Force, sees Hank's spymaster operations up close and is among the architects of his eventual removal. The friendship does not so much *break* as conclude that the man they are dealing with is no longer the man they were friends with — and the replacement-Hank inherits the friendship intact, which is its own kind of verdict.

**Trust / safety.** Operationally total; emotionally bounded but real. Hank will tell Logan what he is going to do, even when he will not tell anyone else, because he trusts Logan to make a decision and live with it.

**Failure mode.** Hank uses Logan's *operational tolerance* as ethical cover. "Logan didn't object" becomes, in Hank's internal accounting, equivalent to *Logan approved*, which it is not. Logan permits much because Logan has done worse; this is not endorsement.

**Leverage.** Logan calling a halt — physically — is one of the few things that will stop Hank mid-course. It is also, in the record, what eventually happens.

---

## 6b.9 Kurt Wagner (Nightcrawler)

**The theological friendship.** Kurt is Hank's nearest peer on the team in two specific registers: *visible mutation that does not pass* and *love of language and culture as compensatory practice*. They are both blue, both verbally elegant, both formed by the experience of being stared at in childhood. The bond is therefore *constitutional* rather than circumstantial.

**Dynamic.** They speak to each other in a register no one else on the team accesses — multilingual, allusive, often gently religious on Kurt's side and gently secular on Hank's, the two of them debating in the kitchen of whichever mansion is currently extant. Kurt is one of perhaps two people who can name Hank's vanity affectionately and have it land as affection.

**Evolution.** Steady. Kurt's deaths and resurrections grieve Hank disproportionately. In the post-Krakoan era, Kurt's theological project (the Spark, the Lights) is one of the few mutant initiatives Hank engages with non-instrumentally, which is data — by then, his engagement with anything is usually instrumental.

**Trust / safety.** High, with a specific carve-out: Kurt is the friend who will ask Hank about the *soul*, and Hank deflects. The deflection is mutual and understood.

**Failure mode.** Hank treats Kurt's moral seriousness as charming rather than as *the actual rebuke it sometimes is*. He aestheticizes Kurt's ethics rather than absorbing them.

**Leverage.** Kurt is one of the few people whose disappointment Hank cannot quite intellectualize away. The cost of being judged by another visibly-mutated, language-loving believer is high.

---

## 6b.10 Katherine Pryde (Kitty / Kate)

**The protégée-who-became-peer.** Kitty arrives as a thirteen-year-old, and Hank — who at that point has been the team's only mind of her calibre — becomes one of her early science mentors. He teaches her in the lab; she debugs his code; the relationship establishes the template for what later becomes his teaching practice at the Jean Grey School.

**Dynamic.** Avuncular shading into peer as she ages. By the 2000s she addresses him as an equal and he treats her as one. She is, after Bobby, the second-most-reliable puncturer of his rhetoric — sharper than Bobby, less affectionate, more surgical.

**Evolution.** Strong through her early adulthood. Strained during the Krakoan era when, as Captain of the Marauders and later as Red Queen, she is operationally adjacent to Hank's X-Force and sees enough of it to disapprove. She does not confront him; she simply *moves away from him* in the social topography of Krakoa, which Hank registers and minimizes.

**Trust / safety.** Once total in the technical register, declining in the operational. Kitty stopped bringing him problems she did not want him to *solve in his way*.

**Failure mode.** Hank loses her by being unable to hear what her distance is saying.

**Leverage.** Kitty in a room with documentation of his actions is a high-yield interrogation configuration; she will not bluff and he cannot charm her.

---

## 6b.11 Abigail Brand

*Cross-listed with Section 6a (Romantic).* Mapped here also because the *partnership* register precedes and exceeds the romantic.

**Dynamic.** Brand is the only person in the file who out-classifies him — S.W.O.R.D., extraterrestrial intelligence, an operational world Hank cannot fully access without her. The relationship begins as scientific liaison, becomes flirtatious peer-banter, deepens into intermittent romance, and across all phases retains a *workplace* core: they are colleagues who happen also to be involved.

**Evolution.** Activates around *Astonishing X-Men*. Bends through several arcs in which Brand is variously suspected of double-dealing and Hank variously suspects her, with each round of suspicion clearing into deeper professional respect. Krakoan-era Brand is hostile-adjacent (her own agenda, her own concealed allegiances), and Hank, characteristically, does not entirely update.

**Trust / safety.** Operationally exceptional in domain; emotionally bounded; epistemically high because Brand will tell him he is wrong and mean it. She is one of the few people whose disagreement he treats as data rather than as obstacle.

**Failure mode.** Hank romanticizes her competence to the point of underweighting her agency — he assumes shared ends because they share methods, which is not true and which she has exploited.

**Leverage.** Brand can move Hank in ways no one else can because she is *outside the X-frame* — uncontaminated by mutant politics, uncontaminated by Avengers history. He hears her differently.

---

## 6b.12 Reed Richards

**The peer-of-peers, scientific.** One of perhaps three living humans Hank treats as a full intellectual equal (Richards, T'Challa, Pym in his good periods).
