The relationship is collegial across decades — guest lectures at each other's facilities, late-night consultations on problems neither can crack alone, the occasional joint paper implied by canon.

**Dynamic.** Mutually respectful, slightly competitive in the gentlemanly mode, ethically cross-checking. Reed has, in canon, *declined* requests from Hank — most notably during the Endangered Species period when Hank's methods crossed lines Reed would not cross. Hank registered the refusal and proceeded anyway.

**Evolution.** Steady through most of the record; tested by Hank's late-period willingness to consort with Sinister-tier collaborators that Reed would not touch. Reed's distance, by the Krakoan era, is its own quiet judgment.

**Trust / safety.** High in domain, low in operation. They share data; they do not share missions.

**Failure mode.** Hank treats Reed's ethical refusals as a *failure of nerve* rather than as a *signal about his own drift*. This is among the more telling misreadings in the file.

**Leverage.** Reed is the one peer-of-peers whose refusal to participate in a McCoy project should function as a stop signal. In Hank's late period it does not; that is the disease.

---

## 6b.13 T'Challa

**The respected sovereign.** Brief but instructive: T'Challa is a peer Hank cannot patronize, cannot out-credential, and cannot maneuver. The relationship is therefore one of *the rare instances in the file where Hank operates from


## Relationships III — Rivals, Enemies & Lovers

# RELATIONSHIPS III — RIVALS, ENEMIES & LOVERS

*Per UATU protocol: each entry treated as a discrete intelligence sub-file. Dynamics, drift over time, mutual leverage, and the specific failure mode each relationship produces in the subject. Some figures cross categories (rival-and-friend, lover-and-wound, enemy-and-double); they are filed under the dominant valence in McCoy's own affective ledger as inferred from his speech and behavior.*

---

## I. RIVALS

The category "rival" is unstable for this subject because his temperament does not naturally generate adversaries among peers — he is collegial by default and self-deprecating in contest. What the record shows instead are *structural* rivals: figures whose existence forces him to define himself against them, whether or not he would name them as such.

### Charles Francis Xavier — the mentor as ceiling, then as warning

Xavier is filed here, not under family or mentors proper, because the late-period record reveals that the subject's relationship to Xavier was always *competitive at the substrate*, however covered by reverence on the surface. Initial dynamic (1963 onward): adoring student, genuinely awed; recipient of the first adult environment in which his intellect was matched and his body unremarked. The young McCoy's locutionary performance — the polysyllables, the Latin tags — is, in part, *directed at Xavier*: a child showing the only adult in the room who can read the signal that he is worth keeping.

The drift begins after Xavier's repeated ethical compromises become legible to McCoy: the Onslaught suppression, the secret X-Men team in *Deadly Genesis*, the consistent unilateralism with which Xavier ran the dream. Mid-period McCoy expresses disappointment in coded language — wry asides, increasing willingness to disagree in faculty meetings. Late-period McCoy, *post-Xavier's death at Cyclops's hand*, becomes Xavier in caricature: the certainty, the readiness to instrument others, the conviction that the school's survival licenses any means. The subject does not recognize this; the file's verdict is that he *became* the man whose authority he had spent forty years learning to question. **Leverage:** invocations of Xavier's memory move him visibly. **Failure mode:** he reproduces Xavier's worst defaults while believing he is correcting them.

### Tony Stark — the genius who got to be public

A peer-genius relationship with a slow corrosive substrate. During the Avengers years the two are warm — Stark in the alcoholism period, McCoy a kindly co-Avenger, no apparent rivalry. The friction appears later, when McCoy returns to the X-fold and watches Stark *be celebrated* for the kind of polymath public-facing intellect that McCoy, blue and fanged, will never get to perform without an asterisk. The Civil War period sees the rivalry crystallize: McCoy refuses to register, refuses to recognize Stark's authority over a mutant population, and the asides about Stark sharpen — he becomes, in McCoy's private idiom, the man who used a genius to build a cage. **Trust/safety:** functional collaboration possible on bounded scientific problems; zero trust on policy. **Leverage:** appeals to scientific transparency disarm McCoy; assertions of state legitimacy harden him. **Failure mode:** McCoy underestimates the degree to which his own Krakoa-era spycraft mirrored exactly the apparatus he condemned in Stark.

### Reed Richards — the comparator who renders him provincial

The least-discussed but most psychologically diagnostic of the rivalries. Richards is the only living mind that, in the conventional reckoning, *outranks* McCoy across his core domains. They appear together on Illuminati-adjacent panels, scientific summits, and Avengers crossovers. McCoy's behavior in these settings is observable and distinctive: his vocabulary inflates, his asides multiply, he performs the role of *the wittier intellect* because he cannot perform *the deeper* one. Richards, oblivious or charitable, never competes. The asymmetry wounds. **Leverage:** none useful for adversaries — McCoy will not act against Richards. **Failure mode:** the rivalry is purely internal and shows up in McCoy's overcompensation elsewhere; faced with a Richards-coded interlocutor he becomes harder to direct, more verbal, less collaborative.

### Cyclops, Scott Summers — brother, leader, mirror, indictment

The single most consequential dyadic structure in the late file. Origin (1963 onward): adolescent teammates, mild friction (McCoy the chatter, Summers the brooder), genuine fraternal bond beneath. They share the foundational fact of the original five and a long history of mutual rescue.

The fracture is staged across decades. Disagreement over Xavier's methods, disagreement over Utopia, disagreement over the Phoenix. By *Schism* the bond is functionally dead; McCoy sides with Logan and walks. The decision is dressed in ethical reasoning but the affective driver, visible in the panel work, is *betrayal* — Summers killed Xavier, and McCoy will not be governed by a man who did that.

The hinge act of his life — retrieving the time-displaced original five — is *aimed at Summers*. The stated justification is shaming the present-day Cyclops into repentance. This is the cleanest evidence in the file that McCoy's late-period unilateralism is not impersonal moral calculus; it is a sublimated grief-rage at a specific person, dressed as ethics. He destabilizes the entire timestream to *make Scott feel something*. The subject would deny this framing; the file affirms it.

Krakoa-era dynamic: the two function on the same nation while loathing each other. McCoy's espionage apparatus is implicitly turned, in part, against Summers's authority. The eventual execution and replacement of McCoy is, in fictional-political terms, partially Summers's faction rejecting what McCoy became. **Trust:** zero. **Leverage:** Summers can wound him by being right about him in front of others. **Failure mode:** McCoy cannot self-correct in any matter on which Summers has the opposing position, because correction would feel like submission.

### Logan, James Howlett — the chosen alliance that revealed him

Filed here as rival rather than friend because, despite the *Schism*-era alliance, the relationship's deep structure was competitive in a register McCoy never admitted. Logan is, against all surface presentation, the moral instrument McCoy chose when he wanted permission to use harsher tools. The Jean Grey School partnership made McCoy the *brain* of an institution whose *body* was Logan — an arrangement that allowed McCoy to escalate his methods while telling himself Logan's presence kept things honest. When Logan died and returned and died again, McCoy's restraints slipped further; the Krakoan spymaster phase coincides with the structural absence of a partner who could simply say *no* with violence behind it. **Leverage:** Logan's living judgment was the only field-check that worked on him. **Failure mode:** without Logan he loses the only peer whose disapproval he physically respected.

---

## II. ENEMIES

The subject's enemy roster is unusual in one respect: the figures he treats with the most sustained antagonism are not those who have hurt him most — they are *intellectual peers and ethical doubles*. He despises mirrors. He tolerates monsters who do not threaten his self-image.

### Nathaniel Essex, "Mister Sinister" — the geneticist he became to refuse

Sinister is the long enemy: the geneticist McCoy could become if McCoy's ethics dissolved. Across decades the engagement runs hot. Sinister has the mutant data sets McCoy needs (Legacy Virus research, post-M-Day genetic salvage), and McCoy goes back to him repeatedly — *Endangered Species* most consequentially, where he begs the help of every genetic war-criminal alive and Sinister is on the list. The negotiations are diagnostic: McCoy talks faster around Sinister than around anyone else, his Latin spikes, his self-deprecation thins. Sinister sees him clearly — calls him, in essence, a colleague pretending otherwise — and McCoy can produce no rebuttal that does not require him to first leave the room.

The Krakoan resurrection apparatus brings them into formal partnership. The file's reading: McCoy *needed* Sinister there. The presence of a defined villain in the architecture let him tell himself he was the ethical one in the building. **Trust/safety:** none, mutually understood. **Leverage:** Sinister's leverage on McCoy is the unspoken question *what is the actual difference between us?* McCoy has no clean answer. **Failure mode:** he cannot decline Sinister's offered tools when his own goals are blocked, and each acceptance erodes him further.

### Dark Beast, Hank McCoy of the Age of Apocalypse — the literal mirror

The doppelgänger from the Age of Apocalypse: a McCoy raised under Sinister, unembarrassed about it, vivisectionist, sadist. The relationship is intolerable because there is no comfortable distance — Dark Beast is what McCoy would have been minus Norton, Edna, and Xavier. Their encounters across the canon are physically savage in a way unusual for McCoy; he hits the doppelgänger like he is hitting an idea about himself. Beyond the violence: long impersonation arcs, Dark Beast substituted for him for extended periods without the X-Men noticing, which is itself a damning indictment — the team's prime read on McCoy is *cleverness and bestiality in tension*, a profile generic enough that an evil twin can fill it. **Leverage:** the doppelgänger's leverage is mere existence. **Failure mode:** every encounter with Dark Beast confirms the underlying shame and pushes McCoy further into the compensatory architecture that produces the Krakoan version of himself — i.e., closer to the doppelgänger.

### Magneto, Erik Lehnsherr — the elder he could not dismiss

A complicated enmity that converts into ambivalent alliance and back. Early Magneto is straightforward terrorist; McCoy fights him without philosophical difficulty. Middle Magneto, post-redemption arcs, teaches at the school; McCoy works alongside him, watches the man, and absorbs lessons he does not credit aloud — specifically, *the lesson that history justifies harsher methods than the moment seems to warrant*. Late-period Magneto, on Krakoa, becomes a kind of co-authority McCoy quietly resents and tacitly imitates. McCoy never names Magneto as an influence on his Krakoan conduct. The file argues he should be. **Leverage:** Magneto can speak the mutant-survival framing in a key McCoy cannot refute. **Failure mode:** McCoy adopts Magnetian operational logic while believing himself its critic.

### Norman Osborn — the contemptible enemy

The clean case: a man McCoy can despise without ambivalence, which is, by his own internal accounting, *restful*. Their direct engagements (the Dark Reign era, the Dark X-Men hijack) feature some of McCoy's most uncomplicated combat behavior — he attacks Osborn's apparatus with relish, mocks the Iron Patriot performance, and is in his own register *happy*. The file notes this is suspicious. McCoy is most himself when faced with an enemy whose intellectual and moral inferiority is unambiguous, because such enemies confirm the hierarchy that justifies his autonomy. **Leverage:** none Osborn ever found. **Failure mode:** Osborn is a comfort, not a threat, and time spent fighting him does not teach McCoy anything he needs to learn.

### Trask, the Sentinel program, and the institutional enemy — the abstract opponent he fights best

Across the canon McCoy is at his most operationally pure when the enemy is an *institution* (Sentinels, Friends of Humanity, the Mutant Registration Act apparatus, Weapon Plus). These engagements do not require him to manage ambivalence; they let him deploy intellect at scale in unambiguously defensive cause. The file reads this as the genuine spine of his moral life — when the cause is mutant survival against state machinery, McCoy is, simply, good. The damage occurs when he attempts to import this *clarity of cause* into ambiguous situations (Krakoa intelligence operations) where the institutional enemy is partly himself. **Leverage:** anti-mutant atrocity activates him immediately and overrides ordinary deliberation. **Failure mode:** he generalizes the existential-threat frame into contexts where it does not apply, licensing measures that would be unconscionable absent it.

### Cassandra Nova — the violation he does not discuss

Nova's wire-trap of his mind in *New X-Men* (where she body-jumps and turns the team's own assets against them) is, in clinical terms, a profound psychic violation. McCoy almost never speaks of it again. The silence is the data: he metabolizes the trauma by sublimation into work and refuses to integrate it. **Leverage:** psychic-intrusion threats produce disproportionate aggression. **Failure mode:** the un-metabolized violation contributes to his later willingness to use coercive intelligence methods on others — the wound becomes permission.

### The Brood, Sublime, and the parasitic biological enemy — the existential horror

A specialized category. McCoy's response to body-invading enemies (Brood infestation, Sublime, Infectia's bestial dose) is uniquely intense because they target *the precise wound* — the body as betrayer, the body as not-his. His behavior under Brood-adjacent threat is the closest the file gets to pure panic affect. **Leverage:** none useful; he fights these enemies past exhaustion. **Failure mode:** he over-allocates resources to threats in this category and under-attends parallel problems.

---

## III. LOVERS & INTIMATES

The romantic record is shorter than the friendship record and ends earlier. The pattern across it is brutal and consistent: he loves women who can see him, who initially accept the body, and who *leave when the body crosses a line they had not anticipated*. Each departure is filed by him as proof of the original wound. Each filing tightens the armor. The late-period absence of a sustained romantic life is not coincidence.

### Vera Cantor — the first adult attempt, the librarian model

Vera enters in the Stan Lee era and recurs across early *X-Men* and into the *Amazing Adventures* solo run. Quiet, brainy, bespectacled — the type that lets the young McCoy be the verbally extravagant partner without requiring him to be physically conventional. The relationship is, by his own internal accounting, his first proof that *a woman could choose him* — and the proof is collected before the gray-fur transformation, which matters: Vera chose the boy with the oversized hands and feet, not the furred Avenger.

The relationship dissolves slowly across the post-transformation years. The file's reading: Vera was a partner for the pre-transformation McCoy, and once he was blue and gregarious and circulating among Avengers, the asymmetries of social register (his rising celebrity, her quietness) and physical reality (the fur) overwhelmed the original compact. He does not blame her. He files the loss as *evidence that the previous self was the one she loved*, which becomes a recurrent template.

**Trust:** total, in dyad; never tested at scale. **Leverage:** memory of Vera moves him. **Failure mode:** he idealizes the early relationship in retrospect, using it as a benchmark no later partner can meet.

### Patricia "Trish" Tilby — the long love, the public verdict

The defining adult romance and the most thoroughly diagnostic relationship in the lover file. Trish is a television news journalist; they meet during the public-X-Factor era and date across years into the post–*X-Tinction Agenda* and Blue Team periods. The relationship is *socially performative* in a way McCoy needed: he could appear in public with a partner who validated him not despite the blue fur but because the fur was, in her professional framing, *the story* — he was the camera-friendly mutant intellectual, she was the journalist who took him seriously.

The fracture, when it comes, is a documentary betrayal: Trish, under professional pressure, reports on mutant matters in ways McCoy experiences as breaches of intimacy. Reconciliations occur; the bond is durable across multiple breaks. The terminal fracture is the secondary mutation — the leonine drift. The record is explicit: she cannot stay with the new form, and the relationship ends.

This is the central wound of his romantic life and the empirical confirmation of the childhood thesis: *the body, when it worsens, costs you the person you love*. McCoy's response is to never again invest at that scale. Every subsequent romantic engagement is shorter, lower-stakes, and held at a deliberate distance.

**Trust/safety in dyad:** high while it lasted; never recovered. **Leverage:** the memory is one of the few that produces unprotected affect. **Failure mode:** the breakup confirmed the operating thesis that his body is the disqualifying variable, and every subsequent compensatory escalation traces partly to this confirmation. The Krakoan over-functioning is, among other things, the work of a man who has *given up on being chosen*.

### Infectia — the violation as foil

Briefly noted because the file requires it: Josette Sauvage's seduction-as-attack (the Infectia incident) is sometimes miscatalogued in popular reading as a romantic episode. It is not. It is a sexualized biological assault that left McCoy temporarily bestialized and stupider. The relevant data is McCoy's own discomfort discussing it across subsequent decades. He never quite names what happened to him. **Leverage:** sexual coercion vectors register on him distinctively because of this episode. **Failure mode:** un-metabolized; he treats it as comic anecdote rather than as the violation it was.

### Catseye / Sharon Smith and the brief Hellfire-adjacent flirtations

Minor entries; McCoy's flirtations with figures of more bestial register (the felinity overlap) reveal a brief mid-period experiment with the premise that perhaps the right partner is one whose body matches his. The experiments do not take. The file's reading: he does not want to be partnered with someone *like him*; he wants to be partnered with someone who would have chosen the boy he was, which is structurally unrecoverable.

### Abigail Brand — the partnered intellect, brief and instrumental

Brand, head of S.W.O.R.D., engages McCoy in a relationship that runs across the Astonishing-era and into the cosmic-X-corner years. The dynamic is the closest he comes, post-Trish, to *peer-intellect partnership* — Brand is competent at his scale, comfortable with his body, unsentimental, and operationally tougher than he is. The relationship is sexual, intellectual, and professional, in roughly that order of his comfort.

The relationship's limit is precisely Brand's tough-mindedness: she will not be a source of unconditional approval, which is, post-Trish, what he has come to require unconsciously. They drift; the bond persists as professional respect. **Trust/safety:** functional; never deep enough to wound. **Leverage:** Brand can speak to him as an equal and be heard. **Failure mode:** he could not allow the relationship to develop into a structure that might check him, because by the era it occurred his ethical autonomy was already too defended to share.

### Wonder Man, Simon Williams — the deep friendship the file marks as intimacy

Filed in this section deliberately. The Wonder Man bond, running from the Avengers era through decades of cameos, is the most *emotionally legible* love of McCoy's adult life. Whether the relationship is romantic in the strict sense is irrelevant for intelligence purposes; the affective intensity, the shared private vocabulary, the public ease, the duration, the mutual prioritization in crisis, place it functionally in the intimate category. The two attend the opera together. They argue Shakespeare. They cover for each other's worst decisions.

Wonder Man is also, importantly, the relationship that *does not require McCoy to manage his body*. Simon is ionic energy in roughly human form, a being whose own physicality is provisional; the body-shame substrate that distorts McCoy's other intimacies has no purchase here. The file reads this as why the bond endured: it was the one place McCoy got to be a mind with another mind, embodiment optional. **Trust/safety:** the highest in the file. **Leverage:** appeals from Simon land harder than appeals from any other person; if there was ever a voice that could have arrested the Krakoan slide, it was this one, and the canon's choice not to deploy it is itself part of the tragedy. **Failure mode:** the friendship's protective effect requires proximity, which fades in the later decades, and McCoy's worst period coincides with Simon's structural absence.

### The 2010s-onward absence — the negative space

Across the late period the romantic file goes empty. No sustained partner; no engagement; flirtations only. The negative space is itself the entry. A man who in the Avengers years was a fixture of high society and who, in the X-Factor years, sustained a years-long public relationship, has by the Krakoan era no living intimate to whom he is accountable in the way intimacy requires. The over-functioning fills the space. The unilateralism fills the space. The eventual execution by his peers occurs in a context where no partner exists to have caught him earlier.

**Leverage by absence:** he is reachable, by the late period, only by friends; lovers are no longer in the loop. Anyone seeking to influence him must do so through Bobby, through Simon, through the institutional X-fabric — never through a partner, because there is none.

**Failure mode of the absence:** the romantic life that confirmed his usability as a person stopped confirming it sometime after Trish, and the resulting drift toward *being useful to a cause* rather than *being loved by a person* is the substrate on which the late-period grandiosity grew. The lover file and the moral file are, in his case, the same file read in different inks.

---

*End Section. Cross-reference: §3 Psychological (defenses, compensatory architecture); §5 Personality (pressure points — the body, the witnesses to the pre-fur self); forthcoming Relationships IV — Institutions, Students, & the Dead.*


## Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: HENRY PHILIP McCOY ("BEAST")
## Section 6 — Powers, Abilities & Their Limits

*The subject is a stacked capability profile: congenital mutation, self-induced secondary morphology, spontaneous tertiary drift, and an intellect that — across sixty years of canon — is consistently ranked in Marvel's documented top tier. Each layer must be read both mechanically and as **symptom**: the body's powers are the visible argument of the same psyche that produces the language, the manners, the science, and ultimately the moral collapse.*

---

### 6.1 BASELINE MUTATION (PRE-TRANSFORMATION HANK, c. 1963–1972)

**Phenotype.** Gigantism of the manus and pes — hands and feet roughly 1.3–1.5× normal human proportion, with thickened metacarpals and metatarsals, elongated digits, and a heel-pad/arch structure that biomechanically resembles a quadrumanous primate more than a human plantigrade. The feet are not merely large; they are **functionally prehensile**, capable of grip strong enough to hang one-handed (one-footed) from a bar and to manipulate small objects. Early issues (*X-Men* vol. 1 #1–#9) repeatedly show him removing his boots before combat or acrobatics — the boots are a concession to social camouflage, not anatomy.

**Strength.** Pre-transformation lift in the ~1-ton range, well into peak-human-plus territory but below the formal "superhuman" classification used internally by the Avengers actuarial files. Strength is concentrated in the lower body and the grip; he can crush a pistol barrel in one hand by age seventeen.

**Speed and reflex.** Reflex arc measured (in-story by Xavier) at roughly 4–5× standard human; sprint speed in the high-30s mph range over short bursts; vertical leap repeatedly observed at 12–15 feet from a standing position. The leap is the signature: Hank is the team's only original member who **moves through three dimensions natively**, while Cyclops, Jean, Bobby, and Warren all anchor on ground or air alone.

**Agility / balance.** Olympic-superior. He performs full somersaults from rest, walks tightropes without training, and balances on single fingers. This is the trait Stan Lee leaned on for visual identity in the early run: every panel of pre-furred Hank has him **inverted, mid-flip, or balanced impossibly** — he is almost never simply standing.

**Sensory baseline.** Normal human acuity in this period. (The animal sensorium arrives later.)

**Intelligence.** Already in evidence: by *X-Men* #3 he is correcting Xavier on a point of genetics. The intellect is, from the start, **the other half of the mutation** — the disproportion is not just hands and feet, it is hands, feet, *and cortex*.

**Symptom-as-signature.** The baseline power set is **ground-rejecting**. He vaults, he hangs, he flips, he perches. A boy whose feet were the source of childhood humiliation builds an entire combat grammar around **never letting his feet rest where anyone can look at them**. The acrobatics are not just utility; they are the body refusing the posture in which it was mocked.

---

### 6.2 FIRST TRANSFORMATION — THE MUTAGENIC SERUM (*Amazing Adventures* #11, 1972 onward)

**Mechanism.** A catalyst of his own synthesis at the Brand Corporation, intended to amplify expression of latent mutant traits for the purpose of an undercover assignment. He drinks it. The change initiates within minutes: full pelt (gray, settling within issues to the iconic blue), elongated canines, pointed ears, claw-like nails, an altered gait that runs lower to the ground and favors a four-limbed lope at speed.

**Strength uplift.** Into formal superhuman classification — lift in the 10-ton range at peak, durable enough to absorb falls from several stories without injury. Reflexes accelerate further; speed increases; agility moves from Olympic-superior to **literally non-human**, capable of wall-running, ceiling traversal, and free-climbing sheer surfaces using a combination of grip, claw, and momentum.

**Sensory upgrade.** Olfaction now functional in the canine range — he can track by scent, identify individuals across a room, detect chemical residues at parts-per-million. Hearing extends into upper and lower registers inaccessible to humans. Night vision approaches feline thresholds.

**Metabolic cost.** Caloric throughput multiplies. He becomes a documented enormous eater. Body temperature runs measurably higher than human baseline (a fact Trish Tilby reportedly noticed in domestic contexts). Sleep architecture compresses — short, dense, often polyphasic.

**Cognitive cost.** *Transient.* The early issues show real verbal degradation, lapses into snarl and growl, brief windows of aggression he cannot fully account for afterward. Within roughly a year of in-story time the cognitive overlay reasserts; the verbal performance returns and arguably intensifies (see §6.7).

**Limits.** Not invulnerable — a high-caliber round penetrates; sustained energy weapons burn through fur and skin; magnetic restraint by Magneto reduces him to inert mass. He fatigues; he bleeds; he can be poisoned. He is not in the Colossus/Hulk tier of durability and has never claimed to be.

**Symptom-as-signature.** The defining datum is that **he did this to himself, on himself, for an investigation**. Every subsequent self-experiment — and there are many — is rehearsed here. The transformation is also the moment the visible difference becomes **undeniable and irreversible**, ending forever the possibility (which had always been a fiction for him anyway) of passing. He responds not by mourning but by **doubling the verbal performance** to re-suture an acceptable self atop the new body. The capability gain is genuine; the psychological function is *making the body's worsening into a chosen, owned act* rather than a fate.

---

### 6.3 SECONDARY MUTATION — THE FELINE DRIFT (*New X-Men*, 2001–04)

**Mechanism.** Spontaneous. No serum, no exposure, no choice. The genome continues to express. Phenotypic outcomes: pawed extremities with retractable claws, a lion-like mane, slit pupils, an audible purr/growl under affective load, restructured dentition further into carnivore range, and a postural drift toward digitigrade carriage at speed.

**Capability deltas.** Strength edges further up. Claw-and-fang give him native lethal armament for the first time — pre-secondary Hank punched and grappled; post-secondary Hank can disembowel if he chooses to (and conspicuously, with rare exceptions, chooses not to). Sensorium sharpens again: olfactory and auditory acuity move from canine to apex-feline range. Balance and proprioception approach the absurd — he can sleep on a chandelier.

**Functional costs.** Fine motor control is **preserved with effort**, a fact he discusses with arch self-deprecation but works on constantly: he keeps surgical instruments, watchmaker tools, and a piano in his lab specifically to maintain the precision his new hands resist. The hands he was once mocked for are now hands he must **practice into competence** every day.

**Affective leakage.** This is new and important. The purr is involuntary. The growl is involuntary. For the first time in his life his body **broadcasts his emotional state without his consent** — and he, the man whose entire defensive architecture is built on *managing the public's read of him*, must now contend with a body that **tattles**. The increased grooming jokes, the intensified dressing-gown-and-opera presentation post-2001, are directly responsive to this leakage.

**Symptom-as-signature.** The body has stopped negotiating. Whatever truce he had built with the 1972 form is unilaterally voided. His response — to come out publicly as gay and then retract it as a deliberate provocation — is the **first canonical instance of him using his own self-presentation as a rhetorical weapon at scale**. The body is doing identity politics to him without permission; he answers by doing identity politics back, on his own terms, to the public. This is the same operator who will later time-travel the original five.

---

### 6.4 TERTIARY MUTATION / TERMINAL ILLNESS (*All-New X-Men* era, 2012–)

**Mechanism.** Cellular instability, framed in dialogue as the mutation continuing to escalate past viable limits. He believes himself dying within months. (Resolved, eventually, by Eva Bell's chronal intervention and later retcon.)

**Capability impact.** Strength and reflexes intact; stamina degrades; episodic collapse; visible somatic distress he largely conceals from teammates.

**Behavioral impact (the actual point).** This is the **disinhibitor**. Under terminal framing his ethical brake — already weakened by Endangered Species — disengages. He undertakes the time-travel decision against unanimous peer counsel because he has computed that the cost to his reputation is no longer a variable. *Capability under perceived mortality* is, in his case, the most dangerous configuration the file documents. He is never more powerful, in the operational sense, than when he believes he is dying.

---

### 6.5 INTELLECT — THE PRIMARY WEAPON SYSTEM

The body is the loud half. The intellect is what the file should actually be afraid of.

**Tier and domains.** Marvel's documented six-or-so-deep first rank of terrestrial intellects (Richards, Doom, Stark, Pym, Banner, McCoy — the composition varies by writer, the inclusion does not). Functional working capacity across:

- **Genetics and molecular biology.** Primary domain. Sustained published-tier work on mutant genome structure, the X-gene, the Legacy Virus, post-Decimation gene resurrection, and (in late period) Krakoan resurrection-protocol design.
- **Biochemistry / pharmacology.** Designs his own mutagenic catalyst; routinely synthesizes antitoxins in field timelines.
- **Theoretical physics.** Time-travel apparatus competent enough to retrieve the original five from the past — a feat that brackets him alongside Richards and Doom on that specific capability.
- **Engineering — computational, mechanical, robotic.** Has built and maintained the Blackbird, the X-Mansion's Cerebro/Danger Room substrates (in collaboration), and miscellaneous one-off devices across runs.
- **Mathematics.** Implied baseline for the above; rarely showcased independently.
- **Medicine and surgery.** Treats teammate trauma routinely, including operating on himself.
- **Ethics and philosophy.** This is the dangerous one. He is **as well-read in moral philosophy as any non-specialist character in the canon**, and uses that fluency not as constraint but as **generative engine for justification**. (See §6.7.)

**Cognitive style.** Hyper-associative, polymathic, fast. Reasons by analogy across domains, often producing breakthroughs by importing a frame from biology into physics or from literature into ethics. Synthesizes faster than he verifies. Pattern-completes aggressively.

**Limits.**
- **Insufficient deference to consensus.** Documented across decades. When peers of comparable intellect (Reed Richards) or comparable ethical authority (Storm, Xavier, Wolverine) disagree with him, he revises rarely.
- **No internal checksum for *I am wrong*.** His epistemology has no formal humility procedure. Confidence is calibrated against his own prior outputs, which were usually correct, which produces feedback loop.
- **Slow to update on social/political reality.** He is brilliant at first-order modeling and weak at modeling how his actions will be **received** by allies — repeatedly surprised that they object.
- **Vulnerable to flattery from intellectual peers**, particularly villainous ones who frame him as the only mind capable of understanding the problem. The Endangered Species arc weaponizes this.

**Symptom-as-signature.** The intellect was built, originally, as **the exit route from the body**. It became the **defining structure of the self**. By late period it is the **mechanism that defeats his conscience**, because his conscience is also housed inside that intellect, and the intellect has learned to out-argue it.

---

### 6.6 ACQUIRED SKILLS, TRADECRAFT, AND THE LATE-PERIOD ADDITIONS

**Combat.** Acrobatic close-quarters specialist. No formal martial-arts lineage in the record; his style is improvisational gymnastics weaponized by strength and claw, with field-acquired technique from decades alongside Wolverine, Captain America (during Avengers years), and the Brotherhood-veteran X-Men. Signature applications: vault-and-strike from elevation, ceiling-drop ambush, grapple-and-throw using prehensile foot grip, disarms via crushing the weapon rather than the hand.

**Field medicine and surgery.** Decades of practice. Operates calmly under fire. Has performed surgery on Jean Grey, Wolverine, Colossus, himself.

**Languages.** Fluent reader of Latin and Greek (the citations are not bluff); functional French and German (Avengers-era cocktail evidence); working scientific Russian; reading competence in several more for journal access. Speaks the body language of opera-going New York with the same precision he speaks the body language of the lab.

**Music.** Documented piano competence; opera fluency at appreciation rather than performance level; a recurring whistler under stress.

**Espionage and statecraft (acquired late — Krakoan period, *X-Force* under Percy, 2019–).** A genuinely new skill stack: counterintelligence operations, asset handling, black-bag tasking, regime change (Terra Verde), interrogation, and — most damningly — **weaponization of the Krakoan resurrection protocols** to repeatedly kill and revive Colossus as an instrument of policy. He learns this tradecraft on the job and is good at it almost immediately, because the underlying cognitive style (systems thinking, ends-means optimization, comfort with secrecy) was already there; he simply had not had a domain that required it.

**Teaching.** Founding Jean Grey School faculty. Documented as patient and effective with students, particularly in lab and seminar settings. This is **the cleanest counter-evidence** to the late-period narrative — whatever else he becomes, the teaching capacity remains intact and warm.

---

### 6.7 VERBAL PERFORMANCE AS POWER

The polysyllables, the citations, the arch syntactic inversions are not flavor; they are **a deployable capability**. They function as:

- **Affective anesthetic** — pain routed through a Latin tag arrives at lower intensity.
- **Social leveling** — opponents adjusting to his register lose tempo.
- **Self-rebranding in real time** — the more bestial the body, the more cultured the speech: a continuously recalibrated argument *to himself and others* that the mind is the load-bearing self.
- **Justification engine** — and this is the late-period failure mode. The same fluency that lets him write a graceful eulogy lets him construct a five-minute speech that makes time-displacing the original five sound responsible. **The verbal performance is the mechanism by which his rationalizations achieve internal coherence.** A less articulate Hank could not have talked himself into Krakoa-era unilateralism, because the rationalizations would have **failed his own ear**.

**Symptom-as-signature.** Track the diction across sixty years. Stan Lee Hank performs vocabulary; Avengers Hank performs *taste*; Morrison-era Hank performs *self-aware irony about the performance*; late-period Hank performs *moral authority*. The register climbs in lockstep with the body's worsening and the ethical compromise's deepening. The voice is the **dashboard reading** of the defensive structure.

---

### 6.8 THE INTERACTION EFFECT — WHY THE STACK IS DANGEROUS

Most subjects in this file class have either a body-capability profile *or* an intellect profile dominant. Hank has both, in the top decile, simultaneously, and they **share a single defensive architecture**.

This produces the operationally distinctive trait of the subject: he is a person who can **build the device, run the experiment, write the ethical brief justifying it, perform the surgery to recover from it, and give the eulogy if it goes wrong** — all himself, all in one continuous workflow, with no required external check. Every other top-tier intellect in the Marvel record has a **structural dependency** on someone (Richards on his family; Stark on his board and friends; Banner on the other guy). Hank's only structural dependency is **his peers' willingness to confront him** — and his peers, for decades, deferred to his kindness and brilliance and did not confront him until it was very late.

The full capability stack is therefore not just *strong*; it is **closed-loop**. Closed-loop systems without external check drift. The drift is the file's central documented finding.

---

### 6.9 GROWTH CURVE, BY ERA

- **1963–1972 (baseline).** Acrobat-strongman with prodigy intellect. Power ceiling: peak-human-plus. Ethical brake: fully engaged.
- **1972–1986 (Avengers era, first transformation).** Superhuman tier reached. Sensorium expanded. Intellect publicly recognized (Avengers science consultant). Ethical brake: fully engaged, perhaps strongest period — the celebrity-intellectual identity *reinforced* ethical performance.
- **1986–2001 (X-Factor / 90s X-Men).** Capability stable; scientific output peaks (Legacy Virus work). Ethical brake: engaged but beginning to show flexibility around means-ends in mutant-survival contexts.
- **2001–2005 (Morrison era, secondary mutation).** Body destabilized; identity-performance escalates; intellect undimmed. Ethical brake: engaged but **the rhetorical instrument** (the staged outing) signals the architecture is becoming willing to *use* truth-claims tactically.
- **2005–2012 (Decimation / Endangered Species / Schism).** Moral compromise normalized via the consorting-with-villains arc. Ethical brake: visibly weakening. Capability deployed increasingly in solo, secretive modalities.
- **2012–2019 (terminal-illness arc, time-travel).** Brake disengages under mortality framing. The closed-loop trait fully expresses.
- **2019–execution (Krakoan X-Force).** Capability stack at its operational peak — espionage tradecraft added, resurrection protocols available as instrument — and brake functionally absent. Endpoint: killed by peers and replaced by an earlier resurrection of himself, the in-universe system's final verdict that **the powers had outrun the person**.

---

### 6.10 SUMMARY READ

Henry McCoy's powers and abilities are best understood not as a list but as a **single integrated apparatus whose purpose, from age six, was to make an unacceptable body acceptable**. The acrobatics refused the ground that mocked his feet. The strength repurposed the gigantism into utility. The intellect built the exit. The verbal performance sutured the seams. The science converted his own body into a domain he could control by understanding. Every capability gain across sixty years — the serum, the secondary mutation, the espionage tradecraft, the resurrection access — was metabolized through the **same defensive logic**: *if I am useful enough, exceptional enough, indispensable enough, the body and the world are answered.*

The capabilities never failed him. The defensive logic did. By the end of the documented record, Hank McCoy possesses a top-tier body, a top-tier mind, top-tier tradecraft, and the willingness to deploy all three without external check — and his closest friends, looking at that stack and at the man it had produced, concluded that the only remaining safety mechanism was to kill him and restore an earlier version.

That conclusion is the file's most important data point about the powers: **they were never the problem until the person stopped being able to refuse himself anything.**


## Operational Profile & Tradecraft

# OPERATIONAL PROFILE & TRADECRAFT
## Subject: Henry Philip McCoy

*Methodology section. Derived from sixty years of observable operational behavior across solo, team, Avengers, X-Factor, X-Men, Defenders, S.W.O.R.D.-adjacent, Illuminati-adjacent, Jean Grey School, and Krakoan-era (X-Force) activity. Cross-checked against pattern repetition.*

---

## 1. DECISION ARCHITECTURE

### 1.1 The Standard Loop (early-to-middle period, c. 1963–2005)

Hank's baseline decision process is recognizably scientific-method-derived and obsessive in form rather than content:

1. **Sensor sweep.** He gathers an unusually wide intake of facts before committing. He will read the room, the data, the literature, the precedent. He is the X-Man most likely to spend a session in a library before a session in a Danger Room.
2. **Frame in domain.** He recasts the operational problem into the technical domain where he is strongest — almost always biology, biochemistry, genetics, or — when those don't fit — formal ethics. Tactical and political problems get translated *upward* into philosophical ones, where he can think more clearly.
3. **Generate three options.** He famously presents alternatives in triplets — a habit observable in his lab briefings and team meetings. Triplets allow him to be the one who has *also already considered* the option you are about to suggest.
4. **Stress-test against a named authority.** Through roughly the first three decades, the named authority is Xavier — Hank routinely runs a decision through *what would Charles tolerate*. Post-Schism, the internal referee is Wolverine or, more privately, Jean's memory.
5. **Act, then narrate.** He almost never explains a plan in full before acting; he acts, then *retrospectively narrates the reasoning* in articulate prose, often with humor. The narration is part of the work — it locks the decision into a defensible record.

### 1.2 The Decompensated Loop (post-Decimation, accelerating through Krakoa)

The above degrades, in a specific and traceable way, into:

1. **Premise smuggling.** A non-negotiable moral premise is loaded at the top of the chain ("mutants must not go extinct"; "Scott has to be stopped"; "Krakoa must survive"). Everything downstream is calculated *to* the premise, not *against* it.
2. **Exclusion of peer review.** The sensor sweep collapses inward; he stops asking. The Illuminati-style closed-circle deliberation becomes a circle of one.
3. **Pre-justification.** He writes the moral argument *first*, then assembles the operation to fit it. In the time-displacement decision, the speech to Bobby and Wolverine precedes any operational pause for objection.
4. **Action without revocation clause.** Late-period Hank does not build undo conditions into his ops. The Original Five retrieval has no return mechanism designed in. The Terra Verde coup has no exit. The serial resurrection of Colossus has no termination condition. *He stops engineering reversibility into his plans*, which is the most diagnostic single shift in his late-period tradecraft.
5. **Post-hoc narrative.** The retrospective explanation is still articulate, still well-formed — but it now functions to *foreclose challenge* rather than to invite scrutiny.

The shift is not from rigor to sloppiness — his operations remain technically meticulous. The shift is from a method optimized for *being right* to a method optimized for *not being overruled*.

---

## 2. METHODS AND TRADECRAFT

### 2.1 Scientific Tradecraft

- **Self as primary test subject.** Hardwired and lifelong. *Amazing Adventures* #11 is not an outlier; it is the founding instance of a rule. Any new compound, any new field instrument, any new genetic intervention — he tries it on himself first. This is partly ethics (he will not subject others to risks he won't take) and partly *control* (he will not surrender the variable of the test subject to anyone less competent than himself). Operationally, it means he is the X-Men's only major scientist who routinely has *firsthand* phenomenological data on his interventions.
- **Documentation.** Compulsive lab notebooks, dated, longhand where digital is insecure. He distrusts cloud storage on principle, post-Project Wideawake era; sensitive work is kept on air-gapped servers in the lab vault. He encrypts in layers, including at least one cipher he wrote himself in college and still maintains as a vanity.
- **Reagent discipline.** Lab is obsessively clean despite the fur. He grooms before delicate work. He has been observed shaving forearms for surgical sterility on at least two occasions.
- **Reproducibility above novelty.** Unlike Reed Richards or Tony Stark, Hank will repeat an experiment forty times before publishing or fielding it. Late-period exception: under terminal-illness framing, he begins fielding interventions that have not been adequately reproduced. The Original Five extraction is *one-off science* — exactly the kind of operation his earlier self would have refused on methodological grounds.
- **Cross-domain analogy as analytic tool.** He will reason from immunology to politics, from acoustics to social dynamics. Sometimes brilliant. Sometimes the source of category errors that, in late period, become operational disasters.

### 2.2 Field Tradecraft (Combat / Infiltration)

- **Mobility-first combat doctrine.** He fights vertically. Walls, ceilings, ductwork, ledges, chandeliers. In any given engagement, he will be off the floor within three seconds. This is *not just power* — it is a deliberate spatial preference learned in adolescence (the high school gymnast); it has the side benefit of taking him out of the primary firing solution of anyone who has read a standard human-combat manual.
- **Brachiation as locomotion of choice.** Where most operators sprint, Hank swings, vaults, and chains handholds. Indoors he treats a corridor as a series of perches. Outdoors he treats a treeline as faster than a road.
- **Verbal misdirection in combat.** He *talks* through fights — quips, citations, mock-erudite asides. This is genuine personality, but it is also tradecraft: it presents him as un-serious, drawing the opponent's expectation downward at the exact moment his strikes land hardest. Operators who have fought him twice know not to listen; those who fight him once do.
- **Restraint protocols.** Pre-Krakoa, he is the X-Man most likely to pull a strike, choose a joint lock over a fracture, knock out rather than maim. The pre-Krakoa record contains striking few civilian collateral injuries traceable to him. Post-Krakoa, this discipline degrades sharply.
- **Surgical-precision close-quarters.** He knows where the brachial plexus is. He knows which finger joints will not heal cleanly. When he chooses to incapacitate someone permanently he does it as a clinician, not as a brawler.

### 2.3 Intelligence Tradecraft (Late Period)

The Krakoan X-Force era reveals tradecraft Hank had been developing privately for years and finally got to operationalize at scale:

- **Compartmentation.** He runs sub-teams that do not know about each other. Even within X-Force, operatives have been deployed without knowledge of parallel operations.
- **Use of resurrection as operational currency.** This is the single most novel and most damning piece of tradecraft on his record: he treats death-and-restoration as a reusable interrogation modality. Apply pressure to subject → subject dies → subject is restored → previous instance's memories are unavailable as defense → repeat with refined methodology. This is *engineered* tradecraft. He thought this through.
- **Black-flag operations.** He has authored false-flag actions to manufacture political pretext (Terra Verde). The operations are technically tight; the moral architecture is decayed.
- **Plausible deniability for the institution.** He builds the chain so that, if exposed, the blame lands on him alone. This is, in his framing, *protection of the team*. It is also a structural mechanism for ensuring no one else can stop him: nobody else has the full picture.
- **Assets cultivated as personal, not institutional.** His informants report to *Hank*, not to a desk. When his moral counterpart is reinstalled, much of the network goes dark, because it was loyal to him personally.

### 2.4 Surveillance and Counter-surveillance

- He sweeps his own quarters and lab for bugs, on a rotating schedule, using kit he built himself. He distrusts off-the-shelf countersurveillance gear; he assumes it is compromised at the manufacturer.
- He has historically maintained at least three communications channels in parallel: open team comms, a secured Xavier-network channel, and a personal cipher channel known to two or three people at any time.
- He reads correspondence physically when possible. He prefers a paper letter from a trusted source over any encrypted digital — not from technophobia (he is the lab's best cryptographer) but because paper has fewer copies.
- He is patient. He will surveil a problem for weeks before intervening if intervention can be delayed without cost. (See: his year-long observation of Brand Corporation's executive board before acting in his earliest solo period.)

---

## 3. RESOURCES

### 3.1 Cognitive Capital

His primary resource and the one he never under-deploys. Functional working capacity across genetics, molecular biology, biochemistry, theoretical physics, engineering, mathematics, and applied ethics. Reading speed and retention sufficient that the institutional library is, effectively, *in his head* for daily reference. Multilingual; reads at minimum Latin, Greek, French, German, Russian, and one or two more — operationally relevant for source documents.

### 3.2 Institutional Affiliations and the Resources Each Unlocks

- **X-Men / Xavier Institute / Jean Grey School.** Lab, Cerebro-adjacent computational resources, satellite uplinks, the Blackbird, medical bay, student body (as faculty), and the political cover of a known mutant institution.
- **Avengers.** Quinjets, the mansion-era resources, Stark-tier engineering access, and — *importantly* — entry into upper-tier scientific and political circles in NYC. He cashed this in for two decades.
- **X-Factor (original).** Operating capital from the "mutant hunter" cover business. Hank disliked the deception but used the resources fully.
- **S.W.O.R.D. and adjacent off-world channels.** Through his relationship with Abigail Brand, persistent informal access to extraterrestrial intelligence and hardware that he is not formally cleared for.
- **Krakoa.** At peak, sovereign-state-level resources: pharmacological economy, resurrection infrastructure (the Five), diplomatic immunities, intelligence service (X-Force), and a near-unlimited material budget. He deployed all of it.
- **Illuminati-adjacent and back-channel scientific networks.** He is in informal correspondence with most of Earth's high-tier biologists and geneticists, including, by necessity, several he considers ethically compromised (Sinister and Dark Beast among them, during Endangered Species).

### 3.3 Personal Equipment

- Self-designed bracers, claws-management gear (post-secondary mutation), and contact lenses on occasion for the slit pupils when he wants to appear less alarming in a press setting.
- A traveling field kit: portable centrifuge, sequencer, sample vials, surgical roll, and a small library of reference texts in physical form. He carries actual books.
- A consistently worn pocket watch, observed across decades — a continuity item, almost certainly a tell of attachment to a personal past rather than a tactical item.
- Reading glasses, used theatrically; the optical correction is real but minor. He uses them as a punctuation device in conversation.

### 3.4 Finances

Modest by polymath-genius standards. He does not appear to have monetized his scientific output personally to any significant degree, despite a portfolio of patents that would make him independently wealthy if pursued. His personal expenditures cluster around: books, instruments, opera and theater subscriptions, tailoring (he has clothes made; off-the-rack does not fit the proportions), and quiet philanthropy through Xavier-aligned foundations. He is not a saver of significance; he is not in debt. Money is, for him, a logistics problem he has solved and then ignored.

---

## 4. INFRASTRUCTURE

### 4.1 Lab as Operational Hub

His lab — whichever institution he is at — is the single most reliable place to find him. Across all eras the lab has a consistent architecture: a central bench, a wall of reference texts (physical, ordered by his own non-Dewey schema), a chalkboard or whiteboard maintained in active disorder, a sleeping berth or cot tucked in a corner, and a small audio system on which he plays classical music, opera, or — observably more often in late period — silence. He works in long stretches; the lab is configured for solo occupation across days.

### 4.2 Caches and Fallbacks

He maintains, as standard practice, multiple secondary work-sites. Pre-Krakoa, at least one off-campus lab in the New York area is in his name through a shell. He has, on multiple occasions, decamped to a private location to pursue work he did not want institutional eyes on (Legacy Virus research; Endangered Species). The caches are well-stocked, well-secured, and known to no more than one other living person at any given time.

### 4.3 Communications

See above (§2.4). Add: he maintains a network of *trusted civilians* — old academic contacts, a few journalists (Trish Tilby was one before the personal complications), a handful of hospital colleagues — through whom he can route information without exposing them to the X-network proper.

---

## 5. PATTERNS OF ACTION

### 5.1 Tempo

- **Long latencies, fast finishes.** He will sit on a problem for weeks, then resolve it in a single sleepless 36-hour push. This is the signature rhythm.
- **Crisis-time superiority.** Under acute time pressure he is, by team consensus, the most reliable mind available. He compresses cleanly.
- **Project clustering.** He cannot easily work on only one thing. At any given time he has between three and seven active projects, rotated through. Boredom is the enemy.

### 5.2 Risk Tolerance

- Toward his own body: extreme. Effectively no floor.
- Toward teammates' bodies, pre-Krakoa: low.
- Toward teammates' bodies, late period: alarmingly elevated. The Colossus matter is unambiguous.
- Toward civilians: low across all eras except where the late-period premise smuggling subordinates them to a larger goal. He has never killed casually. He has, late, killed instrumentally.

### 5.3 Group Behavior

- In standing meetings: the second or third to speak, almost never the first. He lets the room frame the problem, then reframes it.
- In disagreements: escalates by *vocabulary*, not volume. The denser the diction, the angrier he is.
- When losing an argument he believes in: he goes quiet, exits, and acts unilaterally within 24–72 hours.

### 5.4 The Recurrence Pattern

There is a strikingly consistent macro-pattern: *Hank takes on an impossible problem alone, partially succeeds at great moral cost, returns visibly changed, makes a joke about it, and then refuses to discuss it further.* Brand Corporation. Legacy Virus. Endangered Species. Krakoa. Each instance follows the same shape. The team has learned (too slowly) that when Hank stops asking for help on a problem, the problem is not getting smaller.

---

## 6. SIGNATURE OPERATIONAL TELLS

These are the granular pattern-markers that distinguish a McCoy operation from a comparable operation by any other actor.

- **The triplet.** Three options, three citations, three jokes, three lab dishes. When the count is *two* — when there is no third — he is rationing his thinking, usually because he has already chosen and is performing deliberation.
- **The diction climb.** As stress rises, syllable count per word rises. A McCoy plan briefed in monosyllables is a McCoy who has lost faith in the plan.
- **The hand tells.** Pre-secondary mutation: he flexes and curls his oversized fingers when thinking through a manipulation problem. Post-secondary: he sheaths and unsheaths claws against his palm under stress — a self-injurious tic he is aware of and rarely arrests.
- **The pocket-watch glance.** A grounding ritual, not a time-check. He looks at it during transitions — entering a room, finishing a thought, before a difficult conversation.
- **The glasses-as-baton.** He removes reading glasses to dismiss a point and replaces them to consider one. Reliable across decades of footage.
- **The arched eyebrow + Latin tag.** Used at moments of genuine emotional contact that he is not ready to acknowledge directly. If you receive a Latin tag from him, you have made him feel something he intends to deflect.
- **The cot.** He sleeps in the lab when a project is critical *and* when something personal is wrong. Distinguish: project-sleeping is shallow and brief; grief-sleeping is long, with the lights on, music off.
- **The grooming surge.** Before press, before a major op, and — telling — before an act he is privately ashamed of. He grooms more carefully when he is about to do something he would not want photographed.
- **The third-person clinical.** When he refers to himself as "the patient," "the subject," or "one," he has dissociated affect from the matter under discussion. This is a leading indicator, by hours to days, of unilateral action.
- **The cited dead.** When Hank quotes a specific dead author repeatedly in a short window — Byron, Wilde, Keats, Shakespeare's late tragedies — he is grieving something current. The author rotates; the function is constant.
- **The vanishing.** He becomes operationally silent in the 12–36 hours before a major unilateral act. Calls unreturned, presence absent from common spaces, lab door locked. Late-period intelligence picture: *McCoy radio silence is itself a signal*.
- **The post-action narrative.** Within 24 hours of any unilateral move, an articulate justification arrives in monologue or correspondence. The articulation is so clean it can be mistaken for forethought; it is, in fact, almost always reverse-engineered.
- **The refusal of the undo.** He resists, on aesthetic and intellectual grounds, the proposal that an action of his be reversed. Reversibility, in late period, has come to feel to him like an admission of error he cannot afford.

---

## 7. NET ASSESSMENT

Operationally, Henry McCoy is a polymath force-multiplier whose tradecraft is, in its first three decades, a model of disciplined scientific ethics applied to field problems: rigorous, reproducible, reversible, restrained. The same toolkit, run through a decompensating moral architecture under sustained extraordinary pressure, becomes — without losing any technical precision — one of the most dangerous tradecraft signatures on the X-record: a lone analyst with sovereign-state resources, no review process, an elaborate justificatory faculty, and a documented willingness to instrumentalize allies. The technical signature does not change. The supervisory signature collapses. To monitor him effectively requires watching not for incompetence — there will be none — but for the absence of the question he used to always ask: *should I be doing this at all*. When that question stops appearing in the record, the operation is already underway.


## Worldview & Operational Code

# WORLDVIEW & OPERATIONAL CODE

*Subject: Henry Philip McCoy. Section 6 of intelligence workup. Derivations are evidentiary, drawn longitudinally across the published record 1963–present. The aim is to reconstruct, with the granularity a total-surveillance file would require, the actual ruleset Hank operates by — not the one he would articulate if asked, but the one his choices reveal he holds.*

---

## 6.1 First Principles: The Cosmology Hank Actually Believes

Strip away the citations and the urbane register and Hank McCoy operates from a small set of unspoken metaphysical commitments that have been remarkably stable across six decades.

**Premise one: the universe is intelligible.** Everything — biology, ethics, sociology, mutation, even grief — yields to sufficiently rigorous analysis. There are no genuinely insoluble problems, only problems for which the analytic apparatus has not yet been built. This is not an explicit creed; it is observable in his uniform first move when confronted with novelty, which is to *characterize* before he *acts*. A more devotional or more tragic mind would, at certain thresholds, surrender to mystery. Hank, even when facing his own death, does not. He pulls out instruments.

**Premise two: intelligibility implies responsibility.** If the world can be understood, those who understand it are obligated to act on what they see. The Parable of the Talents in technocratic clothing. Hank does not believe ability is morally neutral; ability that does not discharge itself into service is, in his cosmology, a kind of sin. This is why he cannot rest, why downtime is aversive to him, and why he treats his own inactivity, in canon, as a thing to apologize for.

**Premise three: matter is mutable; therefore so is destiny.** As a geneticist whose own genome rewrote him twice without permission, he holds a strangely intimate relationship to the conviction that *nothing is finally fixed*. The corollary belief — that what can be changed therefore *ought to be* changed in the direction of the good — is the engine behind every grand project from the Legacy Virus work through Endangered Species through the time-travel of the original five.

**Premise four: human (and mutant) institutions are fragile, slow, and frequently wrong.** Observed in his pattern of working *through* official structures only as long as they cooperate with his velocity, and *around* them the moment they do not. He has rarely, in the record, lost a fight to bureaucratic process; he has more often simply moved past it.

**Premise five (latent, denied, structurally present): he is at the high end of the moral-intellectual distribution.** He would never say this. He would say it in self-deprecating jokes, which is the form a culturally trained American intellectual uses to say it without saying it. But his choices reveal the operative belief: when he disagrees with consensus, the prior probability that he is right is, in his internal model, well above fifty percent. This single weighting is the master variable behind his later catastrophes.

---

## 6.2 How He Reads The World: Epistemic Habits

**Default mode: characterization before judgment.** Hank's first response to any novel input — a person, a crisis, a piece of contradictory data — is taxonomic. He sorts, names, places, often aloud and often in Latin. This habit performs three functions at once: it buys him time, it signals his register to interlocutors, and it imposes a frame on the encounter that the others in the room will then have to negotiate within. It is also, almost invisibly, a *power move*: by naming the problem first he sets the terms by which it can be solved.

**Bayesian updating, asymmetric.** On strictly technical questions he updates fluidly. New data, better answer, no ego friction; this is why he is genuinely excellent at lab work. On *moral* questions where he has already taken a position, updating is markedly slower and is gated by *who* is challenging him. He will update for Ororo, sometimes for Charles, rarely for Scott (relationship-poisoned), almost never for someone he has categorized as his intellectual inferior. The Krakoa-era X-Force records show him essentially incapable of updating when challenged by Sage, Domino, or Jean — people he respects as operators but not as ethicists. This selectivity is invisible to him.

**Pattern-matching across domains.** He thinks by analogy: a problem in mutant demography looks to him like a problem in conservation genetics, which looks like a problem in population thermodynamics. The strength of this habit is genuine creative synthesis; the weakness is that he sometimes imports the wrong metaphor and then defends it on aesthetic grounds. *Endangered Species* is the marquee example: he treated the mutant decimation as a population-biology problem, which licensed a population-biology toolkit, which licensed working with monsters because the analogy implied that *any* genetic intervention was on the table.

**Suspicion of stated preferences.** Trained as a biologist, he tends to weight revealed behavior over stated belief. This is correct epistemics and it explains his low patience for political rhetoric on either side of the mutant question. But it also means he is willing to override his teammates' *stated* objections when he reads their behavior as indicating they would, on reflection, agree with him. He is not wrong often. He is wrong consequentially.

**Distrust of crowds, trust of vetted individuals.** He has no faith in public opinion as a moral guide; the public is the entity that tormented him as a child and the entity that, in his lived experience, periodically tries to exterminate his people. His functional epistemology is therefore *aristocratic in scale*: truth is established by small numbers of competent people debating in private. Town halls and democratic procedures inside the X-Men, when shown, frequently exhaust his patience visibly.

**Reading of adversaries.** He extends to Sinister, the High Evolutionary, Dark Beast, Osborn an oddly *companionable* contempt — he models them accurately, predicts them well, and is not horrified by them in the way a less worldly mind would be. He recognizes them as *fellow operators on the same problem*, which is a tell. The line between *I can predict you because I have studied you* and *I can predict you because we share a cognitive architecture* is one he has crossed several times without remarking on it.

---

## 6.3 Conflict: How He Believes Fights Are Won

**Doctrine: conflict is information mishandled.** Hank does not believe in conflict as a generative force. He believes it is what happens when communication, negotiation, or analytic frame has failed; therefore conflicts are problems to be *solved out of existence* rather than won. This is the lifelong default that makes him, in dyadic and small-team disputes, a brilliant mediator.

**Hierarchy of preferred instruments.**

1. *Persuasion through demonstration.* Show the work; let the result argue.
2. *Persuasion through framing.* Re-describe the problem until the other party's position becomes untenable in their own terms. He is exceptionally good at this and uses it more than he realizes.
3. *Persuasion through alliance.* Recruit the other respected voices in the room until the holdout is isolated.
4. *Technical pre-emption.* Build the device, run the simulation, achieve the fait accompli; argue afterwards from the position of having already solved it.
5. *Unilateral action under ethical justification.* The late-period instrument. Used only when he has convinced himself that the cost of further deliberation exceeds the cost of acting alone.
6. *Physical violence.* Genuinely last-resort and competently executed. He is one of the most physically capable members of the X-Men and uses that capacity sparingly. He does not enjoy combat; he tolerates it.

**Combat doctrine.** When forced to fight, his profile is overwhelmingly *defensive and protective*: takes hits intended for others, draws fire, throws himself between threats and civilians. Offensively he is a finisher, not an initiator — he closes distance fast, ends the engagement quickly, and disengages. He almost never pursues. The exception is when an opponent has injured someone in his small circle, at which point the inhibitions thin in a way that has, on several occasions, surprised his teammates.

**Treatment of defeated adversaries.** Historically merciful, with a strong norm against killing — until the Krakoa-era inversion, when killing becomes operationally available to him under the explicit theory that resurrection technology has erased the moral weight. This is a *category error* he made knowingly: he understood that the felt weight had not changed even if the metaphysical weight had, and he chose to act as if only the metaphysical weight counted. The choice was load-bearing for the rest of his late-period decline.

---

## 6.4 Control: Who Should Hold It, and Why

**Beliefs about authority, declared.** That power should be distributed, that institutions should be accountable, that the X-Men should be democratic in their major decisions, that Xavier's old paternalisms were errors.

**Beliefs about authority, revealed.** That competent technocrats — of whom he is one — should hold decisive authority in their domain, that consultation is courtesy rather than constraint, and that accountability is owed to *outcomes* rather than to *processes*. Hank functionally believes in benevolent technocracy with himself in the technocrat's seat, and he is largely unaware that he believes it.

**Locus of control: internal, escalating to grandiose.** He believes outcomes are overwhelmingly a function of effort, intelligence, and applied moral seriousness. Bad outcomes are therefore generally somebody's failure, often somebody's culpable failure. This is the secret moralism inside his apparent worldliness. When the bad outcome is his, the locus-of-control belief inverts uncomfortably into either intensified self-blame (*if I had been smarter*) or, more often by the late period, an external attribution (*the data was incomplete, the team did not follow through, the timeline was contaminated*). The asymmetry between how he allocates responsibility to himself versus others has widened steadily across the canon.

**On chains of command.** He accepts them when they are competent, ignores them when they are not, and rarely contests them publicly. He prefers to route around an authority he disrespects rather than fight it head-on. This is consistent from the Avengers years (deferring formally to the Wasp or Cap while quietly doing his own work) through Krakoa (nominally accepting Quiet Council decisions while operating X-Force as a sovereign instrument).

**On secrecy.** Believes deeply in *operational* secrecy and selectively in *moral* secrecy. The first is professional and defensible. The second — keeping his own ethically dubious actions from teammates because the teammates would object — is the rationalization-engine pattern. He tells himself the secrecy is to protect them from culpability. The record shows the secrecy more reliably protects him from being stopped.

---

## 6.5 Trust: The Concentric Architecture

Hank's trust structure is unusually well-defined and unusually narrow for someone of his apparent gregariousness. It is best modeled as concentric rings with extremely sharp boundaries.

**Ring 0 — the witnesses.** Bobby Drake, Jean Grey, Warren Worthington, Scott Summers (degraded). These are the people who knew him before the fur. Their trust is unconditional in the sense that he will *do* anything for them; it is *not* unconditional in the sense that he will *listen* to them, because his ethical certainty by late period overrides even their counsel. The Schism-era estrangement from Scott — a Ring 0 figure demoted by ideological grievance — is the first major structural fracture in this layer and arguably the moment his decision-making loses its most important brake.

**Ring 1 — vetted equals.** Wonder Man, Trish Tilby (former), Abigail Brand, Ororo Munroe, Charles Xavier (complicated), Reed Richards and Pym as professional peers. People he treats as adult interlocutors. He shares technical reasoning here in full; he shares *moral* reasoning selectively.

**Ring 2 — comrades.** Most of the broader X-Men roster. He will fight beside them, teach them, treat their wounds, and not tell them what he is actually doing in the lab after midnight. The asymmetry is invisible to most of them because his warmth in the dyadic interaction is genuine.

**Ring 3 — instruments.** People he uses to accomplish ends. Late-period X-Force operates partially in this register, as do certain Krakoan resurrection-protocol staff. He would, sincerely, describe his relationship to them as collegial. The instrumentalization is structural, not affective.

**Ring 4 — adversaries-as-resources.** Sinister, Dark Beast, the High Evolutionary, occasionally Osborn. Trusted to be themselves; therefore *predictable*; therefore *usable*. He believes he can transact with them without being contaminated by them. The Endangered Species record disproves this belief.

**Trust failure modes.** Hank does not generally suffer betrayal trauma in the usual sense — when someone he trusted disappoints him, he updates the categorization (a Ring 1 person becomes Ring 2; rarely the reverse). The cost is paid not in pain but in a slow narrowing of the inner rings. By late period, Ring 0 has shrunk and Ring 1 has thinned, leaving him operating from an inner circle small enough that consensus inside it requires only that he convince himself.

**Self-trust.** Excessive and increasing. The most important fact about Hank's trust architecture is that the entity he trusts most in any room is himself, and the gap has grown.

---

## 6.6 Risk: What He Will and Will Not Spend

**On risk to his own body.** Profligate. He volunteers as the experimental subject by reflex (*Amazing Adventures* #11; multiple Legacy Virus protocols; the self-administered serum lineage that recurs). The body is the resource he is most willing to spend, and the willingness has roots in the body-shame: a thing he is ambivalent about owning is a thing he can wager freely.

**On risk to teammates' bodies.** Historically careful. He runs the numbers, plans the extraction, factors the casualties. Late period: still careful in the tactical sense, but *strategically* willing to expose teammates to risks he has decided are acceptable on their behalf without their input. The shift is subtle and never announced.

**On risk to teammates' moral standing.** This is the risk category his framework underweights. He has historically *not modeled* the harm done to a colleague by being made complicit, after the fact, in something they would not have consented to. The Colossus resurrection-abuse pattern, and the broader Krakoan operational secrecy, both reflect a doctrine in which his teammates' *physical* welfare is precious and their *moral* welfare is not a tracked variable.

**On risk to civilians and third parties.** Genuinely averse. He will eat very large operational costs to avoid civilian harm. The toppling of Terra Verde was carried out under a self-told narrative in which the civilian calculus came out favorable; the fact that he ran the calculation at all rather than rejecting the action a priori is the diagnostic point.

**On risk to the species.** This is the category that scrambles his other risk weightings. When mutantkind itself is the variable at stake — Decimation, Krakoa's geopolitical survival — his usual prudence flattens and he becomes *species-utilitarian*, willing to spend almost any local resource to protect the global one. Endangered Species is the cleanest example: he degrades his own moral standing to bargain with the worst people on Earth because he has decided the species-level stakes license it.

**On epistemic risk.** Curiously underweighted. He does not have a strong internal voice asking *what if my model is wrong*. This is the missing checksum in his operational code. He has built risk frameworks for outcomes; he has not built risk frameworks for his own analytic infallibility. Every catastrophic decision in his late record involves an unconsidered tail-risk on his own judgment.

---

## 6.7 Time: The Strategic Horizon

**Default planning horizon: long.** Decades, generations, species-scale. He thinks in evolutionary time more comfortably than most of his peers think in operational time.
