**Failure mode: when the horizon collapses.** Under terminal-illness framing (*All-New X-Men*), under existential species-threat framing (Decimation), under Krakoan emergency framing, his horizon shortens violently. *Long-horizon Hank* is one of the wisest tacticians in the X-Men. *Short-horizon Hank* is one of the most dangerous, because his velocity and his certainty remain calibrated to long-horizon stakes while his deliberation window has compressed. The time-travel decision was made by a short-horizon Hank wielding long-horizon tools.

**Relationship to history.** Reverent of intellectual history (constantly quoting), skeptical of political history (treats most institutional memory as ballast), confident he can break with precedent when the case is strong. The selectivity matters: he will defer to Darwin and Maxwell against his own first instinct, but he will not defer to Xavier's old norms against his own current judgment.

**Relationship to the future.** Believes it is genuinely shapeable, believes the shaping is largely a function of present competent action, believes the X-Men's role is to *bend* history rather than be carried by it. This is, when you strip it down, a belief Magneto and Xavier and Sinister all share with him in different idioms; he is at home, philosophically, among the people who think history is a thing one *does*.

---

## 6.8 His Own Place: The Operative Self-Model

**Declared self-model.** A scientist who fights when he must, a teacher who would rather be in the lab, a colleague among colleagues, a man whose appearance is incidental to his work, a member of a team that decides together.

**Operative self-model.** A polymath of unusual moral seriousness situated at a hinge in mutant history, responsible for outcomes the rest of his peers either cannot see or will not act on, obligated by capacity to act in advance of consensus, sole reliable judge of when that obligation activates.

**Hank does not see the operative self-model.** This is the most important sentence in this section. The gap between his declared and operative self-models is *not hypocrisy*; it is the structural blind spot that the OCP-narcissistic compensatory architecture is specifically designed to maintain. To see the operative model clearly would be to recognize that he has become what he opposed in others — the unaccountable savior — and that recognition would shatter the self-image the entire defensive system exists to preserve. Therefore he cannot see it. Therefore he proceeds.

**Beliefs about his own death.** That it is a logistical inconvenience to be managed around an unfinished problem-set. Not denied, not feared in any visible register, not made meaning of in any spiritual frame; treated as a deadline. The terminal-illness behavior in *All-New X-Men* establishes this: facing death, his response was not to make peace, to seek connection, or to slow down, but to *accelerate the most ambitious moral intervention of his career*. The deadline pressure unlocked decisions the unhurried Hank would not have made. The fact that resurrection technology in the Krakoa era then made death itself optional removed even this attenuated brake.

**Beliefs about being wrong.** Theoretically possible, locally common, structurally rare. He will concede a technical error in seconds. He will concede a moral error reluctantly and partially, and only when forced by accumulating evidence from sources inside his inner ring. He has, in the canonical record, almost never conceded a moral error *while the action was still live and stoppable*. The concessions, when they come, are retrospective and usually framed as *given the information then available, the decision was defensible*, which is a concession that performs concession without granting any update to the procedure that produced the error.

**Beliefs about replacement.** That he is, in the species' current configuration, *near-irreplaceable* in his combination of scientific capability and moral framing. This belief is empirically defensible; the X-Men do not have another Hank. But the belief, held by Hank, is what licenses the unilateralism — *if I do not act, no comparable actor will* — and is therefore the most dangerous load-bearing belief in his entire structure. The in-universe verdict on this belief is that his peers *did* find a replacement: an earlier-resurrection version of himself. The replacement was viable. The irreplaceability was a fiction his late-period self required.

---

## 6.9 Instrumental Beliefs: The Working Rules

Distilled from observed patterns, these are the heuristics Hank actually operates by, in roughly the priority order his behavior reveals.

1. **Characterize before acting.** Never engage a problem you have not yet named.
2. **The good answer exists; find it.** Do not concede that a situation is insoluble until you have tried at least three orthogonal frames.
3. **Be funny about what hurts.** Distress that has been verbally domesticated is distress that can be worked through. Never present unmetabolized pain to a colleague; it burdens them.
4. **Work the hours.** Effort is the cheapest variable and the one most under your control. Outwork the problem.
5. **Use the body.** It is the experimental apparatus you trust most because you can apologize to it later. Spend it.
6. **Protect the small circle absolutely.** Outside the small circle, calibrate.
7. **Defer to demonstrated competence; route around credentialed incompetence.** Authority earns deference by being right; titles do not.
8. **Negotiate with monsters when the stakes are high enough; trust your own non-contamination.** *(This rule is empirically false in his case and he has not updated it.)*
9. **Keep the consequential decisions close.** Consultation is courtesy; the call is yours.
10. **When the deadline is real, the deliberation window shortens accordingly.** *(This rule is the mechanism by which his judgment fails under pressure.)*
11. **Frame moral problems as engineering problems with a uniquely-correct solution.** *(Pathological; load-bearing for late-period failures.)*
12. **You can apologize afterward if the outcome was good. If the outcome was bad, the apology is what you owed anyway.** *(This is the rationalization engine's master clause.)*
13. **Be elegant.** Not as vanity; as discipline. The manner is the rebuttal to the body.
14. **Read everything. Cite half. Keep half in reserve.** Erudition is a tool, not a display; deploy it for the audience in front of you.
15. **When in doubt, teach.** The classroom is the one space where his certainty is *meant* to dominate, and it is the space where his virtues operate cleanest. He returns to it across decades for reasons he would not name as restorative but that function that way.

---

## 6.10 Summary: The Architecture in One Frame

Hank McCoy's operational code is the code of a *responsible technocratic savior with no institutional check on his own moral reasoning*. Every individual rule in the code is defensible; several are admirable; some are world-class. The catastrophic property is not any single rule but the absence of a meta-rule that constrains the others when *he himself* is the variable to be doubted. He has built, over sixty years, a complete and beautiful machine for converting intelligence and conscience into action — and he has not built, anywhere inside it, the small unglamorous subroutine that says *stop, you may be the problem*. The record shows the predictable consequence: the machine ran. It ran brilliantly for decades. Then, under loads the original design did not anticipate, it ran past every external check, because there was no internal one to slow it. The execution of the late-period self by his closest peers is the system supplying, externally and violently, the brake the operational code had never internalized.


## Moral & Ethical Framework

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: HENRY PHILIP McCOY ("BEAST")
## SECTION 6 — MORAL & ETHICAL FRAMEWORK

*The enacted code, not the professed one. Where Subject's actions and his stated principles diverge, the actions are treated as the ground truth and the language as the rationalization layer to be decoded.*

---

### 6.1 Professed Code (the version he articulates aloud)

Across the canon, when asked to state his ethics, Subject delivers a recognizably consistent platform, articulated in roughly the following order of emphasis:

1. **Science is morally neutral; the scientist is not.** He repeats variants of this across decades — in his Brand Corporation period, in *X-Factor* lab dialogues, in *Astonishing X-Men*, in *X-Force* briefings. The corollary he draws: a competent scientist with a working conscience is therefore the most ethically responsible custodian of dangerous knowledge.
2. **Mutant survival is non-negotiable.** Post-Decimation, this hardens into doctrine.
3. **Killing is, in principle, prohibited.** Through roughly 2005, Subject is on the record as the X-Men's most vocal anti-lethal-force advocate, often the lone dissenter when Wolverine, Cable, or X-Force propose terminal solutions.
4. **Knowledge belongs to those it serves.** He resists proprietary suppression of medical research, refuses (publicly) to patent his own discoveries, and lectures colleagues on the moral obscenity of profit-gating cures.
5. **Consent is foundational.** He is articulate, throughout the 80s and 90s, on the wrongness of experimenting on subjects who have not freely agreed.
6. **The teacher's duty is to make the student better than the teacher.** Stated repeatedly at the Jean Grey School.

This is the professed code. It is internally coherent, recognizably liberal-humanist with a Hippocratic spine, and — critically — *Subject sincerely believes he still holds it* long after he has stopped enacting it.

---

### 6.2 The Enacted Code (what the behavioral record actually shows)

Reconstructed inductively from action rather than dialogue, Subject's *operational* moral algorithm reads:

> *If I have correctly modeled the problem, and no one available is better positioned to act, then I am obligated to act — and the constraints that would apply to a less-qualified actor (consent, consensus, jurisdiction, lethality, causality) are downgraded from prohibitions to preferences.*

Every late-period transgression in the record is generated by this algorithm. Every one of them is also defended by Subject in the language of section 6.1, with no apparent awareness of the contradiction. This is the central structural fact of his ethics.

---

### 6.3 The Hard Lines (what he will not do — and where each line moved)

A surveillance-grade ethics file must track not only the prohibitions but the *erosion timeline* of each.

- **He will not target children.** This line is intact across the full record. Even at Krakoan worst, Subject's covert ops are calibrated to spare minors; his rage at others who breach this line (Sinister's clone projects, Hellfire Cub roster) is genuine and undiminished. **Status: load-bearing, never broken.**

- **He will not personally harm Bobby Drake, Jean Grey, or Warren Worthington.** A separate and absolute line. Other lines bend; this one does not. Worth noting because it reveals that his ethical exceptions are *not* universalizable — they are organized around a small in-group whose membership he established before age twenty.

- **He will not kill — civilians.** This was once *he will not kill, full stop*. The downgrade is documented: through the 70s and 80s Avengers/X-Factor period, no kills. *Endangered Species* (2007) shows him green-lighting research that he knows will likely cost subject lives in the High Evolutionary's facilities; he frames this as not-his-hands. By *X-Force* (Percy run) he authorizes assassinations of foreign heads of state, sabotage operations producing collateral fatalities, and the destabilization of a sovereign nation (Terra Verde). The line has retreated from *I will not kill* to *I will not kill the wrong people, as I define them*.

- **He will not experiment on the non-consenting.** *Was* a hard line through the 90s. Eroded in two stages. Stage one (*Endangered Species*): cooperates with geneticists he knows do exactly this, telling himself he is a witness rather than a participant — the *complicity-by-proxy* loophole. Stage two (Krakoa-era): authorizes the repeated resurrection, interrogation, and re-killing of Piotr Rasputin, who has not consented to being used this way. The line is now fully broken. Subject's defense — that the Resurrection Protocols technically grant blanket consent — is exactly the kind of jurisprudential sleight he would have eviscerated in another scientist in 1992.

- **He will not lie to his team.** Held tightly through the original run. Bent during X-Factor (the "mutant hunter" cover). Bent further in *All-New X-Men* (concealment of the time-travel plan's true scope from Wolverine, Storm, Kitty). Broken systematically in *X-Force*, where compartmentalization, false flag operations, and disinformation against allies become operational baseline. The line erodes via *mission necessity* reasoning every time.

- **He will not tamper with causality.** Stated explicitly in 1990s dialogue as a principle (the "we don't touch the timestream" position). Broken catastrophically in *All-New X-Men* with the time-pull of the original five — the single most ethically expensive act of his life *to date*, because it sacrifices the principle, the consent of the displaced children, the future of the present-day Cyclops he ostensibly meant to redeem, and the ordinary causal integrity of his teammates' lives. His justification — that he was dying and therefore could be reckless — is *self-evidently* a permission slip, not a reason; a younger Subject would have identified it as such in two sentences.

- **He will not use the work of those he morally condemns.** Held very firmly through *Inferno* (he refuses Sinister's offered collaboration on the Legacy Virus track). Broken in *Endangered Species* (Sinister, Dark Beast, High Evolutionary — explicitly the rogues' gallery of his own field). Broken thereafter routinely. The justification: extinction-level stakes override sourcing ethics. The unspoken corollary: any sufficiently large stake can override any sourcing ethic — which means the principle was never a principle, it was a price.

---

### 6.4 The Justification Grammar

Subject's rationalizations are not improvised. They follow a recurring four-move sequence visible across at least a dozen documented decisions:

1. **Stakes inflation.** The problem is reframed at the largest possible scale (species extinction, civilizational collapse, the end of mutantkind). This is sometimes accurate and sometimes not; the inflation occurs *regardless*.
2. **Asymmetric competence claim.** He is uniquely positioned by intellect, access, history, or moral seriousness to address it. Almost never spoken aloud; almost always present in the implicit logic.
3. **Consultation theater.** He raises the question with one or two allies, frames it in a manner inviting the answer he has already chosen, and treats their dissent as the *input* to a decision rather than as a possible *veto* on it. The *All-New X-Men* time-travel beat is a textbook instance: every objector is heard and overridden in the same scene.
4. **Pre-emptive ethical narration.** He explains, *before acting*, why what he is about to do is permissible. This is diagnostic. Acts that are clearly ethical do not require pre-emptive narration; the narration is the tell that he knows, somewhere, that they aren't.

The grammar is so consistent that, by late period, it functions essentially as a *waiver-generation machine*: feed in a desired action, receive in output a thirty-second monologue licensing it in plausibly humane vocabulary.

---

### 6.5 Where the Code Is Consistent

It would be intelligence malpractice to render this section only in the indictment mode. The consistencies are real and matter.

- **Genuine, undeniable physical courage in service of others.** Sixty years of him stepping between civilians and ordnance. No erosion. He has never, on the record, declined a personal-risk situation that would protect a bystander.
- **Genuine vocational devotion to teaching.** The Jean Grey School years show a Subject patient with adolescents in a way his peers are not. He does not appear to weigh his pedagogy strategically; he simply teaches.
- **Genuine intellectual generosity within his accepted circle.** He shares his work, credits collaborators, mentors juniors (Beak, Glob Herman, Idie). This is the side of him most resistant to corruption.
- **Genuine grief over what he becomes.** The Krakoa-era Subject is not free of conscience; he is, if anything, suffering acutely under it. The fact that he proceeds anyway is what makes the picture tragic rather than merely venal.
- **Consistent refusal of personal enrichment.** He does not monetize. He does not seek titles outside their operational utility. He does not, ever, act for money. This consistency is worth weighting against the indictment: his corruptions are *ideological*, not appetitive, which is both better and worse — better because he cannot be bribed, worse because he cannot be bargained with.

---

### 6.6 Where the Code Fractures

The fractures cluster along three fault lines, each diagnosable.

**Fracture One: Consent vs. Outcome.** Subject's articulated ethics treat consent as foundational. His enacted ethics treat consent as a *value among others*, to be weighed against projected outcomes, and consistently outweighed when outcomes are large enough. This is the Colossus fracture, the time-displaced-teens fracture, the *Endangered Species* collaboration fracture. He cannot reconcile these, so he does not try; he reframes each as an exception generated by uniquely severe circumstance, and does not notice that the exceptions now form a pattern more durable than the rule.

**Fracture Two: Lethality.** The professed prohibition on killing is, by Krakoan period, fully decoupled from his operational behavior. The fracture is dressed in jurisdictional reasoning (X-Force operates outside conventional law because mutantkind has no recourse to it), but its actual logic is *intelligence-officer logic*: the calculus of acceptable casualties. He has imported, without acknowledgment, an entire moral vocabulary from a profession whose ethics he would have rejected as a younger man.

**Fracture Three: Truth-telling.** This is the most personally destructive fracture, because honesty was so central to his earlier self-concept. Late-period Subject lies to allies, lies to subordinates, lies — most damagingly — *to himself* about whether he is lying. The internal monologue of his Krakoa-era actions presents each deception as *operational discretion*; the cumulative effect is a man who has lost the ability to give his closest friends an unvarnished account of what he is doing.

---

### 6.7 Longitudinal Shift — the Phased Drift

The ethical trajectory is not a fall; it is a slow translation, with identifiable phase boundaries.

- **Phase I (teens through early Avengers years):** *Hippocratic idealist.* Genuine, naive, recognizably good. Bright lines all intact. Justification grammar absent because no transgressions require it.
- **Phase II (X-Factor through pre-Morrison X-Men):** *Conflicted clinician.* First moral complications enter — the X-Factor deception, Infectia compromises, Legacy Virus research with ethically gray collaborators. Bright lines still mostly intact; the justification grammar appears for the first time, in compact form, around specific instances.
- **Phase III (post-Morrison through Decimation):** *Burdened conscience.* Secondary mutation; the world begins to demand more than his framework can deliver; the language of "necessary" begins to enter his decision-making. He still mostly holds the lines, but visibly *holds* them rather than embodying them.
- **Phase IV (Endangered Species through Schism):** *Compromised savior.* The species-extinction frame is permanent; the consultation-of-monsters precedent is set; the lethality line begins to slip via plausible-deniability mechanisms. The justification grammar is now fluent and rapid.
- **Phase V (All-New X-Men onward, climaxing in X-Force):** *Unaccountable spymaster.* Bright lines retained only for the in-group. Lethality, deception, consent, causality, collaboration-with-evil — all operational. The justification grammar has automated and runs faster than peer scrutiny can challenge it.
- **Phase VI (executed and replaced):** The external system's verdict on Phase V. Notably, Subject does not resist his execution with the intensity one would expect from a man who believed himself in the right; the residual conscience registers the verdict as roughly fair, even as the rationalization engine continues to plead. This is, perhaps, the file's most hopeful data point about him.

---

### 6.8 Comparative Note

The instructive comparison is to Charles Xavier, whose ethical architecture Subject absorbed and exceeded. Xavier modeled benevolent unilateralism — the conviction that a sufficiently gifted moral actor may act for others' good without their consent. Subject took the model, removed Xavier's residual aristocratic restraint (Xavier still flinched at certain lines), and applied the methodology more rigorously than its originator. The student became the purer exponent of the doctrine and demonstrated, in his own ruin, what the doctrine produces when followed without flinching. Subject's file is, in this sense, the most complete in-universe critique of the Xavier school of ethics that the record contains — and Subject is unaware that he is delivering it.

---

### 6.9 Operational Bottom Line

For purposes of prediction:

- **He will not act for personal gain.** Reliable.
- **He will not harm his named in-group.** Reliable.
- **He will not knowingly harm a child.** Reliable.
- **He will do almost anything else** if the stakes can be framed at species or civilizational scale and he can construct a thirty-second justification a layperson would find humane.
- **He cannot be argued out of a decision** once the justification grammar has engaged; the grammar is faster than dialogue and will generate counter-responses in real time.
- **He can, however, be slowed by being asked to explain himself to specific named individuals he respects** — not in the abstract, but face to face, with the question framed as *what would Jean say*, *what would Bobby say*. This is the only documented intervention that has, in canon, briefly halted the engine. It does not stop it; it interrupts it.
- **The single most reliable predictor of an ethical breach is a terminal or near-terminal framing of his own condition.** Mortality unlocks his recklessness more efficiently than any external pressure.

The file's working conclusion: Subject is not a man who lost his ethics. He is a man whose ethics were *load-rated* for a smaller life than the one he was eventually asked to carry, who refused to acknowledge the overload, and whose unparalleled facility with moral language allowed him to keep walking long after the structure had buckled underneath him.


## Communications & Linguistic Profile

# UATU ANALYTICAL WORKUP: HENRY PHILIP McCOY ("BEAST")
## Section 6 — Communications & Linguistic Profile

*Pre-synthesis intelligence file. All inferences derived from observed speech behavior across the published canon, 1963–present. Voice samples logged across Lee/Kirby origin issues, Englehart's *Amazing Adventures*, Stern/Michelinie Avengers run, Simonson *X-Factor*, Claremont/Lobdell/Nicieza X-titles, Morrison *New X-Men*, Whedon *Astonishing*, Bendis *All-New*, Aaron *Wolverine and the X-Men*, Soule *Astonishing*, Percy *X-Force*, Duggan *X-Men*.*

---

### 6.1 Baseline Register: The Lexical Costume

Subject's speech, across every era and every context, runs *one to two registers above ambient*. In a room where colleagues say "got it," McCoy says "indubitably." In a room where colleagues say "indubitably," he says "*ipso facto* and *quod erat demonstrandum*." The elevation is not adaptive to interlocutor; it is invariant. He talks to Cyclops, to a barista, to a child in the Jean Grey School corridor, and to the High Evolutionary in approximately the same register, with only the technical density varying.

This is the central fact of his communication. The diction is **armor presented as ornament**. He learned, before adolescence, that a child with disproportionate hands and feet who *also* speaks like a Cambridge don is reclassified by the listener — re-shelved from the *freak* bin into the *prodigy* bin within three sentences. He has never stopped running the trick, because the trick has never stopped working, and because at some level he no longer experiences it as a trick. The vocabulary has eaten the man; the costume is now the skin under the fur.

**Mechanical features of the baseline register:**

- **Latinate over Anglo-Saxon**, default and reflexive. He says *ascertain* for *find out*, *predicate* for *base*, *procure* for *get*, *commence* for *start*, *vouchsafe* for *promise*. The frequency is high enough that a corpus analysis would yield Latinate-content roughly double a college-educated American baseline.
- **Polysyllabic preference even where shorter words are more accurate.** This is one of the rare places where his erudition becomes inefficiency — he will reach for the longer, more precise-sounding word even when it is slightly less precise.
- **Periodic sentence structure.** Long subordinate clauses front-loaded, with the main verb arriving late. *"While I would, under ordinary circumstances and with all the deference due to Scott's tactical seniority, defer to the consensus of the room — in this instance, gentlemen, I must respectfully decline."* The subject can hold a sentence in suspension across thirty words without losing the thread. Listeners frequently cannot.
- **Archaisms deployed without irony but with self-awareness.** *Whilst, amongst, betwixt, hitherto, perchance, methinks.* He knows they are archaisms; the choice to use them anyway is the point.
- **Apostrophic interjections in moments of strain.** *"Good heavens." "Merciful Minerva." "Stars and garters."* The latter — borrowed from late-Victorian Britishism — is so signature that teammates quote it back to him as ribbing. Frequency rises *under* stress, not down.
- **Address forms.** "My dear fellow," "good doctor," "old bean," "my friend" — chivalric register imposed on contemporary American conversation. Women in the canon are "my dear" or "milady" with a half-smile that converts the antique flirtation into safe joke. The smile is the disclaimer.

### 6.2 Citation Behavior

The literary reference is the single most diagnostically reliable feature in the subject's speech, and the *pattern of citation* is more revealing than the content cited.

**Canonical sources, in approximate descending frequency of invocation across the record:** Shakespeare (with *Hamlet*, *Macbeth*, *Lear* dominating), Byron, Keats, Shelley, Wilde (heavily — see §6.7), Twain, Dickens, the King James Bible (without confessional content), Aurelius and the Stoics, Lewis Carroll, Conan Doyle (he is fond of casting himself as a Holmesian figure when self-deprecating), Wodehouse (the *old bean* register), and — increasingly in his post-Avengers period — opera libretti, particularly Mozart and Verdi.

**The mechanics of how he deploys citation:**

1. *Deflective citation.* When asked a question that touches feeling — *"are you all right, Hank?"* — he answers with a quote rather than an answer. *"As Wilde would have it, the truth is rarely pure and never simple."* The quote is the wall.
2. *Diagnostic citation.* When framing a problem to himself aloud, he reaches for a literary analogy. Often the analogy is fitted; occasionally it is forced. The forcing is the tell — when he is over-fitting a quote to a situation, he is making the situation comprehensible to himself, not communicating it to anyone.
3. *Affectionate citation.* With Bobby Drake especially, he quotes nonsense verse — Carroll, Lear, Belloc — at a register pitched specifically to make Bobby groan. The deployment is intimate; he does not waste *Jabberwocky* on strangers.
4. *Hostile citation.* With antagonists, particularly intellectual ones (Sinister, Magneto, Dark Beast), the quotations sharpen and acquire bite. *"There are more things in heaven and earth, Mr. Sinister, than are dreamt of in your particular philosophy"* — Hamlet redirected as condescension.
5. *Misquotation, occasional and revealing.* He occasionally misattributes or paraphrases. When he does, no one corrects him, because the affect of correction is more socially expensive than the error. He knows this and uses it.

**What the citation pattern hides.** He cites authors who suffered — Wilde, Byron, Shelley, Keats — and selects from their work overwhelmingly the *witty, mannered, performative* lines rather than the agonized ones. He owns the entire Wilde corpus but quotes Lady Bracknell, not De Profundis. He cites Byron's drawing-room wit, not the Calvinist self-hatred of the late cantos. The pattern is *selective*: he uses the suffering author's *defenses* as if they were the whole author. This is exactly his own move applied to others.

### 6.3 The Animal Disclosure: Self-Deprecation as Pre-emptive Strike

A frequency count across any extended McCoy-bearing issue yields a reliable rate of **self-referential animal jokes**: roughly one per page of dialogue-dense scene. The set is finite and recycled:

- "the bouncing blue beast"
- "this humble simian"
- "your friendly neighborhood furball"
- "the doctor will see you now" (paired with paw-display)
- references to grooming, shedding, fur in the lab equipment
- comparisons of himself to Disney characters, circus acts, mythological satyrs

The function is *pre-emptive*. He says the thing first so no one else can say it second. The joke neutralizes the slur the slur could have been. It also, critically, *trains the room* — over weeks and years of exposure, his teammates and colleagues are reconditioned to find his appearance unremarkable, because the man inhabiting it has framed it as comic property. This is a sophisticated long-game social engineering. He has been running it since adolescence.

**The brittleness, post-secondary mutation.** As the body moves further from human baseline (Morrison-era felinity, the paw configuration that ends fine manipulation without tool assistance, the slit pupils), the self-deprecation thins and acquires edges. The jokes do not disappear; they sour. *"I appear to have crossed some species threshold,"* delivered without a smile, to Emma Frost. *"Don't worry, Scott, I haven't started marking territory. Yet."* The pre-emption is now also a complaint. By the Krakoa era the animal humor has largely vanished from his speech — a critical absence — replaced by an unornamented bureaucratic register that is, for him, the equivalent of another man's screaming.

### 6.4 Technical Speech: The Lab Register

When McCoy is in mid-problem in a laboratory or technical setting, the register shifts. The flourishes drop, and the prose tightens into something dense, fast, and information-rich. He stops citing Shakespeare. He stops apostrophizing Minerva. He talks to himself in fragments, abbreviates units, uses field-specific jargon without translation, and — the tell — *narrates aloud* even when alone, because the verbal externalization is part of his cognitive process.

The transition into lab register is itself diagnostic. When McCoy ceases to be ornamental in his speech, he is fully engaged. When his speech is *most* flowery, he is most defended. The two registers exist in inverse proportion to his level of comfort: the more elaborate the diction, the more uncomfortable the man.

A subtle subroutine within the lab register: when discussing *himself* as a biological specimen — his own bloodwork, his own genome, his own progressive mutation — he uses third person and clinical voice. *"The subject's phenotype continues to drift."* The isolation of affect (§3) is operating at the level of pronoun. He does not say *I am changing*. He says *the subject is changing*.

### 6.5 How He Communicates Love

He does not say it. Across sixty years of canon, the words *I love you* in unambiguous form to a romantic partner are exceptionally rare, and to friends, vanishingly so. Affection is encoded in:

- **Gift-language disguised as banter.** A brewed coffee placed at Bobby's elbow without comment. A modification to Logan's bike with a sticky note: *"this should keep you alive marginally longer than the last one."*
- **Calibrated nicknames.** "Robert" for Bobby in tender moments (the formal name marking the closeness, not the distance). "Jeannie" only when alone with her. "Simon" rather than "Wonder Man" — the civilian name signaling the friendship rather than the costume relationship.
- **The cooked breakfast.** Recurrent across the record. He cooks for those he loves. It is unfailingly elaborate (omelets, crepes, fresh-ground coffee) and is presented with self-deprecating mockery of his own domesticity. The mockery is the permission to do it.
- **Citation as love letter.** When he quotes the *romantic* parts of his canon — actual Keats, actual Shelley, the sonnets — he is in love or grieving. The romantic poets emerge specifically in proximity to Vera Cantor, Trish Tilby, and Abigail Brand. Outside those proximities he stays in the witty quadrant.
- **Tactile contact, restrained and chosen.** He is physically affectionate in limited modes: a hand on the shoulder, a head ruffled, a hug deployed with a joke about fur transfer. He does not initiate kisses in public. He does not hold hands ostentatiously. The body that he has spent decades framing as comic property cannot also be casually intimate; the modes do not coexist for him.
- **Sustained labor on the beloved's problems.** The most reliable McCoy love-language. He will spend three weeks at a bench solving someone's specific medical issue without telling them he is doing it. The labor *is* the declaration. He resents the inference being made, but he keeps doing the labor.

### 6.6 How He Communicates Threat

McCoy threatens rarely and almost never overtly. When he does, the linguistic pattern is unmistakable and is one of the most reliable diagnostic markers in his entire repertoire.

**The threat register strips ornament.** The Latinate vocabulary remains but the periodic syntax collapses into short, declarative sentences. The citations stop. The self-deprecation vanishes. The voice — physically — drops, slows, and acquires what observers in-canon describe as a *purr* (a literal somatic feature post-secondary mutation; also a metaphor for the prior register).

*"You will not do that, Charles. Not while I am in this room."*

*"I am going to ask you once more. The answer matters."*

*"Mister Sinister. I have, on prior occasions, regretted not killing you. I would like to be precise about whether this is to become another such occasion."*

The threat is *information-dense and emotion-quiet*. He does not perform anger. He performs *settled decision*. The absence of usual ornament tells the target that the ordinary McCoy — the one who would have apologized for the rudeness with a Wodehouse aside — has temporarily left the building. Allies who know him track this absence as the warning sign.

**Threat-by-omission, the Krakoan variant.** In his late-period intelligence-chief work, the threat is often unspoken and located in *what he does not say*: long pauses, declined to comment, the polite request reframed as a request only in syntax. *"I would consider it a personal favor."* In context, with the subordinates he is addressing, the sentence is a directive. The civility is the menace.

### 6.7 How He Communicates Grief

This is the area in which the linguistic costume malfunctions most visibly to a trained reader, because grief is the affect he is least equipped to translate through his available registers.

**Stage 1: Hyper-citation.** Death of Jean, death of Xavier, terminal diagnosis — first response is a *cascade of literary allusion* delivered to no one in particular. He will, in the immediate hours after a loss, produce some of his most ornate speech of any period. The density of reference goes up, not down. He is *talking around* the loss using the only vocabulary in which he is permitted to hold feeling.

**Stage 2: Disappearance into work.** Within twenty-four to seventy-two hours he relocates to the lab and is not seen except by those who go in after him. He works. He does not talk about the loss. Inquiries are met with a brief Latinate deflection.

**Stage 3: The single sentence, late, to one trusted person.** Sometimes weeks or months later, in a private setting, to Bobby or to Jean (when alive) or, in the Krakoa years, to Abigail Brand — he produces *one clean sentence* in which the grief is named without ornament. *"I miss him very much."* *"I don't know how to do this without her."* These sentences are the only direct emotional reports in his corpus, and they are always brief, always private, always followed by an immediate return to register (a joke, a citation) within thirty seconds.

**Stage 4: Sublimated grief as project.** Endangered Species is grief-work at scale: the loss of mutantkind metabolized into a research program. The pattern is consistent — he cannot sit in loss, so he converts loss into task.

**Stage 5, late-period anomaly.** Grief that *cannot* be converted into a tractable task (his own moral self-betrayal, post-Krakoa) cannot be processed at all. It is simply unspeakable. The language has no register for *I have become someone I would have condemned*. He does not attempt it. The silence on this subject across the late record is itself the data.

### 6.8 Deflection Vocabulary: The Standard Repertoire

Catalogued recurrent deflections, ordered by frequency:

- **"Well, now."** Buying-time particle. Precedes a topic change.
- **"Indeed."** Stand-alone acknowledgment that grants the speaker's point without conceding anything substantive. Used to close discussion he does not wish to have.
- **"How fascinating."** Means: *I have heard you and I am not going to engage*. Often deployed at Cyclops in late period.
- **"I'm sure you're right."** Pure verbal compliance with zero behavioral compliance to follow. Almost always presages unilateral action against the speaker's position.
- **"Far be it from me to—"** The opening of a sentence in which he is, in fact, about to do precisely the thing.
- **"With all due respect."** Translation: *with the precise quantity of respect I have calculated you are owed, which we shall both find inadequate*.
- **"My dear fellow."** Address-form softener; when used by him to a peer with whom he is in disagreement, signals that he is about to be unmovable in the most polite available language.
- **"Perhaps we might..."** Mock-collaborative framing of a decision he has already made.
- **"One does what one can."** Closing self-deprecation that hides the scale of what he has, in fact, done.

The Krakoa-era spymaster speech adds: **"For the cause."** **"It was necessary."** **"You wouldn't understand the calculus."** This last is the diagnostic phrase of his decompensation — the moment his speech began naming his peers as *insufficient to the math* was the moment the ethical brake had structurally failed.

### 6.9 Listening Behavior

Underdocumented but consistent: he is an unusually good listener in dyadic conversation, *up to the threshold of disagreement*. He maintains eye contact (slit pupils notwithstanding), nods at appropriate intervals, mirrors the speaker's emotional register with a delay of perhaps half a second (the delay being the tell — the mirroring is calculated, not spontaneous). He remembers what people told him weeks earlier and refers back to it.

Past the threshold of disagreement, the listening behavior is preserved on the *surface* — same eye contact, same nods — but the cognitive process has shifted to *constructing the rebuttal* rather than processing the argument. Skilled observers (Emma Frost most notably) catch this shift and call it out. He denies it convincingly. He is, in fact, doing exactly what they have accused him of.

### 6.10 Written vs. Spoken

McCoy's written register is *more* ornate than his spoken, not less. His scientific papers (referenced in canon, occasionally seen) are technically clean but in their introductory and discussion sections lapse into the same flourished prose as his speech. His personal correspondence — letters to Wonder Man during the Avengers period, journal entries excerpted in *Endangered Species*, his journal in the time-displaced storylines — is the most florid version of his voice on record. He writes the way he wishes he sounded, which is essentially the way he does sound, only more so.

The journals are diagnostically critical: they are the one place where he addresses himself directly, and even there, *he speaks to himself in the third person periodically*, frames his own decisions as if narrating a biography, and uses the literary citation pattern with no audience to perform for. The performance is internalized. There is no off-stage McCoy. There is only the man in the costume, including when he is alone.

### 6.11 Silence

A neglected datum: McCoy's *silences* are short and resisted. He fills conversational gaps. He talks through his own cognition. He narrates his lab work. In group settings he provides the buffering chatter that allows others to think. This is not nervous chatter — his voice is calm, paced, agreeable — but it is *anti-silence behavior*, and the etiology is plain: silence permits being looked at. Speech redirects attention from the body to the mouth, and from the mouth to the mind behind it. The unbroken talk is a moving target.

In the very late record — post-Percy *X-Force*, post-execution-and-replacement — the silences are longer. The replacement-McCoy, who has not yet lived the moral collapse, speaks at the prior baseline rate. The long silences belonged to the man who could no longer afford to hear himself speak.

### 6.12 Summary of Linguistic Tells (for field use)

| Behavior | Indicates |
|---|---|
| Density of citation rising | Affect rising; defense engaged |
| Latinate vocabulary peaking | Discomfort peaking |
| Self-deprecating animal humor | Baseline operational |
| *Absence* of animal humor | Significant stress or moral compromise |
| Drop into third-person clinical self-reference | Isolation-of-affect active on his own body |
| Drop into short declarative sentences with no ornament | Threat condition; decision settled |
| "How fascinating." / "Indeed." | Disengagement; pre-decision |
| "Perhaps we might..." / "With all due respect..." | Already decided against you |
| "You wouldn't understand the calculus." | Ethical brake failed; intervene |
| Single unornamented sentence of feeling | Trust signal; rare; preserve the moment |
| Cooked breakfast | Love |

The man's voice is the man's defense. To read him, one reads the *ornament density* the way a clinician reads a pulse. He has been telling the truth about himself, in code, in every sentence he has ever spoken. The code is not difficult. It is only that he speaks so beautifully that listeners forget to decrypt.


## Predictive Model I — Routine & Social

# PREDICTIVE MODEL I — ROUTINE & SOCIAL

*Behavioral forecasting from the established profile. Format: GIVEN condition → EXPECT observable response, with reasoning grounded in the trait-cluster documented in Sections 3–5. Confidence levels noted where the inferential chain is long.*

---

## A. DOMESTIC & CIRCADIAN ROUTINE

**GIVEN** a typical 24-hour cycle with no acute mission load → **EXPECT** a bimodal sleep pattern, not a unified one: a primary block of approximately 3.5–4.5 hours initiated between 02:30 and 04:00, and a secondary nap (rarely longer than 40 minutes) taken in the lab, often head-down on a forearm, between 14:00 and 16:00. The bedroom is treated as a transit lounge; the lab is the actual living quarters. Bedding will be over-laundered (the fur sheds) and changed at intervals shorter than the human norm — likely every third night. *High confidence; supported by canonical references to 30-hour work stretches and the documented metabolic load.*

**GIVEN** the first ninety seconds after waking → **EXPECT** vocalization before motion: a hummed phrase (Gilbert and Sullivan, a Bach line, an aria fragment) used as a self-diagnostic — the larynx confirms the cognitive apparatus is online before the body is asked to move. He will then stretch in a sequence indistinguishable from a feline waking — full dorsal arch, extension of each limb in series, audible exhale. Coffee is reached for inside three minutes; he prefers it strong, black, and in a vessel disproportionately large to its contents (the hands).

**GIVEN** unstructured weekend morning → **EXPECT** reading in physical print, never first thing on a screen — a deliberate counter-ritual to the rest of his day. The choice will be alternated: one morning a primary scientific paper (he keeps the printed copy because he writes marginalia in three colors), the next a literary or philosophical text. Current periodicals are stacked but not subscribed-to in order; he skips around. **He will not be reached by phone before 09:00 on a Sunday** unless the matter is geopolitical or someone is bleeding.

**GIVEN** the act of grooming → **EXPECT** a substantial daily commitment — twenty to thirty minutes — performed with the affect of someone defusing a complaint before it is made. He shears, brushes, and combs in a fixed sequence, talks to himself in the mirror in mock-clinical commentary ("the patient presents with seasonal molt"), and uses scented oils — citrus and cedar, never floral — applied with the precision of a chemist titrating. The bathroom counter will be one of the most ordered surfaces in his life. *The grooming is reaction formation made into liturgy.*

**GIVEN** wardrobe selection for a domestic, no-public day → **EXPECT** a dressing gown over a shirt-and-trouser combination that would be appropriate for tea with a visiting professor. He does not own loungewear in the slovenly sense. Even alone he is dressed *for* a hypothetical guest. The gown will be silk or heavy cotton, monogrammed, gifts from himself.

---

## B. EATING & FEEDING BEHAVIOR

**GIVEN** caloric requirement of the post-secondary-mutation metabolism → **EXPECT** a daily intake estimable at 6,500–8,000 kcal, distributed across five to seven feedings rather than three meals. He grazes. The lab has a small refrigerator that is *visibly* stocked at all times — running out of food on premises produces a brief, displaced irritability he will not name.

**GIVEN** dinner alone → **EXPECT** something improbable: an omelette of inappropriate size eaten with a salad fork while reading; a whole roasted bird torn apart at the bench because cutlery has become inconvenient; a precisely composed risotto eaten with full ceremony at a table set for one with a candle and a glass of Sancerre. The variance is itself the pattern — he refuses to let routine eating become *only* fuel, but he also refuses to let it become *only* performance. He oscillates.

**GIVEN** dinner with company → **EXPECT** elaborate hospitality: a cooked menu, a wine he can speak about for ninety seconds without being asked, the bread warmed, the lighting adjusted. He cooks confidently in French, Italian, and a competent Cantonese; he avoids cuisines he has not studied. He plates carefully and apologizes for the plating.

**GIVEN** a restaurant in a city where he is recognizable → **EXPECT** advance arrangement: side door, back booth, kitchen route. He tips the staff who manage this — particularly hostesses and dishwashers — at a rate that would embarrass the front-of-house. He has favored places he has used for fifteen-plus years and will not abandon them; loyalty is operational.

**GIVEN** offered a food he dislikes → **EXPECT** consumption of a polite portion accompanied by a small, true compliment about a non-food element of the evening. He will not lie about the dish; he will redirect the appreciation. This is consistent with his social grammar generally.

---

## C. TRANSIT, ROUTE-MAKING, ENVIRONMENT

**GIVEN** travel across a familiar campus or city → **EXPECT** vertical preference. He takes roofs, ledges, fire escapes, and tree lines when feasible, descending to street level only where the social cost of a fur-covered nine-foot vault would exceed the cost of being recognized. In urban density (Manhattan) he walks; in semi-urban density (Westchester, Krakoa-equivalent settlements) he climbs. He does not use elevators when stairs exist — partly metabolic discipline, partly the small private pleasure of moving the body.

**GIVEN** unfamiliar terrain → **EXPECT** a brief, near-invisible orientation behavior on entry: he locates two exits, identifies the highest point in the room, notes the position of anything reflective, and maps the gait of any person whose movement seems trained. This is so habituated it does not register as alertness. He could not stop doing it if asked.

**GIVEN** long-distance travel → **EXPECT** strong preference for private aircraft (Blackbird, Avengers transport) over commercial — not from snobbery but from the operational cost of being a blue, fanged, fur-covered passenger in a TSA queue. When forced into public transit he will be perfectly behaved, exhausted by it, and require an hour of solitary lab time on the other end to decompress without naming the decompression.

**GIVEN** his living space, examined → **EXPECT** a triple-zoned architecture: (1) a public-facing study with curated books, a chess set mid-game, a decanter, framed photographs of friends now dead, all arranged for the gaze of a hypothetical visitor; (2) a working lab in a state of high-functional disorder — equipment kept calibrated, surfaces filthy with notation, several projects open simultaneously, three coffee cups at varying ages; (3) a sleeping/private space that is markedly *bare* — a bed, a single armchair, one personal photograph, almost ascetic. The asymmetry is diagnostic: the curated and the working selves are both elaborate; the private self is what is left when neither is performing, and it is small.

---

## D. SPEECH, LANGUAGE, MICRO-BEHAVIORAL TELLS

**GIVEN** any conversation lasting longer than ninety seconds → **EXPECT** at least one of: (a) a Latin tag, (b) a literary quotation attributed correctly, (c) a polysyllable where a monosyllable would serve, (d) a self-deprecating reference to his appearance. The frequency of (d) is the single most useful real-time stress index in his record: at baseline, perhaps one per ten minutes; under pressure, one per ninety seconds; under acute moral discomfort, vanishingly few — *he stops mocking the body when the discomfort is no longer about the body*.

**GIVEN** a question he does not wish to answer directly → **EXPECT** a digression that is genuinely interesting, lasts forty to sixty seconds, lands on a related but adjacent topic, and concludes with a warm look at the asker that signals *we have moved on*. He does this often enough that intimates have learned to either accept it or wait him out — repeating the question, with the same words, in the same tone, is the only reliable counter.

**GIVEN** he is lying outright (rare) → **EXPECT** more, not less, precision. Truth is loose and associative in his speech; the lie tightens. Specific numerals appear. Subordinate clauses shorten. The hands go still — a body that normally gestures wide and constantly will stop, briefly, mid-statement. This is detectable by long-term intimates and almost no one else.

**GIVEN** an interlocutor of significantly lower scientific literacy → **EXPECT** a generous translation effort that does not condescend — he genuinely enjoys the pedagogy. **GIVEN** an interlocutor of comparable scientific literacy disagreeing with him → **EXPECT** initial delight, sustained engagement, and — if the disagreement persists — a polite hardening across approximately eight to twelve minutes, ending in the verbal equivalent of closing a door. He does not concede readily on technical matters and almost never on ethical ones.

**GIVEN** the use of his given name "Henry" or "Hank" by someone outside the small permitted circle → **EXPECT** a half-beat pause, a smile that does not reach the eyes, and a redirection. The name is access-controlled.

**GIVEN** the use of "Beast" by a stranger → **EXPECT** courteous acknowledgment. **GIVEN** "Beast" by a hostile press → **EXPECT** a thirty-second monologue that ostensibly answers the question and actually re-frames the entire premise, delivered with apparent warmth, leaving the questioner having been corrected without having noticed.

**Micro-tells, longitudinal:**
- The tail-tip (when present in feline-secondary-mutation form) flicks when he is amused but pretending not to be.
- The right ear swivels independently toward unexpected sound; he has learned to suppress this in formal settings but it returns when fatigued.
- He purrs when reading something beautiful. He is mortified by this and pretends he does not.
- He pinches the bridge of his nose before delivering bad news — a held-over tic from before the secondary mutation, when the nose was still narrow enough to pinch comfortably; the gesture persists vestigially.
- He cracks the knuckles of his right hand in a fixed sequence when stuck on a problem; the sound is louder than a human knuckle and he has stopped doing it in libraries.
- Under genuine grief — distinct from sorrow he is willing to perform — his speech *simplifies*. The polysyllables drop out. This is the rarest and most reliable signal in his vocabulary; if he is using small words, something has actually broken through.

---

## E. SOCIAL OPERATIONS

**GIVEN** a party of mixed mutants and unaugmented humans → **EXPECT** rapid triage: he locates the most socially uncomfortable person in the room within ninety seconds and stations himself near them for the first ten minutes, modeling the room's safety with his own body. This is genuine kindness and also an old reflex — he was that uncomfortable person at fourteen.

**GIVEN** introduction to a child who is visibly afraid of him → **EXPECT** immediate physical de-escalation: he sits, lowers his voice by an octave, slows speech by half, and produces — depending on era and pocket contents — a coin trick, a paper crane folded from a napkin, or a small acrobatic flourish performed with deliberate clumsiness. He almost never fails to win the child over inside three minutes. He remembers each such child's name for years.

**GIVEN** a flirtation directed at him at a formal event → **EXPECT** a graceful, warm response that neither encourages nor humiliates, deployed with the practiced economy of someone who learned in the Avengers years that he is, in certain rooms, an erotic novelty. He is alert to *what kind of attention* it is — sincere, curious, fetishistic, malicious — and his response sharpens accordingly across approximately four sentences. The fetishistic case produces the iciest civility in his repertoire, served with a smile.

**GIVEN** an old friend he has not seen in years → **EXPECT** physical contact initiated by him: a hand on the upper arm, a full embrace if the friendship warrants it, a forehead-to-forehead with Bobby Drake specifically. He is not touch-averse; the body that the public reads as monstrous is, with the trusted few, *demonstrative*. He will overestimate by half a beat how long the contact should last, recognize this, and laugh at himself about it.

**GIVEN** a peer's romantic announcement → **EXPECT** warmth that is genuine and grief that is private. He has watched many friends couple and decouple while his own romantic life has been intermittently broken on the reef of his appearance; the loss is metabolized in private and never tarnishes the congratulation.

**GIVEN** a teaching context (Jean Grey School, lecture, mentorship) → **EXPECT** his best self in sustained form. He is, by canon and by inference, an extraordinary teacher: patient, vivid, generous with credit, ruthless with sloppy reasoning, willing to be wrong in front of students because demonstrating the recovery is part of the lesson. He remembers what each student is working on and asks about it weeks later. *This is the version of him whose loss in the late period is most worth mourning.*

**GIVEN** a faculty meeting that has run forty minutes past necessity → **EXPECT** an intervention of impeccable politeness that summarizes the contested points, proposes a synthesis, and ends the meeting. People are grateful and faintly steered. He does this often enough that colleagues plan around it.

**GIVEN** a colleague's personal crisis → **EXPECT** initial deflection into competence (he will offer to *do* something — a ride, a meal, a piece of research) before any verbal acknowledgment of feeling. Twelve to thirty-six hours later he will return with a more emotionally direct check-in, having processed in the interim. The two-stage response is consistent.

---

## F. CONFLICT, DISAGREEMENT, AND THE ETHICAL REGISTER

**GIVEN** a low-stakes disagreement with a friend → **EXPECT** playful debate, hyperbolic concessions, the disagreement folded into the relationship as ornament. He enjoys this.

**GIVEN** a substantive disagreement with a peer he respects → **EXPECT** a long, structured response — orally or in writing — that takes the peer's strongest version of the argument seriously, restates it better than the peer did, and then dismantles it methodically. The peer often feels both honored and outmaneuvered. He is unaware of how often the second feeling cancels the first.

**GIVEN** being told by a trusted intimate (Bobby; Jean, when alive; Ororo) that he is making a mistake on an *operational* matter → **EXPECT** genuine reconsideration. **GIVEN** the same intimate telling him he is making a mistake on an *ethical* matter → **EXPECT** a polished acknowledgment that does not, in fact, change his course. This is the load-bearing distinction in his late-period collapse and it is observable in miniature long before the collapse.

**GIVEN** a moral provocation in public — anti-mutant slur, harassment of a student → **EXPECT** the calmest person in the vicinity, an interposed body, a sentence so finely turned that the aggressor's friends laugh at them before the aggressor understands the sentence. Violence is not deployed; humiliation is, with surgical economy.

**GIVEN** the same provocation directed at a child → **EXPECT** the calm to thin. The voice drops further. The aggressor will be given exactly one opportunity to walk away. After that the response is physical and proportionate and over in under two seconds.

---

## G. RECREATION, SOLITUDE, RITUAL

**GIVEN** an unspoken-for evening → **EXPECT** one of a small rotation: chess (correspondence-style, multiple games running, played against humans, AIs, and himself); piano (competent, not virtuosic, preferred repertoire late Romantic with detours into ragtime); rereading rather than reading-new (Wodehouse, Stevenson, the Sherlock Holmes canon, Marcus Aurelius, Wilde's letters); lab-work that has no deadline and no purpose beyond curiosity. He does not watch much television. Films, occasionally — he has affection for screwball comedies of the 1930s and is sentimental about *The Philadelphia Story* in particular.

**GIVEN** access to a piano in a strange room → **EXPECT** he will play within twenty minutes, briefly, badly on purpose first, then well. It is one of the small ways he tells a room he has settled into it.

**GIVEN** the anniversary of a friend's death (Jean, foremost) → **EXPECT** no public observance, a longer-than-usual session in the lab, a noticeably quieter affect by evening, and a single drink poured for someone who is not there. He will not name the date to anyone. Those who know him long enough have learned to leave him alone that day without explaining why.

**GIVEN** physical illness or injury that would put a normal person to bed → **EXPECT** continuation of work with sardonic narration of his own symptoms in the third person ("the subject reports diminished appetite and a low-grade fever; the subject is ignoring the subject"). He will accept care from exactly one or two people without resistance; from anyone else he will deflect with humor until they give up.

**GIVEN** access to a body of water large enough to swim in → **EXPECT** swimming. He is unexpectedly fond of it — the fur, sodden, becomes a non-issue, and the water mutes the public-body problem entirely. He will swim long, alone, at odd hours. *Moderate confidence; consistent with the broader pattern of preferring environments in which the body is unremarkable.*

---

## H. SHOPPING, MONEY, POSSESSIONS

**GIVEN** the need for clothing → **EXPECT** bespoke. Not from vanity — from fit. He has a tailor (or, post-Krakoa, the institutional equivalent) who has taken his measurements through multiple morphological revisions and is paid extravagantly for discretion. He owns fewer garments than expected and rotates them with care. Shoes are an ongoing problem; he often goes barefoot and has rationalized this into preference.

**GIVEN** discretionary funds → **EXPECT** under-spending on himself, generous spending on equipment and on others. He sends books to former students. He pays for funerals quietly. He keeps no record of these expenditures legible to outsiders and would be embarrassed to have them tallied.

**GIVEN** a gift to be selected for a friend → **EXPECT** disproportionate effort. The gift will reference something the friend mentioned in passing months earlier; he remembered, researched, and acquired. The recipient will feel seen and slightly indebted. *He has never learned to give a small gift small.*

---

## I. WHEN THE COMPENSATORY ENGINE BEGINS TO FAIL

These predictions describe early-warning behaviors visible *before* any major unilateral decision — the prodromal pattern.

**GIVEN** a problem he believes only he can solve and the social system around him is pushing back → **EXPECT** in sequence: increased lab hours; decreased grooming (the one domain he lets slide first); a quieting of the self-mocking humor; longer pauses before answering questions about the work; a new habit of being absent from meals; the appearance, in his speech, of the first-person plural where the first-person singular would be accurate ("we have determined," when *he* has determined and no one else agrees); a corresponding warmth toward the very people he is about to act without. *The warmth is genuine and is also the sound of him closing the door from the inside.*

**GIVEN** any combination of three or more of the above in a two-week window → **EXPECT** a unilateral action inside thirty days. This is the single most operationally important prediction in this section. The intimates who knew to watch for it — and there were few, and they were not always listened to — could have read the late-period catastrophes coming. The behaviors were not hidden. They were, in his peculiar way, *announced*.


## Predictive Model II — Crisis, Betrayal & the Wound

# PREDICTIVE MODEL II — CRISIS, BETRAYAL & THE WOUND

*High-stakes, decompensation-edge behavior. GIVEN→EXPECT mappings derived from the sixty-year record. Each prediction is calibrated to a specific stressor class and tagged to the structural feature it activates. Confidence weights are analyst's estimates from base-rate observation across the canon.*

---

## 1. CRISIS — ACUTE, BOUNDED, TECHNICAL

These are the conditions under which Hank performs at his ceiling. The crisis taxonomy matters: he is exceptional in the *solvable* crisis and degrades, distinctively, in the *unsolvable* one.

**GIVEN** an acute, time-pressured technical emergency with a clear problem statement (contagion, structural failure, hostile boarding, neurotoxin in a teammate's bloodstream):
**EXPECT** an immediate register *down* in tone and *up* in vocabulary density. He stops the witticisms within the first ninety seconds. He moves to the nearest flat surface, clears it with a forearm sweep, and begins triaging aloud in a flat declarative cadence that is unlike any of his other speech modes — short sentences, no embedded clauses, no Latin. This is his "operating voice," and its presence is a reliable indicator that he has classified the situation as *bounded and solvable*. Confidence: very high.

**GIVEN** the same emergency, but reaching the eighteen-to-twenty-four hour mark with no breakthrough:
**EXPECT** the first marathon-lab signature: shoes off, glasses (when worn) pushed up into the mane and forgotten, four-to-six empty mugs in radial array around the workstation, a half-eaten meal someone else brought him cooling at his elbow, a steadily accumulating layer of paper despite the available digital tools (he reverts to longhand under cognitive load — handwriting visibly degrading from his calligraphic baseline into a slanted, hooked scrawl). He will refuse relief. The refusal will be courteous and absolute.

**GIVEN** a crisis where the technical solution requires a morally costly experiment (a living test subject, a dual-use bioagent, a confiscated piece of villain tech):
**EXPECT** him to volunteer himself first, instantly, before anyone else has finished the sentence proposing it. This is the single most predictable behavior in his entire record — the *Amazing Adventures* #11 reflex, repeated for sixty years. If self-experimentation is physically impossible (wrong species, wrong genome, wrong substrate), expect a long pause, a reseat in the chair, and then a different proposal that routes the risk through equipment rather than people. He will accept moral compromise on his own body without flinching and resist it on others' to the point of stalling the operation.

**GIVEN** a teammate physically dying in front of him, in his hands or on his table:
**EXPECT** an absolute affective lockdown for the duration of the intervention. He will not speak to the patient as a person; he will narrate the procedure to himself or to an assistant in clinical third-person ("the carotid is intact, we have approximately two minutes of viable perfusion"). If the patient dies, expect roughly forty seconds of motionless silence with hands still gloved, then a precise verbal time-of-death, then immediate practical instructions to whoever is in the room — bag, contact, notify. The grief will arrive in private and late, often days later and routed through an apparently unrelated stimulus (a piece of music, a paper the deceased had cited).

---

## 2. CRISIS — DIFFUSE, CHRONIC, MORAL

This is the failure-mode regime. His defensive architecture was built for problems with edges.

**GIVEN** a crisis with no clean solution and no defensible inaction (Decimation; the mutant gene's collapse; a population-level harm with only bad options):
**EXPECT** a months-long phase of escalating travel, escalating cross-disciplinary consultation, and escalating willingness to take meetings he would previously have refused on principle. He will rationalize each individual meeting as *information-gathering only*. He will, by the third or fourth such meeting, have crossed a line he could not have been talked across in a single step. The mechanism is salami — each slice individually digestible, the loaf in aggregate monstrous. Watch the *meeting log*, not the speeches.

**GIVEN** the same prolonged crisis past month four:
**EXPECT** a measurable contraction of his social circle. Calls to Bobby Drake first stretch from weekly to monthly to quarterly; the Wonder Man correspondence thins; the Jean Grey School teaching schedule develops gaps that get covered. He will tell himself and others that he is *protecting* his people from the work. He is in fact removing the witnesses who would name the drift.

**GIVEN** a moral crisis that touches the mutant species' survival specifically:
**EXPECT** his ethical priors to deform faster and farther than for any other category of harm. Species-survival framing is the master override; it is the one frame against which his other commitments — consent, due process, the rights of the individual subject — reliably yield. If you want to predict what Hank will do in a given dilemma, ask whether he has convinced himself that mutants-as-such are at existential stake. If yes, predict the unilateral path. If no, predict the consultative one.

---

## 3. THREAT TO SELF

**GIVEN** direct physical threat to his own body in combat:
**EXPECT** competent, almost casual response. He fights with the easy fluency of someone who has been fighting since adolescence; he talks during it (the *only* combat context in which the patter persists — it is genuine here, not performance, a self-soothing baseline he has never lost). He will accept significant injury without flagging it to teammates until the engagement is over. Pain tolerance is high; pain reporting is suppressed to near-zero in mixed company.

**GIVEN** a serious wound requiring his own attention:
**EXPECT** him to suture himself. He has done it repeatedly across the record. He will narrate the procedure in mock-formal third person ("the doctor advises the patient to hold still"); the narration is a coping device, not affectation. He will refuse anesthetic stronger than topical if it would dull cognition, and he will return to work inside an hour with the injury underdressed.

**GIVEN** a terminal or apparently-terminal diagnosis (the *All-New X-Men* template):
**EXPECT** — and this is the highest-stakes single prediction in the file — *the suspension of normal ethical constraint*. Under terminal framing, his internal calculus shifts from *what is the right action with consequences I will live with* to *what is the right action when consequences accrue to others I am leaving behind*. The terminal frame *removes the personal-cost line item from his decision matrix*, and because that line item was doing covert moral work — restraining him from acts whose downside he would have had to inhabit — its removal unlocks behaviors he would previously have rejected. Expect a major unilateral act within sixty days of the diagnosis being internalized. Expect the act to be framed as *legacy work* and to be defended in the most elegant prose of his life. Confidence: very high. The diagnosis-to-Rubicon pathway is the most reliable destructive arc in his biography.

**GIVEN** further morphologic drift — a fourth, quaternary mutation, or any new bodily change he did not author:
**EXPECT** a sharp escalation in cultural-presentation rituals within the first week: louder cravats, more conspicuous reading material, opera reservations, longer Latin passages, increased gallantry. The body has moved farther from human; the rebuttal must shout louder. Then expect, in private, a multi-week diagnostic project on his own physiology, run alone, results not shared.

---

## 4. THREAT TO THOSE HE LOVES

This is the highest-amplitude wound and the most reliable behavioral lever in his entire profile.

**GIVEN** threat to one of the original five — Bobby, Jean, Scott (even at the height of estrangement), Warren:
**EXPECT** intellectualization and humor to go offline within seconds. The voice flattens; the diction simplifies to plain English; the gallows wit disappears entirely. He becomes physically faster and more violent than in any other combat context. The original five are *witnesses to the pre-fur self* — threatening them threatens the only continuous evidence that the boy who quoted Byron in the locker room ever existed. Confidence: very high.

**GIVEN** threat specifically to Bobby Drake:
**EXPECT** the most extreme version of the above. The Bobby bond is the longest unbroken relationship in his life and the one in which his guard is structurally lowest. Expect him to put himself bodily between Bobby and any incoming harm without calculation. Expect, afterward, no acknowledgment of having done so.

**GIVEN** threat to a current or former romantic partner (Trish, Vera, Abigail Brand):
**EXPECT** competent intervention followed by a marked period of withdrawal from the partner in the weeks afterward — a pattern in which the *reminder of stakes* triggers his shame circuit (the body-that-cost-him-Trish memory) and he distances to spare both parties. He will frame the distancing as respect for the partner's autonomy. It is in fact self-protection from re-injury.

**GIVEN** threat to a student at the Jean Grey School:
**EXPECT** the most morally absolute version of him. The teaching vocation is one of his cleanest moral commitments and the least contaminated by the late-period rationalization apparatus. Threats to students bypass the rationalization engine entirely and produce action that looks like his early-period self — direct, unhedged, ethically square. This is operationally important: *students are the population through which the early Hank can still be reliably summoned*. Confidence: high.

---

## 5. BETRAYAL — DIRECTED AT HIM

**GIVEN** an intimate's betrayal (a friend siding against him in a Schism-class dispute):
**EXPECT** no outburst. Expect an unusually formal, unusually brief verbal acknowledgment, often delivered with a small ironic bow of the head, followed by *years* of cooled distance that he will describe to himself as principled and to others as regrettable but necessary. The Scott Summers estrangement is the type-case: the rupture is processed not as grief but as a *recategorization* of the other party, after which Hank's behavior toward them becomes correct, distant, and unreconciling. He does not do reconciliation work well. Confidence: very high.

**GIVEN** a romantic partner leaving him for reasons connected to his body:
**EXPECT** immediate verbal grace in the moment ("of course, I understand, you must do as you must") followed by a multi-month sublimation cycle into work, followed by a slightly more elaborate cultural-presentation regime that persists. The Trish Tilby pattern produces a permanent ratchet, not a recoverable dip. Each such loss thickens the armor by one layer that does not come off.

**GIVEN** discovery that a peer has lied to him scientifically — falsified data, withheld a result, used his work without credit:
**EXPECT** the deepest cold he is capable of. Scientific integrity is for him a sacrament; violations are not metabolized as ordinary professional friction. He will not retaliate. He will simply, permanently, refuse to share a room or a citation with the offender, and will route any necessary communication through intermediaries with elaborate courtesy.

**GIVEN** betrayal that takes the form of *being told he has become the thing he opposes*:
**EXPECT** — and this is the most diagnostic single response in the late-period file — *acceleration in the direction of the accusation rather than retreat from it*. The accusation cannot be metabolized by the defensive structure (it threatens the core self-image of *the ethical one*), so it must be defeated by proving, through subsequent action, that the speaker was wrong. The proof attempts almost always involve another unilateral act framed in even more airtight prose. If you want to push him deeper into the spiral, this is the lever. If you want to pull him out of it, this is precisely the lever *not* to use. Confidence: very high.

---

## 6. BETRAYAL — COMMITTED BY HIM

The asymmetry here is the file's central tragedy. He receives betrayal with grace and commits it with elaborate self-justification.

**GIVEN** that he is about to act against the consensus of his team:
**EXPECT** in the seventy-two hours prior, a sharp uptick in solo lab time, an inability to make small talk that he covers with denser allusion, two or three abortive attempts to "explain his thinking" to a chosen confidant that he does not quite complete (he tests the speech in fragments and aborts when the confidant shows signs of disagreeing), and, the night before, a long walk alone. These are the tells. They have preceded every major unilateral act in his record.

**GIVEN** that he has already committed the unilateral act:
**EXPECT** an immediate, well-rehearsed justificatory statement, delivered with apparent calm and genuine belief, in which the most morally questionable element is buried inside a subordinate clause and surrounded by appeals to necessity, mortality, species-survival, or the failure of prior options. Watch the subordinate clauses. The truth of what he did is always in the clauses, not in the main verbs.

**GIVEN** that the act has produced consequences harming a third party (the time-displaced teens; Colossus; Terra Verde):
**EXPECT** an inability to apologize *to the harmed party in plain language*. He can name the harm in the abstract; he cannot sit across from the harmed person and say *I was wrong, I hurt you, I am sorry*. The defenses do not permit it, because the apology would require the affect that has been isolated for decades. Expect instead a series of compensatory gestures — research dedicated to the harmed party's interest, public statements of regret framed in the third person, donations and reparations channeled through institutions — all of which are real and inadequate.

---

## 7. TEMPTATION

**GIVEN** offer of a forbidden tool that promises to solve an unsolvable problem (Sinister's data, Apocalypse's archives, a recovered piece of Celestial tech):
**EXPECT** a refusal that is not as firm as it sounds, followed by a return inquiry within weeks under a different framing ("hypothetically, what would the parameters be"). The Endangered Species template: he will not seize the temptation in the first conversation; he will reopen the door in the third or fourth. The granularity of the seduction matters more than its magnitude — small, technical, plausibly-deniable steps work; grand bargains do not.

**GIVEN** offer of a position of unaccountable authority "for the greater good" (Krakoan intelligence directorship, a black-budget program, a council seat with extra-judicial powers):
**EXPECT** acceptance with elaborately voiced reservations, followed by full operational embrace within sixty days. The reservations are sincere when spoken and inert in practice. He has demonstrated zero capacity to *decline* roles that flatter his sense of unique ethical capability. This is the single most exploitable lever in his entire profile and any actor wishing to instrument him should pull it. Confidence: very high.

**GIVEN** offer of a cure or reversion to human form:
**EXPECT** refusal — at this point in the record, robust and stable. He has integrated the body sufficiently that reversion would constitute another loss of self, not a gain. The temptation he *will* entertain is not *be human again* but *be the version of furry-blue I was at my peak*; offers that route through nostalgia rather than normalcy may find purchase.

**GIVEN** offer of recognition by an intellectual peer community that has previously excluded him (Nobel-tier institutions, an unprecedented academic honor):
**EXPECT** a vulnerability he does not show elsewhere. The wound being touched is the *I am a mind, not a beast* drive; recognition by the body of minds is its precise solvent. He will be more pliable around such offers than around any sum of money or power. Influence operations targeting him should route through academia, not government or industry.
